1001 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Anderson v. State


No. 01-84-0451-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8654



October 29, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 248th District Court, Harris County, Texas Trial Court, Cause No. 315053.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On remand, appellant challenged the judgment of the 248th District Court, Harris County, Texas, which convicted appellant of securing execution of a document by deception.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of securing execution of a document by deception. On appeal, the court reversed the judgement for a determination of whether appellant had notice of the acts or omissions of which he was charged. Appellee state sought review by the appellate court, which remanded the case for review in light of new caselaw that held that an appellant who challenged the sufficiency of the charging instrument had to show harm that was apparent in the statement of facts. In affirming the judgment of the trial court, the court concluded that while the complete statement of facts was missing, appellant had adequate notice of its absence, and his failure to object to the completed record for appeal by the clerk of the court demonstrated that he had not been harmed. The court held that appellant had waived his claim of a notice defect of the indictment because he failed to raise the issue in a timely fashion, and that the indictment's charge of the offense was sufficient enough to confer jurisdiction on the court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court convicting appellant of securing execution of a document by deception because the statement of facts in the indictment did not harm appellant.

 

1002 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Stanglin v. Dallas


No. 05-86-01265-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


744 S.W.2d 165; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 9248



October 29, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from a District Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant skating rink owner sought review of the judgment of the District Court of Dallas County (Texas), which denied appellant relief in his action contesting the constitutionality of Dallas, Tex., City Code §§ 14-8.1, 14-5 (d), which applied age-limit restrictions to appellant's dance hall operations, but not his roller skating operations.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, a skating rink owner, brought an action to contest the constitutionality of Dallas, Tex., City Code §§ 14-8.1, 14-5 (d), which placed age and hour restrictions on the operation of dance halls expressly catering to a juvenile clientele. The city ordinance restricted the operation of the dance hall, but not the roller rink appellant also operated on the premises. The lower court denied appellant relief. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment of the lower court and enjoined the enforcement of Dallas, Tex., City Code § 14-8.1, the ordinance that placed an age limit on patrons, but affirmed the part of the judgment that found constitutional the restrictions of § 14-5 (d) on the hours of operation. The court held that § 14-8.1 was unconstitutional because minors had the right to freely associate under U.S. Const. amend. I, and the ordinance was overly broad in its attempt to protect minors from unsuitable influences. Section 14-5 (d), which restricted the hours of operation, was constitutional because the city provided a rational relationship between the ordinance and the legitimate public purpose it served.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's decision denying appellant skating rink owner relief and found unconstitutional the section of a city ordinance that placed age limitations on those frequenting dance halls, because it denied minors their first amendment right to freely associate. The court affirmed the section of the ordinance that restricted appellant's hours of operation because it was rationally related to a legitimate public purpose.

 

1003 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Jingles v. State


No. B14-86-593-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


752 S.W.2d 126; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8578



October 22, 1987, Decided  
October 22, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 155th District Court, Waller County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 5544.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review after a jury in the 155th District Court of Waller County (Texas) convicted him of burglary of a building with intent to commit theft and enhanced his sentence based upon two prior felony convictions.


OVERVIEW: After a jury convicted him of burglary of a building with intent to commit theft, enhanced by two prior felony convictions, appellant sought review. Appellant contended that the state failed to prove all the elements of burglary because the owner of the building died before the trial and that the indictment failed to specifically allege the elements of an enhancement offense. The court affirmed. The court held that Texas law permitted proof by circumstantial evidence to show lack of the owner's consent to a burglary. The court held that appellant waived any objection to a jury charge during the punishment stage of the trial because he failed to object at trial. Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 36.19 (1981). The court held that the state's indictment provided appellant with sufficient notice that he was charged with having been twice convicted of prior felonies. Tex. Penal Code § 12.42(d) (1987). The court held that the state was not required to allege enhancement counts in an indictment with the same degree of specificity that the primary offense required. The court rejected appellant's speedy trial claim because the statute on which he relied had been declared unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for burglary of a building. The court held that the indictment provided appellant with sufficient notice that he was charged with having been twice convicted of prior felonies and that the state proved the elements of burglary of a building.

 

1004 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Head v. State


No. 01-86-0973-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8587



October 22, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] On Appeal from the 232nd District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court CAuse No. 443,755


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the 232nd District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of delivery of hydromorphone despite failing to give the parole charge under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07(4) (1987).


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted appellant of delivery of hydromorphone. The court reversed that conviction on appeal, finding that a failure to give the parole charge under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07(4) (1987) was reversible error. The court also remanded the case. The court determined that art. 37.07(4)'s provision that the court shall charge the jury mandated that its charge be given, and that a reversal was required because appellant objected to the omission in the charge. The court also concluded that it was obvious that the error caused appellant some actual harm, and that the state did not meet its burden of showing beyond a reasonable doubt that the error was not harmful.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's conviction for delivery of hydromorphone, holding that a failure to give a mandatory statutory parole charge was a reversible error, and remanded the case. The court determined that a provision that the court shall charge the jury mandated that the statute's charge be given, and that a reversal was necessary because appellant objected to the charge's omission and the omission caused him actual harm.

 

1005 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Douglas v. State


Nos. 01-86-00452-CR, 01-86-00453-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8506



October 8, 1987, Decided and Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] On Appeal from the 351st District Court Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause Nos. 439,373 & 439,374.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the 351st District Court Harris County, Texas, convicting appellant of possession and delivery of marihuana.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court. Appellant was convicted for possession of and delivery of marihuana, and sentenced to 15 years' confinement; appellant sought review on four points of error. On review, the court held that The Speedy Trial Act, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32A.02 (1987), was held unconstitutional and did not provide relief for appellant. The court held that appellant's point that a memorandum was not prepared by the grand jury prior to the indictment and signed by the foreman was not a ground for vacating the decision. The court also held that pretrial motions were subject to effective review and were properly preserved such that appellant's argument that his guilty plea was not knowingly and intelligently entered was invalid. The court further held that appellant's trial counsel provided effective assistance and any alleged ineffectiveness would not have changed the outcome.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting appellant for possession of and delivery of marihuana was affirmed. The indictment and trial procedures were proper, appellant's guilty plea was knowingly and intelligently entered, and appellant was not denied effective assistance of counsel.

 

1006 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Blackwell v. State


No. 2-86-065-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


738 S.W.2d 78; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8663



October 8, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for review granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE 89TH DISTRICT COURT OF WICHITA COUNTY


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction in the 89th District Court of Wichita County (Texas) for the offense of aggravated robbery pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 29.03(a) (1974).


OVERVIEW: In affirming defendant's conviction for aggravated robbery, the court found that his right to a speedy trial under U.S. Const. amend. VI was not violated because he and his counsel were to blame for any delays in bringing him to trial. The court did not find any showing that any delay prejudiced his defense. The court found that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4, which authorized and directed jury instructions on the law of parole, was constitutional and that jurors were not likely to disregard the trial court's instruction not to consider how the parole law might be applied to him. The court applied a five-prong test for determining whether jury misconduct constituted reversible error and found that defendant failed to meet three of the five prongs. Issues of fact involving jury misconduct were for the trial court to decide and the trial court had the discretion to grant or deny his motion for a new trial on that basis. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion because the evidence of jury misconduct conflicted and defendant failed to meet the five-prong test.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for aggravated robbery because he was not denied a speedy trial, as the delays were his fault and there was no showing that any delays prejudiced his defense. The jury instructions on the law of parole were proper, and the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying his motion for a new trial for jury misconduct because the evidence conflicted.

 

1007 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Burt v. State


No. 01-86-00445-CR .


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8399



October 1, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 248th District Court for Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 429,147.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the 248th District Court for Harris County (Texas), which convicted appellant of attempted murder and assessed punishment at 15 years confinement and a $ 10,000 fine.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of his conviction of attempted murder. He contended that the trial court erred in denying his motion for mistrial because the state improperly characterized him as a "murderer" during final argument. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. It held that although the evidence supported an argument that the appellant attempted to murder the complainant and that he thought he had murdered her, the evidence did not show that the appellant was a murderer. The court held that the prosecutor's statement was improper because one cannot be characterized as a murderer until he had legally committed a murder. The court concluded that the prosecutor's remark was not so inflammatory that its prejudicial effect could not have been removed by the instruction given to the jury to disregard the statement. The court held that no reversible error was shown. The court determined that appellant had waived the constitutional error in a Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 (1987), charge because he did not timely object to the charge in the trial court, and first asserted the objections in his motion for new trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court which convicted appellant of attempted murder. The court held that the statement by the prosecutor where he characterized appellant as a "murderer," was improper, but any prejudicial effect should have been removed by the court's instruction to the jury to disregard the statement. The court found that no reversible error was shown.

 

1008 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Jackson v. State


No. 01-86-00411-CR .


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8417



October 1, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 232nd District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 442,342.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the 232nd District Court of Harris County (Texas), which found defendant guilty of robbery.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for robbery because it found there was sufficient testimony to prove venue by a preponderance of the evidence. The court found the testimony from the complainant and the off-duty police officer about the location of the robbery was sufficient to prove the county in which the incident occurred. The court found that the evidence was sufficient to prove that defendant had committed the robbery. The court found that the complainant had positively identified defendant at the time of the arrest and at trial, and in addition, the court found that defendant admitted that he was present at the scene and had taken complainant's purse. The court concluded that there was sufficient evidence to show that defendant intended to obtain and maintain control of complainant's purse and its contents without her effective consent. The court held that the evidence was also sufficient to show that defendant had intentionally or knowingly caused bodily injury to the complainant by hitting her while committing the theft. The court held that a rational trier of fact could have found that the essential elements of the crime were proven beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's robbery conviction because it found that there was sufficient evidence to show that defendant intended to obtain and maintain control of complainant's purse and that he had caused bodily injury during the theft.

 

1009 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Lawson v. State


No. B14-86-686-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8430



October 1, 1987, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 268th District Court, Fort Bend County, Texas, No. 16,811.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment by the 268th District Court, Fort Bend County (Texas), which convicted appellant for the offense of arson, enhanced by a prior felony conviction.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted for arson, enhanced by one prior felony conviction. Appellant entered a plea of not guilty, but a jury found him guilty and assessed punishment at seven years confinement in the state department of corrections. The court affirmed appellant's conviction. It concluded that the trial court did not err in not granting appellant his oral motion to quash the indictment since such motion had to be in writing as required by Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 27.10 (1966). The court held that the state properly alleged the requisite facts to give appellant notice of the manner and means by which he set the fire or caused the explosion. Appellant failed to object at the first opportunity under Tex. R. App. P. 52(a) to the fact that the state read the second paragraph of the indictment to the jury at the punishment phase of trial when the jury had only found him guilty of the charges alleged in the first paragraph of the indictment, as such he preserved nothing for review and he received the relief requested and the instruction to disregard cured any error. The trial court did not err in failing to instruct the jury to disregard a prior felony conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for arson, enhanced by a prior felony conviction. The court concluded that appellant's oral motion to quash his indictment did not preserve anything for review since such motion must be in writing. The court did not err in failing to instruct the jury to disregard the armed robbery conviction alleged as a prior felony conviction and appellant failed to obtain an adverse ruling thus waived any error.

 

1010 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. State


No. 05-86-00865-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


737 S.W.2d 933; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8544



September 28, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from a Dallas County District Court (Texas), which convicted defendant of possession with intent to deliver cocaine, a controlled substance. Defendant was sentenced to 30 years imprisonment under the Texas Controlled Substance Act, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 4.039(d)(3).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of possessing, with intent to deliver, a powdery substance that weighed a total of 1331.09 grams, of which only 349.51 was pure cocaine. Defendant was sentenced to 30 year's confinement under the Texas Controlled Substance, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 4.039(d)(3), for possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance with an aggregate weight, including any adulterants of dilutants, of 400 grams or more. Upon appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that Tex. Penal Code § 4.03(d)(3) was not unconstitutionally vague where a person of ordinary intelligence could reasonably ascertain the plain meaning of the words "adulterant" or "dilutants." The court also found that the statute did not violate constitutional due process and equal protection requirements where the legislature had a rational basis for concluding that possession of greater amounts of controlled substances should be punished more severely. The court held statements made by defendant after he was arrested were admissible res gestae statements where eight police officers had burst into a hotel room defendant was in and defendant made the statements within minutes after the police arrived.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of possession with intent to deliver cocaine, a controlled substance. The court held that the controlled substance statute defendant was sentenced under was not unconstitutionally vague where a person of ordinary intelligence could reasonably ascertain the meaning of the words "adulterants" or "dilutants."

 

1011 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Watt v. State


No. A14-86-868-CR .


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8369



September 24, 1987, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 122nd District Court of Galveston County, Cause No. 85-CR-650.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the 122nd District Court of Galveston County (Texas), which convicted him of aggravated sexual assault after a jury trial. The jury made a affirmative finding that appellant used a deadly weapon and assessed punishment at 10 years' confinement. Appellant presented nine points of error, including a challenge to the constitutionality of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 (1986).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault using a deadly weapon. On appeal, he challenged the constitutionality of jury instructions. At the punishment phase, the trial court gave the jury an instruction that tracked verbatim Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 (1986), which merely advised the jury regarding certain parole statutes. The court rejected appellant's arguments that article 37.07, § 4 violated the separation of powers doctrine, that the statute unconstitutionally invited jurors to speculate on matters outside of punishment, that the statute was unconstitutionally vague and confusing, that the jury charge denied him due process of law, and that the statute was vague and ambiguous in application because of drafting errors. The court held that the instruction simply clarified the law as to the effect of parole and good time credits on the sentence, matters about which jurors tend to speculate. However, the court agreed that the judgment was mistaken in stating that the court found that appellant had used a deadly weapon, when in fact the jury made the finding. The court reformed the judgment accordingly.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of aggravated sexual assault, but reformed it to reflect that the jury, rather than the judge, made the finding that appellant used a deadly weapon. The court concluded that the statute in question and the related jury charge were not unduly vague, and did not invite juror speculation as a matter of law. The court held that the challenged statute and associated jury charge were not unconstitutional.

 

1012 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Lovall v. State


No. A14-86-00628-CR .


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8373



September 24, 1987, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 228th District Court Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 440,402.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the 228th District Court Harris County (Texas), which convicted defendant of assault on a peace officer under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.02(a)(2)(A)(1983) and assessed punishment at three years probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged her conviction of assault on a peace officer based on insufficient evidence, and the validity of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.02(a)(2)(A)(1983), which defined assault on a peace officer. The court affirmed defendant's conviction for assault on a peace officer. It was no longer necessary for the state to prove that defendant knew the officer was lawfully discharging an official duty. Thus, the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction. Further, the court held that § 22.02(a)(2)(A) was not unconstitutional because it did not require a mental intent to assault a peace officer since § 22.02(a)(2)(A) did not require that the accused have knowledge that the officer was acting in the lawful discharge of an official duty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant because the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction and the statute was valid since it was not necessary for the state to demonstrate that defendant had knowledge that the officer was lawfully discharging an official duty.

 

1013 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Jackson v. State


No. 01-85-00873-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8374



September 24, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion on Motion For Rehearing Overruled September 29, 1988


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 228th District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 429,980.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction from the 228th District Court of Harris County (Texas) for robbery, alleging that the lower court erred in denying a motion for continuance, in permitting state's jury arguments, and in admitting a line-up photograph in which appellant appears in jail clothes.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of robbery and sought review on the grounds that the lower court improperly denied his motion for a continuance to obtain tape recordings of statements made by complainant, allowed state to make impermissible jury arguments on appellant's failure to testify, and admitted a line-up photo of appellant in which he appears in jail attire. The court held that denial of appellant's request for continuance was proper because appellant's request was based solely to obtain merely impeachment or cumulative evidence and the complainant had already admitted to testifying differently at appellant's parole hearing. The court also held that state's use of "I" in jury arguments was not a comment on the failure of appellant to testify, but a discussion of defensive theories in the case, and a fair summation of the evidence offered at trial, and the effect on the jury, if any, was cured by prompt and clear instruction. Finally, the court held that the line-up photo was excised to eliminate any visible words or numbers printed on any of the pictures, showing the appellant from his chest up, and made it virtually impossible to identify appellant therein as a prisoner.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for robbery was affirmed on the grounds that appellant's motion for continuance was sought solely to obtain impeachment evidence on an issue already admitted, that state's jury argument was summation of evidence and any error was cured by prompt instruction to disregard, and that proper steps were taken to eliminate effects of appellant's admitted line-up photo.

 

1014 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Villalon v. State


No. 13-86-508-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


739 S.W.2d 450; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8379



September 24, 1987, Decided  
September 24, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the 139th District Court of Hidalgo County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the 139th District Court of Hidalgo County (Texas), which convicted him for aggravated sexual assault pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.011 and Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.021(a)(5).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.011 and Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.021(a)(5). During trial, a school nurse had testified that the victim had hurt her, but when the child testified, she never used language which would establish penetration of the vagina. On appeal, defendant claimed that the evidence was insufficient to prove penetration and, under the amended indictment, it was essential for the prosecution to prove that defendant knowingly and intentionally caused his penis to penetrate the child's vagina. The court reversed the conviction and remanded for an entry of acquittal because the hearsay testimony of the nurse was contradicted by the victim, and was not corroborated by any other evidence. The court held it would be irrational to hold that the unsworn hearsay evidence had the same, or more, probative value than the sworn testimony of the party who made the hearsay statement and had actual knowledge of the facts.


OUTCOME: Defendant was entitled to acquittal because the hearsay testimony was contradicted by the child victim and was not corroborated by any other evidence. The court held it would be irrational to hold that the nurse's unsworn hearsay evidence had the same or more probative value than the sworn testimony of the child victim who had made the statement and had actual knowledge.

 

1015 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Vasquez Orona v. State


No. 2-86-156-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


737 S.W.2d 432; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8519



September 24, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Addendum to Opinion November 10, 1987


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT NO. 2 OF TARRANT COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of Criminal District Court No. 2 of Tarrant County (Texas) that convicted appellant of murder following a jury trial and sentenced appellant to 99 years confinement.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of the murder of his wife. Witnesses testified that they heard the victim outside of her house yell "no" and appellant's name and then heard two shots. There was also testimony that appellant had previously threatened the victim. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction. The court held that there was sufficient circumstantial evidence to sustain the conviction even though no one actually saw the crime. During closing argument, the prosecution stated that the defense lawyers knew how to argue to get people off. The court held that the prosecution's closing argument was improper but that it did not constitute reversible error because it did not infect the trial with unfairness as to make the resulting conviction a denial of due process. The court held that the trial court did not err in charging the jury pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(a) because the instruction authorized by the statute was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that convicted appellant of murder because there was sufficient circumstantial evidence to sustain the conviction, the prosecution's improper closing argument did not constitute reversible error, and the trial court did not err in instructing the jury.

 

1016 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Browning-Ferris, Inc. v. Brazoria County


No. 3-86-132-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


742 S.W.2d 43; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 9145



September 23, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 200TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT NO. 357,114, HONORABLE JOSEPH H. HART, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a waste management company and the Texas Water Commission, challenged the order of the 200th District Court of Travis County (Texas) that dismissed the petition for judicial review filed by appellees, a citizens action committee and Brazoria County, pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4477-7 § 9. Appellants claimed that the order entered by the Commission was a final decision.


OVERVIEW: Appellant waste management company obtained a permit to build and operate a hazardous-waste disposal well from appellant, the Texas Water Commission. Appellees, a citizens action committee and Brazoria County, filed for judicial review under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4477-7 § 9. The trial court ruled that the order in dispute was not a full and final order, and that the findings of fact were inadequate to support the order. The court held that the statute authorizing judicial review had to be interpreted in light of the judicial doctrines of finality and ripeness. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and held that appellant commission's order was not a final order for purposes of judicial review because the order allowed appellant waste management company the option to give some type or kind of financial assurance in the future rather than a bond in designated sums as required by statute. The court determined that it was insufficient for the agency merely to fix the amount of financial assurance to be supplied by the permittee in the future, because the statute required that a bond be executed or alternate form of assurance be given before any permit was issued.


OUTCOME: The court found that the governing statute required the execution of a bond before a permit was issued to appellant waste management company by appellant Texas Water Commission. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court issued in favor of appellees, a citizens action committee and Brazoria County, in part. The court vacated the remand portion of the order because the matter was not final and therefore still before appellant commission.

 

1017 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Fisher v. Kerr County


No. 04-86-00544-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


739 S.W.2d 434; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8780



September 23, 1987, Decided  
September 23, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 216th District Court of Kerr County, Trial Court No. 83-263-A, Honorable Robert R. Barton, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner sought review of a judgment of the 216th District Court of Kerr County (Texas), entered in favor of appellee county in an action to recover delinquent ad valorem taxes.


OVERVIEW: Appellee county filed a lawsuit to collect delinquent ad valorem taxes owed by appellant landowner. The trial court entered judgment in favor of appellee. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the notice requirements of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 7174A, § 4 did not conflict with Tex. Const. Art. VIII, § 1-d-1. Article 7174A, § 4 required a person seeking agriculture use designation and assessment of land based on it productive capacity to file an application with the tax assessor. Appellant's failure to file an application made his land ineligible for such assessment. Article 7174A, § 4 required the tax assessor to mail an application form to each person that owned land that qualified under article 7174A in the preceding year. The court held appellee did not fail to comply with the notice requirements because appellant failed to file a proper application the preceding year. The court held that there was no evidence that appellee was aware that appellant's property qualified. The court held that appellee provided proper notice of the reappraisal of appellant's land pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art 7255c when it deposited the notice in the mail.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court entered in favor of appellee county because appellant landowner failed to file an application seeking agriculture use designation for his land, appellee complied with all statutory notice requirements, the statutory notice requirements were constitutional, and the notice of reappraisal was deemed delivered to appellant when it was mailed by appellee.

 

1018 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. State


No. 09-86-119 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Ninth District, Beaumont


737 S.W.2d 923; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8615



September 17, 1987, Decided  
September 17, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Original Dissent Opinion corrected October 15, 1987, Decided and Filed.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALED FROM THE 75TH DISTRICT COURT OF LIBERTY COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the 75th District Court of Liberty County (Texas), which entered a judgment convicting him in a juried proceeding of the delivery of cocaine in the aggregate amount exceeding 400 grams, and fixing a punishment of 20 years confinement and a $ 20,000 fine. Appellant claimed the defenses of entrapment and mistake of fact.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of the trial court's judgment convicting him of delivery of cocaine in the aggregate of 400 grams despite his claimed defenses of mistake of fact and entrapment, contending that there was insufficient evidence to prove he delivered over 400 grams of cocaine by constructively transferring the same, and that the trial court erred in allowing an undercover informant to testify over appellant's objections to hearsay statements he allegedly made. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, holding that the evidence was sufficient to prove appellant constructively transferred cocaine to a special Drug Enforcement Agent pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 1.02(6) (1987), by leaving it in an airplane so that the agent could take physical possession of the drugs. The court further held that the hearsay testimony concerning who made the initial move or the first telephone call for purposes of appellant's entrapment defense had already been elicited by appellant during his cross-examination of the agent, and therefore he waived his hearsay objection to this evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting appellant of delivery of cocaine in the aggregate of 400 grams because the evidence sufficiently proved he constructively transferred the required amount of drugs, and appellant elicited from the drug enforcement agent the same hearsay testimony that he challenged on appeal, and therefore any hearsay objection to the agent's testimony was waived.

 

1019 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. State


No. 09-86-050 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Ninth District, Beaumont


737 S.W.2d 901; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8624



September 16, 1987, Decided  
September 16, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEALED FROM THE 284TH DISTRICT COURT OF MONTGOMERY COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the 284th District Court, Montgomery County (Texas), which entered his jury conviction on two counts of attempted capital murder, with findings of true on three sentencing enhancements. Defendant was sentenced to 99 years' imprisonment on each count, to run consecutively. Defendant alleged that the trial court erred in permitting the jury to enter dual sentences on convictions arising out of one incident.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by a jury on two counts of attempted capital murder, in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03, for the shooting of two robbery victims. Defendant was sentenced to 99 years' imprisonment on each count. Defendant appealed his convictions and sentences, alleging, inter alia, that the trial court committed error in entering sentences on both convictions that stemmed from one incident. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment in all respects, finding that defendant's failure to object to the sentencing at trial constituted a waiver of any error because an error was not permitted to be raised for the first time on appeal. The court also found that the two offenses did not arise out of the same transaction, because there were two different people shot and two different robberies.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentence, finding no merit to his contentions of error, including the assertion that the court erred in sentencing him on two offenses that arose out of one incident and one indictment. The court found that not only were there two victims of attempted murder, but also that defendant waived this assignment of error by failing to raise it at any time prior to appeal.

 

1020 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Pavek v. State


No. 07-86-0313-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Seventh District, Amarillo


737 S.W.2d 136; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8304



September 14, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE COUNTY COURT AT LAW OF POTTER COUNTY; NO. 48,314; HONORABLE DAVID L. GLEASON, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant lay midwife appealed from a judgment by the County Court at Law of Potter County (Texas), which denied her pretrial application for a writ of habeas corpus. Appellant contended that the charge for committing an act prohibited by Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4512i, § 17(3) (1987), violated due process guarantees under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and Tex. Const. art. I, § 19, because the statute was void for vagueness.


OVERVIEW: Appellant lay midwife was charged with committing an act prohibited by Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4512i, § 17(3) (1987), the removal of placenta by invasive techniques. She filed a pretrial application to be released from the charge on the ground that the statute was void for vagueness in violation of U.S. Const. amend. XIV; Tex. Const. art. I, § 19. Appellant argued that because the legislature did not define the terms "remove" and "invasive techniques," these terms failed to give fair notice of the conduct forbidden. Her application was denied. The court affirmed, holding that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague. The court found that the language was sufficiently clear to put persons of ordinary intelligence, particularly lay midwives who possess special knowledge and training, on notice of the acts prohibited. The court held that the language simply stated that a lay midwife should not move the placenta from its position or take it from the body by any procedure which involved an entry into the body.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, which denied an application for writ of habeas corpus by appellant lay midwife, seeking dismissal of charges under a statute regulating lay midwives. The court held that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague because it was sufficiently clear to put persons of ordinary intelligence, particularly lay midwives who possess special knowledge and training, on notice of the acts prohibited.

 

1021 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Greenville v. Emerson


No. 05-86-00823-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


740 S.W.2d 10; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8929



September 11, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from a District Court of Hunt County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged an order of the District Court of Hunt County (Texas), which rendered judgment for appellee retirees in a breach of contract action concerning the calculation of retirement benefits.


OVERVIEW: Appellee retirees filed a breach of contract action against appellant city that requested the city compute benefits according to the per hour pay rate at a 56 hour instead of a 60 hour work week. The lower court held that appellant breached its contract in using the 60 hour computation formula. Appellant challenged this ruling, contending that the judgment effectively required appellant to pay more than what was due under the contract without receipt of additional consideration and was a second contract that contravened Tex. Const. art. III, § 53. The court reversed the lower court's order, concluding that the there was no express or implied contract created by the memos and documents referring to retirement benefits that were presented into evidence. Moreover, the judgment required that appellant pay benefits above what appellees were paid under a valid contract without receipt of additional consideration, which violated the constitutional limits on appellant's authority to contract because there was no approval by the city council of such a contract.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment, which rendered judgment for appellee retirees in a breach of contract action concerning the calculation of retirement benefits, and held that the agreement between appellant city and appellees provided additional benefits without consideration and, therefore, was unenforceable as an unconstitutional exercise of power by appellant.

 

1022 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Hightower v. State


Nos. 11-86-193-CR, 11-86-194-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eleventh District, Eastland


736 S.W.2d 949; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8252



September 10, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeals from Taylor County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the order of the Taylor County Court (Texas), which convicted him of the offenses of aggravated kidnapping and indecency with a child in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 20.04 (1974) and 21.11 (Supp. 1987), and found that the two enhancement allegations were true under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 12.42(d) (Supp. 1987).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with aggravated kidnapping and indecency with a child in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 20.04 (1974) and 21.11 (Supp. 1987). The lower court convicted appellant on both charges and found that two enhancement allegations were true under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 12.42(d) (Supp. 1987). Appellant challenged his convictions, contending that his rights to effective assistance of counsel and confrontation under U.S. Const. amend VI were violated by the trial court's use of videotaped testimony, and that the trial court erroneously admitted illegally seized evidence and improper testimony by the child victim and her mother. The court affirmed the lower court's judgment, holding that appellant's constitutional rights were not violated because counsel for appellant was permitted to question the child during the taping of her testimony. The lower court properly admitted evidence taken from appellant's home and pick-up truck, which were reasonably included in the search warrant, and admission of the child's testimony and the mother's testimony concerning the child's hearsay statements was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions for aggravated kidnapping and indecency with a child and held that appellant's right to confront witnesses and to be effectively assisted by counsel were not violated by the use of videotaped testimony of a child witness. The trial court did not commit error in admitting lawfully seized evidence and the testimony of the child and her mother.

 

1023 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Lindley v. State


No. 2-86-117-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


736 S.W.2d 267; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8435



September 9, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal FROM THE 271ST DISTRICT COURT OF WISE COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the 271st District Court of Wise County (Texas), which convicted appellant of the attempted manufacture of methamphetamine, pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.03(d)(3) (Supp. 1987), imposed a punishment of 75 years, and levied a fine of $ 75,000.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of the attempted manufacture of methamphetamine pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.03(d)(3) (Supp. 1987). Appellant challenged his conviction in ten points of error. The court affirmed the lower court's judgment that convicted appellant because the charging instrument gave sufficient notice of which method of manufacture was attempted under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.03(a) (Supp. 1987). The court reasoned that the terms "manufacture" and "synthesis" referred to manufacture by production and that the charging instrument sufficiently alleged production. The court held that there was sufficient evidence to link appellant to the manufacturing process and hold him criminally responsible because appellant signed the lease for the site of the methamphetamine manufacturing, applied for electrical services, and occupied the premises. The court sustained appellant's point of error that challenged the lower court's refusal to hear an amended motion to quash once the trial had begun, but determined the error did not result in harm to appellant. The court overruled appellant's remaining points of error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of the attempted manufacture of methamphetamine because the charging information provided him with sufficient notice that "manufacture" referred to manufacture by production, there was sufficient evidence to link appellant to the crime, and the lower court's refusal to hear an amended motion to quash did not harm appellant. The court overruled appellant's remaining points of error.

 

1024 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Alford v. Dallas


No. 05-86-00749-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


738 S.W.2d 312; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8641



August 20, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff police officer appealed from the order of the District Court of Dallas County (Texas), dismissing, for want of jurisdiction, an action alleging that defendant city employer's failure to follow regulations regarding the transfer of officers, deprived him of property and liberty interests, and violating his rights to due process, equal protection, and nonimpairment of contract under U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, and U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff police officer applied for a transfer, but when vacancies arose in the desired section, his request was denied due to an alleged hearing disability. In filling one of the vacancies, defendant city employer failed to follow established transfer regulations. Plaintiff then sued for declaratory and injunctive relief, claiming that defendant's decision denied him due process and equal protection under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and impaired his employment contract, in violation of U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, and Tex. Const. art. I, § 16. The complaint was dismissed for lack of jurisdiction and plaintiff appealed. In affirming, the court agreed that the pleadings failed to state a cause of action within the jurisdiction of the trial court. The transfer regulations did not vest in plaintiff any due process property right to a transfer and his expectancy of a transfer did not rise to the level of a protected vested property interest. Even if his reputation was damaged by the denial of a transfer, his reputation was not a protected liberty interest. Defendant had not created any discriminatory classifications and the employment contract was not impaired by the regulations.


OUTCOME: The dismissal order was affirmed because plaintiff failed to establish the jurisdiction of the trial court; he had no vested property interest under the regulations in obtaining a transfer, the expectancy of a transfer did not create a property interest, his reputation was not a protected liberty interest, the regulations did not create any discriminatory classifications, and the regulations themselves did not impair his employment contract.

Cantu Trucking & Materials Co. v. State


No. 3-87-014-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


735 S.W.2d 642; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8303



August 12, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled September 9, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 299TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, NO. 392,103, HONORABLE PETE LOWRY, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant trucking company sought review of a decision by the 299th District Court, Travis County (Texas), in a suit brought by appellee state, which permanently enjoined appellant from transporting goods or commodities by motor vehicle over state highways without a license.


OVERVIEW: Appellant trucking company sought review of a judgment, in a suit brought by appellee state, that permanently enjoined appellant from transporting goods or commodities by motor vehicle over state highways for compensation or hire, between incorporated cities, unless appellant first obtained a license from the Texas Railroad Commission pursuant to the provisions of the Texas Motor Carrier Act (Act), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 911b (1964 & Supp. 1987). On review, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment and held that appellant was required to establish two particular elements that were determinative of its contentions on appeal. First, appellant had to establish that the entirety of its carriage of materials was merely incidental to a business other than the transportation business. Second, with particular reference to appellant's carriage of materials purchased by it from other suppliers, with their contemporaneous re-sale to others, appellant was obliged to establish that its acquisition of title was in good faith. The court concluded that appellant failed to carry its burden.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, holding that appellant trucking company failed to demonstrate that it was not required to comply with the licensing provisions of the Texas Motor Carrier Act.

Southwestern Bell Tel. Co. v. Public Utility Com.


No. 3-86-108-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


735 S.W.2d 663; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8306



August 12, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 345TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, NO. 375,179, HONORABLE JOSEPH H. HART, JUDGE PRESIDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant telephone company sought review of a judgment rendered by the District Court of Travis County (Texas) that dismissed its action seeking to have appellee Public Utility Commission enforce provisions of the Public Utilities Regulatory Act pertaining to local exchange service.


OVERVIEW: Appellant telephone company learned that individuals and businesses had begun to install and utilize "switching systems" within the geographical area assigned to appellant in its certificate of convenience and necessity. Appellee Public Utility Commission regulated "public utilities" through the Public Utility Regulatory Act (PURA), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1446c. Appellant petitioned appellee to amend its rule defining "local exchange service" to make it plain that the "switching systems" amounted to a "local exchange service." Appellee determined that it would not amend its rules as appellant requested. Appellant filed suit in district court alleging that the unregulated activities injured its revenues, investments, and rights conferred by its certificates. The trial court dismissed the action for lack of subject matter jurisdiction. Appellant sought review challenging the jurisdictional issue on various alternative grounds. Appellant contended that the court had jurisdiction under the Uniform Declaratory Judgments Act (UDJA). The court affirmed the dismissal. The UDJA did not itself confer jurisdiction upon the district court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that dismissed appellant telephone company's action seeking to have appellee Public Utility Commission enforce provisions of the Public Utilities Regulatory Act pertaining to local exchange service. The court lacked subject matter jurisdiction.

Brannon v. Randmaa


No. 3-86-079-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


736 S.W.2d 175; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8407



August 12, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing overruled September 30, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF WILLIAMSON COUNTY, 26TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, NO. 84-439-C, HONORABLE WILLIAM S. LOTT, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former husband sought review of the judgment of the 26th Judicial District Court of Williamson County (Texas), which partitioned appellant's military retirement benefits with appellee former wife following their divorce.


OVERVIEW: Appellant former husband sought to set aside the judgment of the district court, which partitioned appellant's military retirement benefits with appellee former wife. The district court held that because the divorce judgment did not dispose of the retirement benefits, the court was empowered to partition those benefits. Appellant maintained that the divorce judgment had the effect of dividing all of the property and was therefore res judicata as to any subsequent partition suit. Appellant claimed that the Uniformed Services Former Spouses Protection Act (USFSPA) violated the separation of powers doctrine and was an unconstitutional impairment of his vested rights. The court affirmed, holding that appellant never acquired a vested, permanent right to his retirement benefits before congress enacted the USFSPA. By passage of the USFSPA, Congress did not retroactively alter appellant's established rights; instead, it lawfully exercised its plenary power to modify the privileges and duties conferred by the benefit scheme. As such, the separation of powers doctrine was not violated, nor was the USFSPA retroactively applied in violation of the Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision to partition appellant's, former husband, military retirement benefits with appellee, former wife, after a divorce judgment because the Uniformed Services Former Spouses Protection Act did not retroactively alter appellant's established rights in his benefits.

Hering v. Norbanco Austin I, Ltd.


No. 3-87-022-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


735 S.W.2d 638; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8308



August 12, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled September 9, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 200TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, NO. 405,779, HONORABLE PAUL R. DAVIS, JR., JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant debtor sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Travis County, 200th Judicial District (Texas), which overruled appellant's motion for a new trial after appellee creditor failed to serve notice in a postjudgment garnishment action as provided in Tex. R. Civ. P. Ann. 663a (Supp. 1987).


OVERVIEW: Appellee creditor failed to comply with the notice requirements of Tex. R. Civ. P. Ann. 663a (Supp. 1987) in a postjudgment garnishment action and never formally served appellant debtor with a copy of the writ of garnishment. Appellant learned of the garnishment action when he attempted to draw on funds subject to the garnishment. The district court overruled appellant's motion for new trial, which alleged a failure to receive notice as provided in rule 663a. Appellee asserted that because appellant received actual notice of the garnishment, the notice requirements of rule 663a were met. The court reversed and remanded the case for a new trial, holding that rule 663a was unambiguous and that the debtor must be served. Appellee's failure to serve appellant was therefore fatal to its judgment in the garnishment action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision to overrule appellant debtor's motion for a new trial in a postjudgment garnishment action because, even though appellant eventually learned of the action, appellee creditor was nevertheless required to formally serve appellant with a copy of the writ of garnishment.

Dominguez v. State


No. 01-86-00792-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7984



August 6, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 262nd District Court Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 449,150.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order from the 262nd District Court Harris County (Texas) convicting him of delivery of a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of his conviction for delivery of a controlled substance. Appellant argued (1) that the punishment assessed, 50 years of confinement and a $ 250,000 fine, was cruel and unusual; (2) that he was denied effective assistance of counsel; and (3) that the trial court erred in denying appellant's motion for mistrial after the prosecutor injected harmful, unsworn testimony before the jury. The court found that where, as here, the punishment assessed was within the range of punishment prescribed by statute, the punishment was not unconstitutionally cruel and unusual. The court also found that appellant had failed to demonstrate that his counsel's performance was deficient and that the outcome would have been different had counsel's representation not been deficient. Finally, the court found that the trial court did not err in denying appellant's motion for mistrial finding that, considering the evidence adduced at trial, the argument was not so prejudicial as to be incurable by an instruction, had one been requested and that, error, if any, was waived.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and verdict finding no error.

James v. State


No. 01-86-0485-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7998



August 6, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 182nd District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 417,786.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from the 182nd District Court of Harris County (Texas), which convicted appellant of aggravated robbery and sentenced him to life based on enhancement allegations of other robberies committed at similar times and in a similar manner.


OVERVIEW: A jury found appellant guilty of aggravated robbery and, based on enhancement allegations, sentenced appellant to life. Appellant claimed that the trial court erred in admitting evidence of extraneous offenses allegedly committed by him. The court affirmed, holding that the extraneous offenses had enough similar characteristics, both as to the time and manner of their commission, so that their probative value outweighed their potential to inflame and prejudice the jury. Appellant also asserted that the trial court erred in submitting an instruction to the jury regarding his failure to testify. At trial, however, appellant objected to the language of the instruction and not to the propriety of its submission. His point of error thus did not comport with his trial objection and preserved nothing for review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's life sentence for aggravated robbery because evidence of extraneous offenses, introduced as enhancement allegations, allegedly committed by appellant were similar enough in character so that their probative value outweighed their potential to prejudice the jury.

Ex parte Parsons

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7999

NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 23rd District Court of Brazoria County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 17,736


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order from the 23rd District Court of Brazoria County (Texas) denying appellant's pretrial motion for habeas corpus relief.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was arrested and charged with attempted sexual assault and aggravated assault. Appellant later moved to dismiss other charges pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 32A.02 (Supp. 1986) (the "Speedy Trial Act"). The trial court granted appellant's motion to dismiss. Appellant then filed a writ of habeas corpus alleging that the dismissal of the charges based on the state's violation of the Speedy Trial Act was a bar to further prosecution under the instant indictment. The trial court denied habeas corpus relief. Appellant sought review of that order arguing that the trial court erred in denying his application for writ of habeas corpus because Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 32A.02 (1986). The court noted that recently the Court of Criminal Appeals held the Speedy Trial Act unconstitutional and its enacting statutes void. The court concluded that because appellant's point of error was based on a void statute it must be overruled.

1033 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Woods v. State


No. C14-86-642-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8001



August 6, 1987, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 25th District Court of Colorado County, Texas Trial Court No. 56-86.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision from the 25th District Court of Colorado County (Texas), which convicted him of murder.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of murder. On appeal, he argued his oral confession should have been suppressed. The court ruled that appellant's statement, given at the time he was placed under arrest was voluntarily given. There was no evidence of coercion and it was not in response to a police inquiry. Although his I.Q. was within the dull/normal range, he had sufficient capacity to understand the Miranda warnings. Thus, both the oral confession and the written confession, made after he had been given the warnings, were admissible. Appellant argued he had ineffective assistance of counsel. The court found the omissions alleged by appellant were not of such nature as would affect the evidence of guilt. Because the evidence of guilt was overwhelming, appellant failed to show that he was prejudiced by the alleged deficient performance, as required for a reversal. The copious evidence of guilt and the circumstances of the offense negated any reasonable possibility that inadmissible evidence contributed to either the conviction or punishment. The court found no error in the jury instruction on the parole law, and it affirmed the decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision which convicted appellant of murder because his confessions were given voluntarily and were properly admitted and the over whelming evidence negated reasonable possibility that any errors by his counsel or in the admission of evidence prejudiced him.

 

1034 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Wilson v. Stephen


No. C14-86-00921-CV.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7963



July 30, 1987, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 212th Judicial District Court of Galveston County, Texas, Trial Cause No. 85-CV-1376-A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, decedent's wife, challenged a judgment of the 212th Judicial District Court of Galveston County (Texas) granting appellee physician's motion for summary judgment, which was based on a limitations defense pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. 4590i (Supp. 1987).


OVERVIEW: Decedent was injured and was referred to appellee physician, who recommended surgery in spite of decedent's history of cardiac problems. After the surgery, decedent had difficulties. Appellant, decedent's wife, questioned appellee regularly about decedent's condition and was reassured that decedent was in no danger. On January 2, 1979, a cardiologist examined decedent. He was in his eighth day of congestive heart failure and suffered two cardiac arrests. Subsequently, decedent's health remained poor, and he died of a cardiac arrest in 1983. In September 1985, appellant filed a claim against appellee. Appellee sought summary judgment based on a limitations defense pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. 4590i (Supp. 1987). The trial court granted the motion, and appellant challenged the judgment. The court affirmed, finding that appellant's proof was insufficient to raise a fact issue as to fraudulent concealment. The court held that the estoppel effect of fraudulent concealment on the limitation period ended when appellant learned of facts that would have caused a reasonable person to make an inquiry, which, if pursued, would have led to discovery of a cause of action.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed because the proof was insufficient to raise a fact issue as to fraudulent concealment, and fraudulent concealment tolled the statute of limitations only until appellant, decedent's wife, learned of the right of action or should have learned thereof through the exercise of reasonable diligence.

 

1035 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Taylor v. State


No. 05-86-00541-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


735 S.W.2d 930; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8338



July 30, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from a District Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from a District Court of Dallas County (Texas), in which she was convicted of arson and sentenced to 15 years in prison. Appellant asserted that insufficient evidence existed to connect her to the fire, that appellee state improperly relied upon an inference based on an inference to prove arson, and that appellee failed to prove that the manner and means of starting the fire were unknown to the grand jury.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court held that in the instant circumstantial evidence case, sufficient evidence showed that appellant committed an offense under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 28.02(a)(6) (Supp. 1987). The court noted that the only reasonable hypothesis to be drawn from the evidence, albeit circumstantial, was that appellant intentionally and unconcernedly started the fire which consumed her home and which took four lives. The court further noted that the existence of evidence showing that the fire was of incendiary nature, in addition to evidence of motive and opportunity, permitted the jury to find the essential elements of arson. The court then rejected the assertion that appellee state's case improperly relied upon an inference based upon an inference, noting that testimony, and not inference, established that at the time of the fire inflammable agents were used in the habitation and in that portion of it where the fire originated. The court affirmed, concluding that appellee successfully proved that the grand jury, after efforts to do so, was unable to find out the exact starting cause of the fire and that no fundamental error was shown in the remaining points of error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentence, holding that sufficient evidence existed for a rational trier of have to conclude that appellant intentionally set fire to her home with the intent to damage or to destroy the property. Appellee state did not impermissibly ground its case on an inference based on an inference where it was testimony, and not an inference, that showed the use of inflammable agents in the home at the time of the fire.

 

1036 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Fish v. State


No. 05-86-01024-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


734 S.W.2d 741; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8170



July 24, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF HUNT COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction for jumping bail, Tex. Penal Code § 38.11 (1974), in a district court of Hunt County (Texas) after a trial before the court. Appellant argued that the evidence was not sufficient to sustain the conviction when the state filed to establish prima facie proof that appellant was notified of the court in which he was to appear.


OVERVIEW: After he was arrested, appellant was released on a bond that required him to appear instanter in a court in Hunt county, without specifying which court. Appellant did not appear for his arraignment, and was served with a copy of the indictment for the original offense 10 months after his arrest. At the trial for jumping bond, Tex. Penal Code § 38.11 (1974), the state presented no evidence other than the bond to show appellant had notice that he was to appear before the 354th Judicial District Court of Hunt County. Reversing his conviction, the court noted that Tex. Penal Code § 38.11(c) provided that appellant had a defense if he had a reasonable excuse for his failure to appear. The court explained that although the language in an instanter bond might have been sufficient to prove a prima facie case that an appellant had notice of the date and time of a hearing, it was not sufficient to prove a prima facie case that he had notice of the place of hearing, because no court was named.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's conviction for jumping bond after a trial to the court, and rendered a judgment of acquittal. The court explained that the state failed to make a prima facie case that appellant knew the place for the hearing, because the instanter bond on which he was released did not specify which court would have held the hearing, and there was no other evidence of notice.

1038 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Houston v. State


No. B14-86-197-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


735 S.W.2d 903; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7892



July 23, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 155th District Court of Austin County, Cause No. 686R.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the 155th District Court of Austin County (Texas), which convicted him of delivery of a controlled substance and sentenced him to 25 years' confinement.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted appellant of delivery of a controlled substance. Appellant was sentenced to 25 years' confinement. Appellant challenged his conviction and sentence. Appellant maintained that the trial court committed reversible error in allowing the introduction of testimony regarding an extraneous offense, and that the trial court erred in giving a jury instruction pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded the case for a new trial. Appellant raised the defense of entrapment at a pretrial motion, during voir dire, and with his own testimony. Appellant's predisposition to commit the offense for which he was tried was not relevant under the objective test of entrapment. Thus, the informant's testimony that appellant had sold cocaine to an undercover police officer three days prior to the alleged offense was improperly admitted, prejudiced appellant, and constituted reversible error. The trial court, however, did not err by giving the parole eligibility charge to the jury pursuant to art. 37.07, § 4. The statute did not invite the jury to consider how parole laws would affect appellant, and was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment convicting appellant of delivery of a controlled substance and sentencing him to 25 years' confinement. The cause was remanded for a new trial because the trial court erred by allowing the introduction of testimony regarding an extraneous offense for the purpose of rebutting appellant's entrapment defense.

Edwards v. State


No. 01-86-00638-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7895



July 23, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 232nd District Court Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 417,228.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the 232nd District Court, Harris County, Texas, which convicted her of murder and assessed punishment at 40 years confinement.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of the murder of her husband. On the night of the shooting, appellant was packing her belongings to move out of the house and end her marriage when her husband arrived home. There was an argument and appellant's husband beat her repeatedly and appellant shot him. The court affirmed the conviction and held that the prosecution's remarks during jury argument in the punishment phase of trial concerning appellant's pregnancy and her plea for probation were responsive pleas for law enforcement, did not inject new facts in the case, did not affect appellant's sentence, and were not so extreme or manifestly improper to constitute reversible error. The court held prosecution's remarks during voir dire that vouched for the credibility of portions of appellant's confession were not erroneous because the intervening trial and the court's admonitions and instructions in its jury charge rendered any error harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. The court held it would not address appellant's alleged error in the giving of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07 § 4 (1987) as an instruction in the charge because appellant failed to object when the court gave the instruction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of murder because prosecution's remarks during sentencing about appellant's pregnancy and her plea for probation were responsive to appellant's pleas, did not add new facts to the case, and were harmless. Prosecution's voir dire remarks concerning appellant's confession did not constitute error where there was no further reference and the court's charge to the jury rendered any error harmless.

Wooten v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Sixth District, Texarkana


735 S.W.2d 574; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7845



July 21, 1987, Decided  
July 21, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the 102nd Judicial District Court of Bowie County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the 102nd Judicial District Court of Bowie County (Texas), which convicted him for delivery of cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Appellant contended that the trial court should have dismissed his indictment for delivery of cocaine for violation of the Speedy Trial Act, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32A.02 (1987), and the state and federal constitutions. The court did not rule on the statutory violation because the statute had been declared void since the time of appellant's trial. The court also held that there was sufficient evidence to support the trial court's presumed finding that the reason for the delay in appellant's trial was the difficulty in locating him. The court affirmed because appellant was not prejudiced by the delay since the state's witnesses possessed sufficient recall to adequately testify, and appellant failed to show how his defense could possibly have been aided by the testimony of a witness he claimed was missing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction because his right to a speedy trial was not violated under the speedy trial statute since the statute had been declared void, and his constitutional right to a speedy trial was not violated because he was not prejudiced by the delay.
