McGehee v. State


No. 01-86-00982-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7802



July 16, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 180th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 453,433.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction from the 180th District Court, Harris County (Texas), for aggravated sexual assault, contending that Tex. Crim. Proc. Code Ann. art. § 38.071(2) (1987), which allowed the use of a videotape of a child sexual assault victim, was unconstitutional because it denied his right of confrontation, and that the trial court erred in admitting the tape, where it was made after the proceedings began.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was accused of fondling an 8-year old girl. At trial, defendant claimed that he was sleep walking, or that he was confused, believing that he was in bed next to his wife. On appeal, defendant challenged the sufficiency of the evidence, and the admission of a videotape of the child's testimony. The court reviewed the trial record and found only a chain of custody objection to the use of the tape, and held that defendant had failed to preserve the issue for appeal, and had waived any objection. The court then reviewed the trial record for abuse of discretion in rejecting defendant's claim to be sleep walking or confused, and held that the trial court's rejection was within the trial court's sound discretion, and affirmed defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated sexual assault, holding that because defendant had not properly objected to the use of the videotape at trial, defendant had failed to preserve the issue for appeal. The court also held that a rational trier of facts could have found beyond reasonable doubt that the appellant possessed the requisite intent to commit the offense charged and that the evidence was sufficient.

Benitez v. State


No. 2-86-204-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


733 S.W.2d 395; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7979



July 15, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE 335TH DISTRICT COURT OF HOOD COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the 335th District Court of Hood County, Texas, that denied appellant's motion or a new trial after he was convicted and sentenced for aggravated sexual assault, in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.021 (1987). Appellant pleaded guilty to the charge and was sentenced by a jury. Appellant contended that jury misconduct denied him a fair trial, and that the parole law was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pleaded guilty to a charge of aggravated sexual assault, in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.021 (1987). After a trial for sentencing, the jury assessed appellant's punishment. The appeals court affirmed, holding that the trial court did not err in overruling appellant's motion for a new trial, where testimony given at the hearing on the motion failed to show that any misstatement of the law was made by a juror. The evidence did not support the contention that jury misconduct denied appellant of a fair and impartial trial. The court held that the parole law, Tex Crim. Proc. Code Ann. art 37.07, § 4(c) (1985), was not unconstitutionally vague and confusing. The trial court's charge in the case followed the language of the statute and the instructions clearly instructed the jury not to consider the effect that the parole law would have on appellant. Thus, the instructions were not unconstitutionally vague and the conviction and sentence were affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment of the district court that denied appellant's motion for a new trial after he was convicted and sentenced for aggravated sexual assault, holding that there was no jury misconduct that denied appellant a fair and impartial trial. The court held that the parole law was not unconstitutionally vague and confusing.

Franklin v. State


No. 2-86-231-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


733 S.W.2d 715; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7981



July 15, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT NO. 1 OF TARRANT COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the Criminal District Court No. 1 of Tarrant County, Texas, which convicted and sentenced appellant for sexual assault, in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.011 (1987). Appellant contended that the Speedy Trial Act, Tex. Crim. Proc. Code Ann. art. 32A.02, §1(1) (1987), was unconstitutional, and that the trial court erred in failing to submit two requested charges to the jury.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of sexual assault, in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.011 (1987). The jury found allegations of two prior felony convictions to be true and assessed punishment. The appeals court affirmed, holding that the trial court did not err when it overruled appellant's motion to set aside the indictment pursuant to the Speedy Trial Act (Act), Tex. Crim. Proc. Code Ann. art. 32A.02, § 1(1) (1987). The court held that the Act was found to be unconstitutional for violating the separation of powers doctrine of the Texas Constitution. The trial court's failure to submit two requested charges defining "force" and "threat of force" was not in error. As the terms were not statutorily defined at the time of the trial and the terms had common and ordinary meanings that jurors could fairly be presumed to know, the trial court did not err in refusing to submit such charges. The conviction and sentence were affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment of the district court that convicted and sentenced appellant for sexual assault, holding that the trial court did not err when it overruled appellant's motion to set aside his indictment, as the Speedy Trial Act was unconstitutional and void. The trial court did not err when it denied submission of appellant's requested jury charges, because the terms were common and jurors would know their meaning.

Billingslea v. State


No. 05-86-00897-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


734 S.W.2d 422; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8133



July 15, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From a District Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction from the district court, Dallas County (Texas), for injury to an elderly individually by failing to obtain medical care for his mother arguing that the indictment was defective.


OVERVIEW: A jury found appellant guilty of injury to an elderly individual by failing to obtain medical care for his mother. Appellant asserted that the indictment was defective since it failed to allege any statutory duty to act. Decedent was lying in her own urine and excrement and had a large bedsore on her heel, which had eaten away part of the heel. Bedsores on the hip and back were ulcerated and had eaten to the bone. Appellant argued that the indictment failed to allege any statutory duty to act. Texas Penal Code Ann. § 22.04 provided that a person committed an offense if he intentionally, knowingly, recklessly, or with criminal negligence, by act or omission, engaged in conduct that caused seriously bodily injury to an individual who was 65 years of age or older. A statutory duty to act was required. Such duty and its omission must be alleged in the indictment and proved. Therefore, the court found that since the state had not alleged a statutory duty to act in the indictment, the indictment was fundamentally defective and the conviction void.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for injury to an elderly individual by failing to obtain medical care for his mother was reversed because the indictment was fundamentally defective for failing to allege a statutory duty to act.

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 339th Judicial District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Cause No. 437,475.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his murder conviction, from the 339th Judicial District Court of Harris County (Texas), arguing that it was error for the lower court to have denied appellant's request for a jury charge on self-defense and that it was similarly error for the lower court to have instructed the jury on the law of parole pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 (1987).


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of his conviction of murder, contending that the lower court erred in denying his request for a charge on the law of self-defense and erred by instructing the jury on the law of parole in accordance with Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 (1987). On appeal, the conviction was affirmed. In support of its ruling, the court held that a jury charge on the law of self-defense was not required as there was a total lack of evidence on whether appellant reasonably believed force was immediately necessary to protect himself, a reasonable person would not have retreated, or appellant reasonably believed deadly force was immediately necessary to protect himself. The court further held that the issue of the lower court's instruction to the jury concerning the law of parole was not preserved for review as appellant made no objection during trial.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed as there was a total lack of evidence justifying a decision to instruct the jury regarding self-defense, and because the issue of the lower court's instruction to the jury on the law of parole was not preserved for review.

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


732 S.W.2d 796; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7920



July 9, 1987 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The case was before the court on remand to review defendant's claims of error by the trial court (Texas) that denied her motion to quash the indictment for driving under the influence on the grounds that the indictment did not state where the offense took place, and therefore did not give her sufficient notice for the preparation of a defense and to bar subsequent prosecutions.


OVERVIEW: The trial court denied appellant's motion to quash the indictment for driving under the influence (DWI) in a public place under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 67011-1(b) (Supp. 1987). The court affirmed the trial court judgment, and appellant filed a petition for discretionary review in the court of criminal appeals, which remanded the case for further review noting that all authorities cited by the court in its original opinion were decided prior to the passage of the present DWI law, § art. 67011-1(b)(1987), which prohibited drunk driving in a "public place" rather than upon a "public road or highway or street or alley, as was required under prior law, 1979 Tex. Gen. Laws 1608. The court again affirmed the trial court judgment denying the motion to quash concluding that the indictment contained sufficient specificity to meet the required burden of notifying appellant of the particular offense charged and to bar subsequent prosecutions for the offense. The court held that appellant did not present evidence to support the motion to quash or file a motion for new trial, and pled guilty, thereby admitting she was intoxicated in a public place.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment denying appellant's motion to quash an indictment for driving under the influence in a public place, holding that allegations in the indictment were sufficient to apprise appellant of the act she was charged with committing and that there was no merit in the contention that the indictment was not sufficient to enable appellant to prepare a defense or to bar subsequent prosecutions.

Mayers v. State


No. 05-86-01051-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


735 S.W.2d 550; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8257



July 3, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of a District Court of Dallas County, Texas, which, after deferred adjudication, entered a final adjudication of appellant's guilt of aggravated assault, on the ground that the Dallas County Magistrates Act and Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, § 3d were unconstitutional, and that there was insufficient evidence to support the decision of the trial court to adjudicate appellant's guilt.


OVERVIEW: Trial court convicted appellant for aggravated assault but deferred the final adjudication of guilt and placed appellant on probation. Subsequently, the State filed a motion to adjudicate guilt. After a hearing on the motion, the trial court found appellant had violated the terms and conditions of his probation and sentenced him to four years confinement in the Texas Department of Corrections. Appellant sought review claiming that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, § 3d, the statute authorizing deferred adjudication, was unconstitutional because it did not allow him the right to appeal the trial court's decision to proceed to an adjudication of guilt. The court affirmed the trial court judgment. The court found that the Dallas County Magistrate's Act was constitutional and also held that art. 42.12, § 3d was constitutional. The court found that art. 42.12, § 3d did not allow appellant to seek review of the trial court's decision to proceed to an adjudication of guilt, or to challenge the sufficiency of the evidence that supported the trial court decision to adjudicate appellant's guilt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction because the deferred adjudication statute did not give appellant right to appeal, nor right to challenge the sufficiency of the evidence, from a trial court decision to adjudicate guilt after deferred adjudication.

Winthrop v. State


No. 01-87-00189-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


735 S.W.2d 545; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7741



July 2, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 6 of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 890,697.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the County Criminal Court at Law No. 6 of Harris County, Texas, that convicted appellant of the misdemeanor offense of enticing a child, under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 25.04 (1974). Appellant entered a plea of nolo contendere to the charge after the trial court denied appellant's motion to quash the information for being overly broad and vague.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged by information with intent to interfere with the lawful custody of a minor child by knowingly enticing, persuading, and taking the child from the custody of her parents, a violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 25.40 (1974). Appellant entered a plea of nolo contendere to the charge after the trial court denied appellant's motion to quash the information on the grounds that the terms in the information were overly broad and vague in violation of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 21.11. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that when, as in this case, the information mirrored the statutory language of the offense it was legally sufficient to defeat a motion to quash. The court determined that the information described the offense in plain, intelligible language, specified a date that the offense allegedly occurred, and provided appellant with sufficient information to adequately prepare her defense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that accepted appellant's plea of nolo contendere and convicted appellant of the misdemeanor offense of enticing a child. The court held that the trial court did not err when it denied appellant's motion to quash the information because the information set forth the charge in clear intelligible language that provided adequate notice to appellant so she could prepare for her defense.

Scharbrough v. State


No. 2-86-211-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


732 S.W.2d 445; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7848



July 1, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Revised August 10, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM COUNTY CRIMINAL COURT NO. 6 OF TARRANT COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from a judgment of the County Criminal Court No. 6 of Tarrant County (Texas), which convicted him of driving while intoxicated and open container under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 67011-1(b) (1987). Appellant was originally sentenced to 90 days in jail and fined $ 400, but was later placed on probation for 24 months on condition that he serve 30 days in jail.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of driving while intoxicated and open container under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 67011-1(b) (1987). Appellant was sentenced to 90 days in jail and fined $ 400. Appellant challenged his conviction on the ground that the trial court should not have denied his pre-trial motion to quash information. The court affirmed defendant's conviction holding that the information sufficiently apprised appellant of the charges against him as it tracked the language of the statute, the words of the statute had plain meaning and did not prevent appellant from acquiring notice of the offense charged, the statute's caption was not constitutionally defective, and the language of the statute was not vague or ambiguous. As such, appellant was not denied an opportunity to adequately prepare his defense. Accordingly, the trial court did not err in denying appellant his motion to quash information.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting appellant of driving while intoxicated and open container was affirmed. The trial court properly overruled appellant's motion to quash information as it tracked that language of the controlling state and sufficiently apprised appellant of the facts of the charges against him, the words had plain meaning, the language was not vague or ambiguous, and statute's caption was not constitutionally defective.

King v. State


No. 05-86-00461-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


733 S.W.2d 704; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8052



July 1, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Discretionary Review Granted March 14, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM A COUNTY COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from a judgment of the County Court of Dallas County (Texas), which convicted him of driving while intoxicated, sentenced him to 30 days confinement, probated him for two years, fined him $ 500, and suspended his driver's license for one year.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of driving while intoxicated, sentenced to 30 days confinement, given two years probation, fined $ 500, and had his driver's license suspended for one year. On appeal, appellant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence that was obtained during an unlawful seizure pursuant to an illegal traffic roadblock. The court reversed and remanded the case for a new trial holding that the roadblock was not authorized by Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6687(b), § 13 (1986), because it was not solely for the purpose of conducting driver's license checks. Alternatively, the roadblock, in light of the evidence presented, was a subterfuge to catch drunk drivers which was unconstitutional because it failed to pass the test of balancing a legitimate governmental interest against the degree of intrusion on the individual's U.S. Cont. amend. IV rights. Hence, the evidence stemming from the seizure at the invalid roadblock should have been suppressed by the trial court.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court convicting appellant of driving while intoxicated, sentencing him to 30 days, probating him for two years, fining him $ 500, and suspending his driver's license for one year was reversed and remanded for a new trial. The roadblock was unconstitutional and was not authorized by statute because it was not solely for the purpose of conducting driver's license checks.

Powell v. Texas State Bd. of Medical Examiners


No. 05-86-00615-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


734 S.W.2d 138; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8120



June 30, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant medical doctor sought review of the order entered by a District Court of Dallas County (Texas) which affirmed the decision by appellee board of medical examiners to revoke appellant's license to practice medicine, after appellant was convicted of two counts of commercially dispensing a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: Appellant medical doctor was convicted of commercially dispensing a controlled substance, a felony. Upon notice and after hearing, appellee board of medical examiners revoked appellant's license to practice medicine, pursuant to the Texas Medical Practice Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4495b, §§ 3.08(2) and 4.01 (1987). The trial court affirmed appellee's decision. Appellant contended that the indictments for which he was convicted were not under the Controlled Substances Act, but were defined in rules promulgated by the Director of the Texas Department of Public Safety. The court held that, regardless of how the indictments characterized the offenses and regardless of whether the charged offenses were offenses under the Texas Controlled Substances Act, the offenses for which appellant was convicted were clearly offenses under the Texas Controlled Substances Act. Under § 4.01, appellee's decision was not erroneous and the trial court did not err in affirming that decision. Appellant also attacked the validity of the criminal convictions underlying this action; however, none of his contentions concerned jurisdiction, and the judgments were regular on their faces.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment which affirmed appellee board of medical examiner's decision to revoke appellant medical doctor's license for convictions of commercially dispensing a controlled substance. Appellee was not in error for revoking appellant's license because he was convicted of offenses that required the revocation, regardless of how the offenses were charged.

 

1052 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Crawford v. State


No. B14-86-230-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7677



June 25, 1987, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: State's Motion for Rehearing on Petition for Discretionary Review Denied January 30, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 228th District Court of Harris County, Cause No. 434,200.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgement of the 228th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which convicted defendant of murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder and appealed. The court affirmed, finding that defendant's speedy trial right, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32A.02, was not violated where defendant signed three agreed reset forms and was tried within 120 days. The court found that sufficient evidence established a corpus delicti of the murder. One occasion of improper jury argument about which defendant complained was proper because it commented on evidence presented at trial, and the other two occasions were cured when defendant's objections were sustained and instructions to disregard were given. The court concluded that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(a) was not unconstitutional, that defendant could not complain on appeal of the denial of a motion for severance that he never made, and that the state did not bolster its witness's testimony by having a police officer testify before her. The trial court's refusal to admit defendant's complete written confession and his audio recorded oral confession was proper where exclusion did not infringe on defendant's constitutional rights, but admission would have infringed on co-defendant's constitutional right to confrontation.


OUTCOME: The judgment that convicted defendant of murder was affirmed because the trial court's refusal to admit defendant's complete written confession and his audio recorded oral confession was proper, defendant's speedy trial right was not violated, sufficient evidence established a corpus delicti of the murder, and each occasion of state's improper jury argument was cured.

 

1053 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Glen Ridge I Condominiums, Ltd. v. Federal Sav. & Loan Ins. Corp.


No. 05-85-00873-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


734 S.W.2d 374; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8054



June 25, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Reported at: 734 S.W.2d 374 at 387.<DSPQ2>


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Opinion of December 30, 1986, Reported at: 734 S.W.2d 374. APPEAL FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, the Federal Savings and Loan Insurance Corporation, sought a motion for rehearing in a case that originated in a District Court of Dallas County (Texas). Appellee contended that appellant condominium developers should have been required to exhaust administrative remedies and that the court erred in its analysis of constitutional issues.


OVERVIEW: Appellee, the Federal Savings and Loan Insurance Corporation, contended on motion for rehearing that the court's previous opinion erred in failing to apply a proper constitutional analysis and in failing to require exhaustion of administrative remedies as a condition to appellant condominium developers' appeal. The court denied appellee's motion for rehearing. Based on its analysis of recent precedent, the court held that appellee's claims of exclusive jurisdiction under 12 U.S.C.S. §§ 1464 and 1729 offended the basic principles of U.S. Const. art. III and were unconstitutional to the extent that judicial review of state law counterclaims raised in administrative proceedings was improperly restricted to a determination of whether administrative action was arbitrary and capricious. With respect to the doctrine of exhaustion of remedies, the court noted that it was not a jurisdictional rule but was a matter committed to judicial discretion and an exercise of comity only. Finally, as to construction of statutes, the court noted that although a court would strain to construe a statute so as to avoid a constitutional issue, it would not judicially rewrite the statute to do so.


OUTCOME: The motion for rehearing was denied because the language and prevailing construction of jurisdictional statutes were too plain to support a construction that would avoid their constitutional infirmity; thus, the court had to address the constitutional issue. Further, exhaustion of remedies was not a jurisdictional rule.

James v. State


Nos. A14-86-00262-CR, A14-86-00263-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7609



June 18, 1987, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 228th Judicial District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Cause Nos. 439,420, 439,421.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his two convictions for burglary of a vehicle, entered in the 228th Judicial District Court of Harris County (Texas).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by jury for two offenses of burglary of a vehicle. Defendant appealed, contending insufficiency of the evidence to sustain the convictions and trial court error in instructing the jury on the law of parol in accordance with Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4. The court affirmed both convictions. Relative to the evidence, the court analyzed the facts. Police officers were conducting surveillance in a garage where numerous vehicles had been burglarized. After observing defendant leaving the garage, the officers stopped him and discovered two car stereos with damaged wiring wrapped in a woman's coat defendant was carrying. The police returned to the garage and found two cars that had been broken into, the owners who had identified the stereos, and the woman who owned the coat. Additionally, defendant's fingerprint was recovered from the door handle of one of the damaged cars, and defendant offered to pay for the damage. The court found sufficient evidence to sustain the convictions. Relative to the instructional error claim, the court found that defendant failed to preserve the matter for review by not objecting to the instruction at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's trial court convictions for burglary of a vehicle because the evidence produced by the state was sufficient to support the convictions and because defendant failed to preserve the instructional error claim for review in not objecting to it at trial.

 

1055 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Richardson v. State


No. 3-85-289-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


733 S.W.2d 947; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8064



June 17, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Motion for Rehearing on Petition for Discretionary Review Denied August 12, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 331ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT, NO. 78,779, HONORABLE BOB PERKINS, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court of Travis County, 331st Judicial District (Texas), which convicted him of involuntary manslaughter, a lesser-included offense of murder for which he was indicted, under Tex. Pen. Code Ann. §§ 19.02, 19.05 (1974). Defendant challenged the jury instruction on parole, jury misconduct, use of grand jury testimony, denial of a motion in limine, and refusal to charge criminal negligence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with murder and convicted of the lesser-included offense of involuntary manslaughter, under Tex. Pen. Code Ann. §§ 19.02 and 19.05 (1974). On appeal, the court held that the parole instruction statute, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(a) (1987), did not produce an unconstitutional judicial interference with the clemency powers assigned to the Governor and was not unconstitutionally vague. The court also held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it overruled defendant's motion for new trial based on one juror's misconduct in considering the effect of parole in assessing punishment. The court found that relevant portions of grand jury testimony of one of defendant's witnesses had been disclosed to defendant. The court further held that a motion in limine did not preserve anything for appeal where defendant did not present or object to the evidence at trial. The court also held that defendant was not entitled to the criminal negligence instruction because he was aware of the risk involved in his conduct and the intervention of an unanticipated factor did not alter that fact. Therefore, the court affirmed the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court convicting defendant of involuntary manslaughter because, inter alia, the jury instruction on parole did not violate the doctrine of separation of powers and was not unconstitutionally vague, a single juror's misconduct did not invalidate the verdict, denial of a motion in limine did not preserve the issue for appeal, and the criminal negligence charge was properly refused.

 

1056 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Leal v. State


No. A14-86-346-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7539



June 11, 1987, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 351st District Court of Harris County, Trial Court No. 428,263.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the 351st District Court of Harris County (Texas) for burglary of a habitation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of burglary of a habitation and contended that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. art. 37.07, § 4 was unconstitutional. Defendant alleged that the prosecutor improperly expressed its opinion during closing argument that defendant was guilty. Defendant also contended that the trial court improperly allowed admission of an officer's testimony regarding defendant's character. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction. Section 4, which prohibited jurors from considering parole and good conduct time, was not unconstitutional. The section was designed to benefit defendants because it was devised to reduce the incidence of juror misconduct. The trial court immediately instructed the jury to disregard the prosecutor's statements, so such instruction cured improper jury argument concerning the statements. Defendant failed to properly preserve for review issues concerning the officer's character testimony because defendant did not raise such objection at trial. Defendant did not object to the testimony as improper character testimony.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for burglary of a habitation. The trial court's instruction to the jury to disregard the prosecutor's improper statements cured any prejudice. Defendant did not object to the officer's testimony as improper character evidence, so such issue was not properly preserved for appeal.

 

1057 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Suburban Homes v. Austin-Northwest Dev. Co.


No. 01-86-00761-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


734 S.W.2d 89; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7545



June 11, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 125th District Court Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 80-39524.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant home manufacturer challenged a decision from the 125th District Court Harris County (Texas) that granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, developer and engineer, in appellant's cross-action for contribution and indemnity.


OVERVIEW: Homeowners initiated an action against appellant home manufacturer alleging that appellant sold them homes on a geological fault line. Five years after such action was filed, appellant filed a cross-action for indemnity and contribution against appellees, developer and engineer. Appellees filed motions for summary judgment on the grounds that the 10 year statutes of repose found in Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code § 16.008 and § 16.009 barred appellant's action. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellees. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision. Appellees proved that there work was completed more than 10 years before suit, so appellant's action was barred. Appellant did not provide any evidence supporting its allegation that appellees' fraud tolled the running of the statute. Appellees were entitled to the protection afforded engineers and developers under the statutes because appellant did not produce any evidence that appellees were not registered engineers or developers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision because appellant home manufacturer's action was barred by the 10 year statute of repose. There was no dispute of fact because appellees proved that their work was substantially completed more than 10 years before suit. Appellant failed to bring forth any evidence supporting its fraudulent concealment allegations.

 

1058 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Sparks v. State


No. B14-86-335-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7553



June 11, 1987, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 338th District Court of Harris County, Cause No. 436,399.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the 338th District Court of Harris County (Texas) for aggravated robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a gas station with a pistol and ordered the clerk to hand over money. When defendant fled, the clerk described defendant to police officers. Officers observed defendant in a vehicle. Defendant was subsequently stopped and a search revealed a pistol. The clerk also identified defendant as the perpetrator. Defendant was convicted of aggravated robbery and contended that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress. Defendant also alleged the trial court improperly gave a parole instruction pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. art. 37.07, § 4. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction. The trial court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress. Officers were justified in stopping defendant because defendant matched the clerk's description. Officers assumed defendant was armed, so they lawfully searched him. The trial court gave the statutorily mandated parole charge under art. 37.07 and such article was previously held constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated robbery because the trial court's statutorily mandated parole instruction was constitutional. The search and seizure was lawful because defendant matched the clerk's description of the perpetrator of the robbery and officers assumed that defendant was armed based on the offense.

 

1059 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Whitney v. State


No. 01-86-00639-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7560



June 11, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 248th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 447,671.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the 248th District Court, Harris County (Texas) for criminal mischief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled no contest to criminal mischief. After defendant was sentenced, he contended that his plea was not voluntarily entered because the trial court did not explain the consequences of a nolo contendere plea. Defendant also challenged the constitutionality of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 26.13(c), which provided that substantial compliance with the admonishment statute was sufficient. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction. Pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 26.13(b), the trial court did not have to define or explain a nolo contendere plea. The trial court was only required to determine if defendant entered his plea knowingly and voluntarily. The record established that the trial court properly accepted defendant's plea. Defendant could not challenge the constitutionality of art. 26.13(c) because it was not applicable. The trial court far exceeded the requirements of the admonishment rule, so the issue of substantial compliance was irrelevant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction because his plea was voluntarily and knowingly entered. The trial court properly admonished defendant, so defendant could not challenge the constitutionality of the substantial compliance provision of the admonishment rule. The trial court did not have to explain the consequences of the nolo contendere plea.

 

1060 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Lovelace v. Sabine Consol., Inc.


No. C14-86-348CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


733 S.W.2d 648; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7566



June 11, 1987, Decided  
June 11, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 152nd District Court of Harris County, Trial Court No. 84-07260, Jack O'Neill, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, construction company, sought review of a judgment of the 152nd District Court of Harris County (Texas), which awarded damages to appellee, contractor, for breach of contract, breach of fiduciary duty, and fraud in connection with a joint venture agreement. Appellant argued that the agreement was illegal and unenforceable and that the trial court erred in rulings on discovery, evidence, lost profits and punitive damages.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, construction company, was awarded two contracts with a city to construct sewers. Appellant entered into two joint venture agreements with appellee, contractor, to share responsibility, control, and profits of the sewer projects. Appellant diverted money from the projects to his own account and appellee filed an action for an accounting and damages. A jury awarded actual and punitive damages, along with attorney's fees. On appeal, the court held that the ordinance approving the contracts with appellant, which prohibited subcontracting, did not make the joint venture agreements illegal. The court also held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in limiting discovery or, if it did, it was harmless and not grounds for reversal and retrial. However, the court held that the trial court erred in awarding punitive damages where there was no independent finding of actual damages in tort and the evidence offered to prove lost profits on one of the projects did not support that part of the verdict. The court also held that the appeal bond did not violate Tex. Const. art. I, § 13. Therefore, the court modified the judgment as to damages and otherwise affirmed it.


OUTCOME: The court held that punitive damages could not be awarded in the absence of an independent finding of actual damages in tort and that the evidence did not support damages for lost profits on one of the projects under a joint venture agreement between appellant, construction company, and appellee, contractor. Therefore, the court modified the judgment to exclude punitive damages and the lost profits; otherwise, it affirmed the judgment.

Phillips v. State


No. 01-86-00548-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7446



June 4, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 338th District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 451,014.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought reversal of the judgment of the 338th District Court of Harris County (Texas) that convicted him of murder where the trial court denied his motion to quash the indictment for its failure to be specific, and admitted evidence of an allegedly void prior conviction.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found guilty of aggravated assault. He appealed and asserted that the trial court erred by refusing to grant his motion to quash the indictment for its failure to be specific and to give him fair notice of the particular offense, and by admitting evidence of a prior conviction that appellant alleged was void. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and held that the indictment was sufficient to apprise appellant of the charge against him. The indictment set forth all of the elements of aggravated assault, including the use of a deadly weapon, and specified that the deadly weapon was a firearm. The court also determined that the indictment is not required to allege a specific place where the offense occurred when the location is not an element of the offense charged. With regard to the evidence of appellant's prior conviction, which was admitted during the punishment phase, the court found that appellant made no effort to demonstrate how, or on what basis he claimed the prior conviction was void. Therefore, he did not preserve any complaint for review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court because the indictment was sufficient to apprise appellant of the charge against him, as it set forth all of the elements of aggravated assault. Further, the court determined that appellant made no effort to demonstrate how, or on what basis he claimed the prior conviction was void. Therefore, it was not error for the trial court to admit evidence of it.

Railroad Com. of Texas v. Bishop Petroleum, Inc.


No. 10-86-140-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Tenth District, Waco


736 S.W.2d 724; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8239; 101 Oil & Gas Rep. 559



May 28, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From 87th Judicial District Court Freestone County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, tract owner and the Texas Railroad Commission (commission), sought review of the judgment of the 87th Judicial District Court, Freestone County, Texas, which reversed and remanded the findings of appellant commission ordering the pooling of tracts owned by appellant tract owner and appellee company pursuant to the Mineral Interest Pooling Act, Tex. Nat. Res. Code Ann. § 86.002(4) (1978).


OVERVIEW: Appellant tract owner applied to appellant Texas Railroad Commission (commission) to pool its tract with a tract appellee company owned. Appellant commission ordered the tracts pooled and ordered appellant tract owner to pay appellee a risk penalty and costs. Appellee challenged the pooling order and the trial court reversed and remanded with instructions to dismiss the proceeding for lack of jurisdiction. On appeal, the court reversed and affirmed the pooling order, holding that appellant commission's pooling authority was limited by the definition of "common reservoir" in the Mineral Interest Pooling Act, Tex. Nat. Res. Code Ann. § 86.002(4) (1978). Regarding reviewable errors, the court found that it was error to reverse the pooling order because substantial evidence supported the findings and the court could not say as a matter of law that appellant commission exceeded its authority.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and affirmed the pooling order of appellant Texas Railroad Commission (commission) in favor of appellant tract owner. Appellant commission's pooling authority was limited by the definition of "common reservoir," and substantial evidence supported the findings regarding the alleged errors that were reserved for review.

Bullock v. Texas Monthly, Inc.


No. 14,692


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


731 S.W.2d 160; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7654



May 27, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing overruled June 24, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Travis County, 345th Judicial District, No. 378,384, Honorable Joe B. Dibrell, Jr., Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant public officials sought review of the decision of the 345th Judicial District Court, Travis County (Texas), which, in appellee publisher's action for recovery of sales taxes paid under protest, entered a judgment in favor of appellee. The lower court found that a statutory tax exemption under Tex. Tax. Code Ann. § 151.312, violated the equal protection clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OVERVIEW: Appellee publisher brought an action to recover sales taxes that were assessed by appellant public officials. The trial court held that the tax exemption granted to religious periodicals under Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 151.312 (1987), violated the equal protection clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and ordered that appellants reimburse appellee for the sales taxes. Appellants sought review. On review the court reversed and rendered a judgment that appellee take nothing. The court held that the trial court erred when it opined that the statutory tax exemption violated the equal protection clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and the equal and uniform clause of Tex. Const. Ann. art 8, § 1(1984), because the legislature had a rational basis for enacting the statute. The court also held that the statute did not violate the establishment clause of U.S. Const. amend. I, because it did not excessively entangle the state in religious activities. The court further held that the legislature's failure to provide a tax benefit to publications other than religious publications did not violate appellee's right of free speech under U.S. Const. amend. I, and Tex. Const. Ann. art. 1, § 8 (1984).


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court was reversed, because the trial court erred when it determined that the statutory tax exemption violated appellant publisher's constitutional rights to freedom of speech and equal protection.

 

1065 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Randolph v. State


No. 01-86-00349-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7343



May 21, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 351st District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 409,836.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction by the 351st District Court of Harris County (Texas), of the offense of burglary of a building with intent to commit theft.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted in the trial court of the offense of burglary of a building with intent to commit theft. The court affirmed. The court held that although the form of one of the prosecutor's questions was objectionable, its substance was not inherently harmful. The instruction to the jury to disregard removed whatever harmful effect the witness's expression of his opinion may have had on the jury's evaluation of appellant's credibility. The court also held that in closing argument, the state was allowed to comment on appellant's failure to call competent and material witnesses, and to argue that the reason for such failure was that any such testimony would be unfavorable to appellant. The court further held that an instruction to the jury on probable cause for appellant's arrest would have been required by Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.23, only if the evidence to establish the legality of his arrest had been in dispute. Appellant's testimony raised no factual issues about the probable cause for his arrest, and therefore no special instruction was required.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction of appellant of the offense of burglary of a building with intent to commit theft. The court held that the trial court's instruction to the jury to disregard removed whatever harmful effect that a witness's expression had on the jury's evaluation of appellant's credibility.

Cole v. State


No. 01-86-00919-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7344



May 21, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 185th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 445,238.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the 185th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of burglary of a building with intent to commit theft. Appellant argued that the trial court erred in admitting into evidence the security company tape recording of the break-in without the proper predicate having been shown. He also argued that the trial court improperly instructed the jury on parole laws.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was arrested for burglary of a building after a security monitor signaled a break-in at a plumbing company. Police arrived to find appellant first crouching in a window of the business and then climbing out of the broken window. Appellant was convicted of burglary of a building with intent to commit theft. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that appellant's objection to the admission of the security tape of the break-in at trial did not comport with his complaint on appeal of improper predicate for the admission of the tape. Further, although the evidence showed that the security console held many accounts, only the plumbing company's was on the screen the night of appellant's arrest. Additionally, even if proper predicate for the tape was not laid, such error was harmless where appellant was seen exiting the building through a broken window, and he attempted to flee the scene. The court held that appellant had failed to preserve his argument that the jury instruction on parole laws given in accordance with Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 (Supp. 1987), was unconstitutional because he did not object to the instruction at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for burglary of a building and held that, even if the proper predicate for the admission of the security company's tape was not laid, the error was harmless because there was sufficient evidence to support the conviction without the tape. Appellant could not complain of the constitutionality of the jury instruction on parole laws where he failed to object at trial.

Williams v. State


No. 01-86-00339-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7364



May 21, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 208TH District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 435,260.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the 208th District Court of Harris County, Texas, which found appellant guilty of the felony offense of injury to a child. Appellant contended that the trial court erred when it denied her request to withdraw her nolo contendere plea and that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.04 (Supp. 1981), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was indicted for the felony offense of injury to a child. After proper admonishment, the appellant entered a plea of nolo contendere without an agreed recommendation of punishment by appellee state. The trial court found appellant guilty as charged and reset the punishment hearing pending preparation and review of a pre-sentence investigation report. After hearing evidence at the punishment hearing, the court assessed punishment at two years confinement. The appellant then requested to withdraw her plea, which was denied. Appellant challenged the judgment, raising two points of error. The court affirmed the trial court judgment and overruled both points of error. First, because appellant had not challenged the constitutionality of the statute in the trial court, the issue was waived. Secondly, the trial court was not required to order that the plea of nolo contendere be withdrawn.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of appellant of injury to a child. The court held that because appellant did not challenge the constitutionality of the statute in the trial court, that the issue was waived. The court also held that the trial court could consider the sufficiency of the evidence prior to a withdrawal of the plea of nolo contendere.

Ngoc Van Le v. State


No. C14-86-213-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


733 S.W.2d 280; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7308



May 14, 1987, Decided  
May 14, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 248th District court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court No. 432,585.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction by the 248th District Court of Harris County (Texas), of aggravated robbery.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted in the trial court of aggravated robbery. The court affirmed. The court held that the trial court properly denied his motion to dismiss pursuant to the Speedy trial Act, Tex. Crim. Proc. Code Ann. art. 32A.02 (Supp. 1987). The court reasoned that the evidence adduced by appellant was insufficient to rebut the state's prima facie showing that the state was ready for trial in conformity with the Speedy Trial Act. The court also held that the trial court did not err in overruling appellant's objection to the competency of a child witness. The court reasoned that in response to appellant's objection, the trial court conducted an examination of the witness and found her to be competent. The court held that appellant received all the relief he requested. The court held that the trial court did not err in admitting evidence of a pretrial lineup, which was held when appellant was not represented by counsel. The court reasoned that the right to counsel under U.S. Const. amend. VI attached only upon or after formal initiation of judicial proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of appellant of aggravated robbery. The court held that the trial court did not err when it overruled appellant's objection to the competency of a child witness. The court found that the trial court had conducted an examination of the witness and had found her to be competent.

 

1069 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Detamore v. Sullivan


No. A14-87-202-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


731 S.W.2d 122; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7310



May 14, 1987, Decided  
May 14, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ORIGINAL PROCEEDING WRIT OF MANDAMUS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator debtors filed a petition for writ of mandamus following the judgment of respondent, the County Civil Court at Law Number Two of Harris County (Texas), which ordered a turnover of relator's stock for sale under a writ of execution in favor of plaintiff creditor, to direct respondent to vacate its turnover order, and to nullify recognition of a foreign country money judgment under Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. §§ 36.001-.008 (1986).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff creditor, real party in interest, obtained a default judgment against relator debtor in a Canadian court. Plaintiff filed the default judgment and an affidavit of last known address in the respondent county court, requesting issuance of an abstract of judgment and a writ of execution. A corrected abstract of judgment and a corrected execution was issued. Respondent also issued a turnover order of relator debtor's stock for a sale under the writ of execution. Relator filed a petition for writ of mandamus on the grounds that the foreign judgment was not properly recognized in the absence of a plenary suit and a plenary hearing and Tex. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 36.00 et seq., was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court conditionally granted the petition and held a plenary suit or a plenary hearing was not required for recognition and enforcement of a foreign money judgment and § 36.00 et seq., was unconstitutional because it did not provide a procedure for relator, a judgment debtor, to receive notice and to have an opportunity to assert grounds for nonrecognition of a foreign country money judgment. Therefore, any enforcement of the foreign country money judgment was void.


OUTCOME: The court conditionally granted relator debtor's petition for writ of mandamus and held the applicable statute did not require a plenary suit or a plenary hearing for recognition and enforcement of a foreign country money judgment and the statute was unconstitutional because it provided for recognition and enforcement of a foreign country money judgment but provided no procedures to assert nonrecognition of such judgment, violating due process.

 

1070 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Rascoe v. Anabtawi


No. 09-86-217-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Ninth District, Beaumont


730 S.W.2d 460; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7577



May 14, 1987, Decided  
May 14, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE 172ND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF JEFFERSON COUNTY, TEXAS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, medical malpractice claimants, sought review of an order in favor of appellees, medical care providers, by the 172nd Judicial District Court of Jefferson County, (Texas), which held that appellants' claim for medical malpractice was not tolled under the tolling provisions of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5538.


OVERVIEW: Appellants claimants brought a wrongful death and survival action against appellees medical care providers. Appellants gave notice of intent to file suit which, under the Medical Liability Insurance Improvement Act (MLIIA), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, §. 4.01(c), gave appellant an 75 days in addition to the two years from decedent's death in which to file suit. The suit was filed two years and 78 days after decedent's death. The trial court granted summary judgment to appellees. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5538 did not toll the statute of limitations on survival actions, and did not apply to wrongful death claims. The court ruled that art. 5538 was not specifically listed in the tolling provision of the MLIIA art. 4590i, § 10.01, and was not part of the statutory scheme on medical liability claims. The court further held that art. 4590i, § 10.01, was not violative of the open courts provision of Tex. Const. art. I, § 13, because appellants could have discovered the injury well within the statute of limitations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment in favor of the appellees, medical care providers, and against appellants, medical malpractice claimants, because the tolling provision cited by appellants were not a part of the statutory scheme of medical liability, and the statutory scheme did not violate the open courts provision of the Texas constitution.

 

1071 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Stout v. Grand Prairie Independent School Dist.


No. 05-86-00729-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


733 S.W.2d 290; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7915



May 14, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FOM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants parents and student sought review of a take-nothing judgment in the District Court of Dallas County (Texas), which denied appellants recovery against appellees school district and teacher for injuries sustained by appellant student while practicing as a cheerleader. Appellants claimed that Tex. Educ. Code Ann. § 21.912(b), prohibiting recovery, violated due process and equal protection under constitutions of Texas and United States.


OVERVIEW: Appellants parents and student brought negligence claims against appellees school district and teacher for injuries sustained by appellant student while practicing cheerleading at appellee school district under supervision of appellee teacher. The trial court granted appellees summary judgment, pursuant to Tex. Educ. Code Ann. § 21.912(b), which prohibited recovery against appellees. Appellants sought reversal and claimed that § 21.912(b) violated appellants' due process under Tex. Const. art. I, § 19, and U.S. Const. amend. XIV § 1; equal protection under Tex. Const. art. I § 3, and U.S. Const. amend. XIV; and the open courts provision of Tex. Const. amend. art. I § 13. The court affirmed the trial court judgment and held that based upon the state's legitimate interest in public education, a rational basis for protecting school districts by sovereign immunity from negligence claims by students and parents, such as appellants, and consequently § 21.912(b), did not violate due process under art. I, § 19, and amend. XIV § 1; equal protection under art. I § 3, and amend. XIV; or the open courts provision of art. I § 13.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of appellees school district and teacher, because appellants parents and student were not denied due process or equal protection by being prohibited from bringing negligence claims against appellees.

 

1072 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Grand Prairie Hospital Authority v. Dallas County Appraisal Dist.


No. 05-86-00787-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


730 S.W.2d 849; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7595



May 11, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hospital authority sought review of an order by the District Court, Dallas County (Texas), which granted summary judgment to appellees, appraisal district and appraisal review board, on appellant's claim that an office building owned by appellant was exempt from taxation, pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4437e, § 16 and Tex. Tax. Code Ann. § 11.11, because it was used for a public purpose.


OVERVIEW: Appellant hospital district brought an action against appellees, appraisal district and appraisal review board, to obtain a judicial declaration that a medical office building owned by appellant was exempt from taxation. All parties moved for summary judgment, and the motions of appellees were granted. Appellant sought review, arguing that issues of fact existed as to whether the property was used for public purposes, and that issues of fact existed as to whether the building was exempt from taxation under Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 11.11 and Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4437e, § 16. The court affirmed, stating that in order for property to receive tax exempt status, pursuant to Tex. Tax. Code Ann. § 11.11 and Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 2(a) the property had to be used for a purely public purpose. The court also stated that the test for whether the property was held for only public purposes was whether it was used exclusively for the use and benefit of the public. The court held that since offices where leased to physicians in connection with their private practice, the property was not held for a purely public purpose and therefore was not exempt from taxation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to appellees, appraisal district and appraisal review board, holding that a medical office building owned by appellant hospital authority was not exempt from taxation because it was not used for a purely public purpose. Appellant rented space to physicians for the physicians' private practice, and such use destroyed any exemption from taxation.

 

1073 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Dubin v. Carrier Corp.


No. 01-86-00561-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


731 S.W.2d 651; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7230; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P11,453



May 7, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 80th District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 84-06504-A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, parents, retailer and apartment owner, sought review of a judgment from the 80th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee manufacturers in a wrongful death action relating to a faulty wall heater.


OVERVIEW: Following cross-actions by appellants, parents, retailer, and apartment owner, appellee manufacturers moved for summary judgment in a wrongful death action. Appellees claimed that the wrongful death action involving the installation and manufacture of a faulty wall heater was barred by the 10-year statute of repose under Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code § 16.009 (1986). The trial court granted appellees' motion for summary judgment. The court reversed this decision. The terms of § 16.009 required that appellees conclusively establish that the heater they designed and manufactured was installed in decedent's apartment more than 10 years prior to the commencement of this action, and also that the heater constituted an "improvement" to real property. Appellees showed that the wall heater constituted an improvement to real property, but they failed to show that the wall heater was installed more than 10 years prior to the action. Allegations in appellees' summary judgment motions were not summary judgment evidence, and testimony failed to conclusively establish the date that the heater was installed. Thus, the trial court's decision had to be reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee manufacturers, because appellees did not present proper summary judgment evidence that the wrongful death action involving a faulty wall heater was barred by the 10-year statute of repose.

 

1074 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Houston v. Harris County Outdoor Advertising Asso.


No. A14-86-00901-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


732 S.W.2d 42; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7245



May 7, 1987, Decided  
May 7, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 281st Judicial District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Cause No. 86-08560.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought the review of the order of the 281st Judicial District Court of Harris County, Texas, which granted appellee advertisers' suit for declaratory judgment regarding appellant's regulation of billboards in and around the city.


OVERVIEW: Appellee advertisers filed a suit for a declaratory judgment regarding appellant city's regulation of billboards in and around the city. The lower court entered an order concluding that appellant's regulation of the billboards violated the state constitution and was inconsistent with federal and state laws also regulating the billboards. On appeal, the court reversed the order of the lower court holding that appellant's regulatory scheme of the billboards was consistent with the grant of authority delegated to it by the state legislature under H.B. 1330, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. arts. 1015(o), 1015(o)(1) (1986). The court also held that appellant was a home rule city under Tex. Const. art. XI, § 5 and had the power to enact ordinances in its exercise of its home rule powers as long as the ordinances were not inconsistent with state laws or the state constitution. Finally, the court, using the plain meaning rule of construction, held that certain provisions of H.B. 1330 were not void as vague or ambiguous under the state constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the lower court, which granted appellee advertisers' suit for declaratory judgment in appellees' suit regarding appellant city's regulation of the billboards in and around the city; appellant's regulation of the billboards were not in conflict with the federal and state statutes, which allocated such regulatory authority to it.

OVERVIEW: Plaintiff patient's representative appealed from a summary judgment granted in favor of defendant health care providers in a medical malpractice case. 1076 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Cleveland v. State


No. 2-86-078-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


728 S.W.2d 490; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7216



April 30, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Motion for Rehearing Granted June 11, 1987, Reported at: 730 S.W.2d 886.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT NO. 2 OF TARRANT COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenges his conviction from Criminal District Court No. 2 of Tarrant County (Texas) for burglary of a building alleging that the lower court erred in overruling his motion to dismiss the jury panel because of systematic exclusion.


OVERVIEW: During his trial on charges of burglary of a building, appellant filed a motion requesting the lower court to dismiss the jury panel because of state's systematic exclusion of black jurors. Appellant submitted testimony in support of the motion and state did not controvert appellant's evidence. The lower court overruled appellant's motion. On appeal, the court held that pursuant to the Batson test, appellant established a prima facie case of purposeful discrimination in state's jury selection because as an African American, appellant was the member of a cognizable racial group, state used its peremptory challenges to remove from venire members of appellant's race, and did so on account of race. The court found that the burden shifted to state to provide a neutral explanation for the exclusion and state's denial alone was insufficient to meet the burden. The court upheld appellant's conviction as there was sufficient supporting evidence and ordered a new jury trial.


OUTCOME: Conviction was upheld and a new jury trial was ordered on the grounds that appellant established a prima facie case of state's purposeful discrimination in jury selection and state did not meet its burden of providing a neutral explanation for the exclusion.

 

1077 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Clark v. State


No. 2-85-239-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


728 S.W.2d 484; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7243



April 30, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 297TH DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the 297th District Court of Tarrant County (Texas), which convicted him of aggravated sexual assault, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.021(a)(5) (1987), and sentenced him to life after a finding of two previous felony convictions.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted appellant of aggravated sexual assault, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.021(a)(5) (1987), and sentenced him to life after a finding of two previous felony convictions. Appellant challenged his conviction. On appeal the court affirmed the trial court. The court first held that a videotape was properly admitted as the officer who took the video had extensive experience and videotaped 20 to 30 child victims a month, so that he was competent. The court also held that, due to an amendment to Tex. Const. art. III, § 35, the court no longer had the power to declare an act of the legislature unconstitutional due to the insufficiency of the caption, so that appellant's challenge to the caption was automatically overruled. The court further held that a declarant's out of court statement did not violate the confrontation clause as the complainant was effectively cross-examined. Finally, appellant could not question the constitutionality of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.071, because it was appellee state who would be the aggrieved party, not appellant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction because a videotape was properly admitted as the taping officer had extensive experience, a constitutional amendment precluded challenges to jury instruction captions, the complainant was effectively cross-examined and so was confronted, despite being out of court, and appellant could not challenge the constitutionality of a statute as appellee state would be the aggrieved party.

Ex parte McIntyre


No. 04-86-00321-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


730 S.W.2d 411; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7495



April 30, 1987, Decided  
April 30, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Corrected June 18, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON RELATOR'S PETITION FOR WRIT OF HABEAS CORPUS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator ex-husband filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus following the contempt order of the trial court (Texas), which confined him until child and spousal support arrearage, costs, and attorney fees were paid.


OVERVIEW: Relator ex-husband's ex-wife filed a motion to hold relator in contempt for failure to pay child support, past-due spousal and child support ordered by the divorce decree, and for refusing to turn over certain personal property awarded her in the divorce decree. The trial court found relator guilty of contempt and ordered confinement until relator had paid the arrearages, costs, attorney fees. Relator filed a petition for habeas corpus. The court found that the trial court's contempt decree was not void. Although relator proceeded pro se at the contempt hearing, he was fully aware of his right to counsel and was not indigent. Although the court reversed the finding of contempt for relator's refusal to surrender items, the court held that relator was not entitled to release from the coercive portion of his confinement because the void portion of the judgment was severable. Relator was remanded to the custody of the sheriff for confinement pursuant to the remainder of the trial court's order of commitment.


OUTCOME: Relator ex-husband's request for habeas corpus relief was granted only to the extent that the trial court's contempt order directed confinement for relator's refusal to surrender items because that part of the contempt order was void. However, that portion was severable, and the portion that ordered confinement for relator's failure to pay child and spousal support arrearages, costs, and attorney fees was proper and upheld.

Beeson v. State


No. 2-86-130-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


728 S.W.2d 950; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7367



April 29, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE 89TH DISTRICT COURT OF WICHITA COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the 89th District Court of Wichita County (Texas), which convicted him of aggravated robbery in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 29.03 (1974).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated robbery in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 29.03 (1974). Appellant sought review of his conviction, alleging that two jury instructions were improper and constituted reversible error. The court affirmed, rejecting appellant's contention that the trial court had to define "knowingly" and "intentionally" to the jurors for the conviction to stand. While the trial court should have included definitions in the charges to the jury, appellant did not object, and the error did not rise to egregious harm. The court considered the entire jury charge, the state of the evidence, the argument of counsel, and other relevant evidence. The court also held that the trial judge's misstatement in the parole instruction was harmless because a second instruction directed the jury not to consider an award or forfeiture of good conduct time.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for aggravated robbery, holding that although the jury instructions regarding the offense were improperly worded, they did not cause egregious harm to appellant based on the relevant evidence and that the parole instruction was proper although the wording was in error.
