Ned v. State


No. 09-84-085 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Ninth District, Beaumont


729 S.W.2d 365; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7428



April 29, 1987, Decided  
April 29, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEALED FROM THE 252ND DISTRICT COURT OF JEFFERSON COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction by the 252nd District Court of Jefferson County (Texas), for possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver, and his life sentence, which was assessed by the jury after finding two prior convictions.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted by a jury of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver. After finding two prior convictions, the jury assessed his punishment at confinement for life. The court affirmed the conviction. Appellant then filed a post-conviction writ of habeas corpus with the Court of Criminal Appeals, which granted him an out-of-time appeal. The court subsequently recalled the original mandate and issued an order allowing appellant sufficient time to review the record and file a pro se brief. Defendant complained in two points of error of the use of one of the prior convictions and the introduction of the "pen packets" before the jury because the conviction was void and the judgment was neither definite nor certain as to the punishment assessed. The court overruled both points of error. The court found that each of the prior convictions showed the verdict was a certain number of years and the judgment applied the indeterminate sentence law by assessing the minimum punishment as that minimum required by law and by assessing the maximum as that set by the verdict. This was correct and proper under the then existing statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in the conviction of appellant of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver and sentence for life. The court held that each of the prior convictions showed the verdict was a certain number of years and the judgment applied the indeterminate sentence law by assessing the minimum punishment as that minimum required by law and the maximum as that set by the verdict.

 

1081 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Hartford Steam Boiler Inspection & Ins. Co. v. State


No. 3-86-131-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


729 S.W.2d 372; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7445



April 29, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 98TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, NO. 392,713, HONORABLE HARLEY CLARK, JUDGE PRESIDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant company sought review of the decision of the District Court of Travis County, 98th Judicial District (Texas), which rejected its plea for pre-judgment "interest" on excess gross premiums taxes paid to appellee state, pursuant to Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 4.10. Appellant contended that it was entitled to the interest as part of its claim for compensatory damages occasioned by appellee's wrongful collection of excessive taxes.


OVERVIEW: Appellant company was awarded recovery for the excess gross premiums tax that it paid to appellee state involuntarily under Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 4.10. The court reversed that part of the judgment that rejected appellant's plea for pre-judgment "interest" on the excess taxes and remanded the matter to the trial court to calculate the pre-judgment interest. The legislature consented to the suit by a resolution, but it did not expressly provide for a waiver of immunity as to prejudgment interest. The court found that the "interest" that appellant sought was not like conventional interest, or interest eo nomine, but was more like interest as damages. The court found that appellant's claim was liquidated and a kind in which pre-judgment interest had always been recoverable. It recognized that the word "interest" was a misnomer when used to refer to interest as damages. Although appellee, as a state, was not normally liable for interest in the absence of a statute or express contract providing for prejudgment interest, that rule only applied to conventional interest, and none of the possible exceptions applied that would have exempted appellee from liability.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded only that part of the judgment that had rejected appellant company's plea for pre-judgment "interest" on excess taxes that it paid to appellee state. The court found that appellant was entitled to the interest because it was not conventional interest, for which appellee was immune from collection, but was more like liquidated damages and, therefore, recoverable.

 

1082 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Gay v. State


No. 07-86-0150-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Seventh District, Amarillo


730 S.W.2d 154; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7126



April 28, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled May 26, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF DONLEY COUNTY; 100TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT; NO. 4214-A; HONORABLE JOHN T. FORBIS, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant beneficiaries sought review of the decision of the District Court of Donley County, 100th Judicial District (Texas), which granted summary judgment for appellees, the state of Texas and the highway department. Appellants asserted that appellees violated their constitutional or civil rights under 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1983, 1985, 1985, 1986, 1988 when they negligently constructed a highway on which decedent was killed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found appellant beneficiaries were permitted to take nothing against appellees, the state of Texas and the highway department, upon any claim predicated upon an alleged constitutional tort or a violation of appellants' constitutional or civil rights under 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1983, 1985, 1986, 1988. The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of appellees. The court found that the general rule of sovereign immunity of appellee state applied even as related to damage suits directly against it for torts. The court did not consider appellee state to have waived its immunity by virtue of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983's definition of a "person." The court found that because appellee highway department was a branch of appellee state, it was also not a person and shared appellee state's governmental immunity. The court found that summary judgment was proper, even though it was partially based upon the pleadings, because the pleadings showed that appellants' suit was against appellee state and appellee highway department and a suit against appellee highway department was a suit against appellee state.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment for appellees, the state of Texas and the highway department, and found that appellant beneficiaries could take nothing against appellees upon any claim predicated upon an alleged constitutional tort or a violation of constitutional or civil rights. The court found that appellees had sovereign immunity in what was essentially a negligence action.

 

1083 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Protz v. State


No. A14-86-388-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7086



April 23, 1987, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 248th District Court of Harris County, Cause No. 444,012.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the 248th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of theft of property, enhanced by a prior conviction. The trial court assessed punishment at 20 years confinement.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted by the trial jury for theft of property, enhanced by a prior conviction, and the trial court assessed punishment at 20 years confinement. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 28.10(b) (Supp. 1987) did not preclude the trial court from allowing amendment of the indictment because the statute applied only after the trial on the merits commenced and the amending occurred before jury selection. The court held that the word "automobile" in appellant's indictment included the word "truck" and therefore was a change of form rather than substance. The court held that appellant's substantial rights were not prejudiced by changing "automobile" to "truck" in the indictment. The court held that art. 28.10 did not violate U.S. Const. amend. V by allowing the court and prosecutor to usurp the function of the grand jury in defining offenses because federal due process did not require the states to observe the Fifth Amendment's provision for presentment or indictment by the grand jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which convicted appellant of theft of property and assessed punishment at 20 years confinement because the trial court allowed the indictment to be amended before jury selection, the change of the words "automobile" to "truck" in the indictment was a change of form and not substance, and the relevant statute that allowed indictment amendments was not unconstitutional.

 

1084 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Shaw v. State


Nos. 2-86-036-CR, 2-86-073-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


729 S.W.2d 134; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7292



April 23, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] This Case Reversed and Remanded April 27, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT NO. 2 OF TARRANT COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the Criminal District Court No. 2 of Tarrant County (Texas), which convicted him of murder, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.02 (1974) and attempted murder, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 15.01 (1987).


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted appellant of murder, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.02 (1974) and attempted murder, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 15.01 (1987). The conviction resulted from an incident in which appellant shot through the plate glass windows at a karate studio which he had attended with an Uzi semi-automatic rifle. Appellant challenged his convictions. On appeal the court affirmed the trial court. The court first held that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(a), which provided for jury instructions on sentencing that took into account the possibility of parole, was not an unconstitutional violation of the separation of powers between the legislative and judicial branches because Tex. Const. art. V, § 31 allowed the legislature to delegate rulemaking authority to the courts. The court also held that art. 37.07, § 4 did not aggravate a crime, did not make it greater than when it was committed, and did not inflict greater punishment than that proscribed when the offense was committed, so that it was not an ex post facto law. Finally, appellant waived any error from a prosecutorial comment that appellant would "do it again," by not requesting the jury to disregard.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction because appellant waived any error from a prosecutorial comment that appellant would "do it again," by not requesting the jury to disregard, and a statute that provided for jury instructions on sentencing that took into account the possibility of parole was neither in violation of separation of powers nor ex post facto.

 

1085 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Proctor v. State


No. 05-86-00204-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


748 S.W.2d 1; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 9278



April 20, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of a District Court of Dallas County (Texas), which convicted appellant of murder and sentenced appellant to life imprisonment and a fine of $ 10,000.00.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of murder, sentenced to life imprisonment, and fined $ 10,000.00. Appellant challenged his conviction, contending that the trial court erred during a hearing on the admissibility of appellant's written statement by admitting evidence of appellant's oral statements made during his custodial interrogation. The court affirmed, holding that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 3822, § 3(a) (1986) only precluded oral statements given in response to custodial interrogation that tended to elicit an incriminating response. The court found that the questions asked by the officer, as to whether appellant understood the Miranda warnings administered, whether appellant could read or write, and whether the written statement was correct, were not reasonably likely to elicit an incriminating response. The court also held that the jury instructions given by the trial court and mandated by Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(b) were not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, which convicted appellant of murder, because the trial court properly admitted an officer's testimony as to the voluntary conditions surrounding the statement given by appellant in response to custodial interrogation, because the questions were not reasonably likely to elicit an incriminating response, nor were the jury instructions as to parole unconstitutional.

 

1086 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Moone v. State


No. C14-86-528-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


728 S.W.2d 928; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7036



April 16, 1987, Decided  
April 16, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 6 of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court No. 890,861.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a guilty verdict entered in the County Criminal Court at Law No. 6 of Harris County, Texas which convicted him of driving while intoxicated. Appellant contended that the chain of custody as to the blood sample was not adequately proven by the state and he was denied a speedy trial.


OVERVIEW: After a fatal two vehicle collision, appellant consented to giving a blood specimen. Appellant argued that the trial court erred in admitting evidence of the blood alcohol specimen because the chain of custody was not properly established. On appeal, the court held that testimonial evidence of each officer and lab technician that had control of the bottle showed that no misplacement or tampering occurred to the sample, and that the chain of custody was sufficiently proven. The court further held that the introduction of a blood alcohol percentage into the statutory definition of the level of intoxication necessary for a finding of intoxication was not unconstitutional and did not create an impermissible encroachment into the province of the jury. The percentage was found to merely be another definition of intoxication. Finally, in affirming the judgment of the trial court, the court found that appellant was not denied the right to a speedy trial because continuances at the request or consent of defendant were excluded from the computation of time by which the state must be ready for trial.


OUTCOME: Conviction for driving while intoxicated was affirmed because the chain of custody of the blood sample was without break and adequately established by the state. The court further held that appellant was not denied a speedy trial because he caused delays which stopped the running of the speedy trial time due to his own actions.

 

1087 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Perez v. State


No. A14-86-607-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7038



April 16, 1987, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 208th District Court of Harris County Cause No. 437,663.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction for aggravated sexual assault on a child in the 208th District Court, Harris County, Texas. Defendant asserted that he was entitled to a jury charge on alibi and that the parole instruction warranted reversal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was tried and convicted of aggravated sexual assault on a child. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in refusing his request for a jury instruction on alibi because he had no access to the child on the date the offense occurred, as alleged in the indictment. However, the evidence at trial showed that the date alleged was incorrect; the offense occurred earlier. In overruling that point of error, the court found that the state was not bound by the date alleged, as long as the evidence showed that the event occurred prior to the indictment and within the statute of limitations. Defendant also objected to the jury instruction given regarding the parole laws and good time. The court found, in affirming the conviction, that the instruction did not violate the due process rights of defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of defendant for aggravated assault on a child. The court held that the prosecution was not bound by the date of the offense alleged in the indictment. Thus, defendant was not entitled to a jury instruction on alibi. Further, a jury charge regarding parole and good time did not warrant reversal.

 

1088 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Del Rio v. Jinkins


No. 13-86-400-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


730 S.W.2d 125; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7058



April 16, 1987, Decided  
April 16, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing May 14, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 138th District Court of Cameron County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought review of the summary judgment granted by the 138th District Court, Cameron County, Texas, on his suit for medical negligence alleging appellees, doctor and medical group, negligently performed radiation treatment. Appellant contended that granting summary judgment was improper where there was a material issue of fact as to whether the patient had a reasonable opportunity to discover injuries.


OVERVIEW: Appellant patient received radiation treatment that resulted in severe stomach problems. Appellant alleged that no subsequent doctor told him his difficulties could have resulted from his previous treatment. Under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590I, § 10.01 (1987), no health care liability claim could be commenced unless filed within two years of the occurrence of the tort. However, the court held that a material issue of fact existed as to whether appellant had a reasonable opportunity to discover that his injuries resulted from his prior radiation treatment. Appellant alleged that he was never informed of this information, while two doctors alleged that they personally informed him of that possibility. Therefore, the court found a genuine issue of material fact remained to be determined and that, if the trier of fact determined that appellant did not have a reasonable opportunity to discover the nature of his injury, the two-year limitation period was unconstitutional as applied to him. The court found that appellant's fraudulent concealment claim against appellees, doctor and medical group, who performed the radiation treatment could not be raised on appeal for the first time.


OUTCOME: Grant of motion for summary judgment in favor of appellees, doctor and medical group, was reversed and remanded because a genuine issue of material fact existed as to whether appellant patient had a reasonable opportunity to discover the cause of his injury. The court held that if there was no reasonable opportunity, then application of the statute of limitations against him would be unconstitutional.

 

1089 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Sepulveda v. State


No. 13-86-268-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


729 S.W.2d 954; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7060



April 16, 1987, Decided  
April 16, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the 319th District Court of Nueces County, Texas.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the 319th District Court of Nueces County, Texas, which convicted her of fraudulently applying for voter registration. Defendant contended that the statutes under which she was convicted, Tex. Elec. Code Ann. §§ 13.001-13.007 (1986), were unconstitutionally vague and indefinite.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of fraudulently applying for voter registration. On appeal, she challenged the statute under which she was convicted, Tex. Elec. Code Ann. §§ 13.001-13.007 (1986), as unconstitutionally vague. The court affirmed, holding that a person who engaged in conduct that was clearly proscribed could not complain of the vagueness of the law as applied to the conduct of others. The court found that where words of a criminal statute were not defined, courts would ordinarily give them their plain meaning. The court noted that the word "applied," as where one applied for voter registration, was certainly not vague, but had an ordinary, common-sense meaning. The court also found the statute did not proscribe the same type of conduct by punishment under one section as a felony and another as a misdemeanor, as appellant argued. One section governed people like appellant, who acted without any claim of agency status, while another governed people who attempted to act as an applicant's agent. The court also rejected defendant's claim that evidence of other extraneous offenses by her was error, holding that they were relevant to her motivation and conduct.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for fraudulently applying for voter registration was affirmed. Defendant's argument that the statute under which she was convicted was unconstitutionally vague was rejected, since the words of the statute had a plain meaning.

 

1090 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Public Utility Com. v. Austin


No. 3-86-019-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


728 S.W.2d 907; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7282



April 15, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing overruled May 13, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 353RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT, NO. 391,757, HONORABLE JOE B. DIBRELL, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, Texas Public Utility Commission and others, sought review of the judgment of the 353rd District Court, Travis County, Texas, which found in favor of appellee city, and declared as unconstitutional an attempted legislative delegation of authority to review municipally-owned utility rates under the Public Utilities Regulatory Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1446c (1987).


OVERVIEW: Appellee city proposed to increase the rates which its municipally owned utility charged nonresident ratepayers. Appellants, Texas Public Utility Commission and others, filed suit on the ground that appellee was exceeding its authority under the Public Utilities Regulation Act (PURA), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1446c (1987). The lower court held that PURA was unconstitutional on the ground that PURA § 26(c), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1446c, § 26(c) (1987), included no statutory criteria to guide appellant Public Utility Commission in exercising its review authority. That judgment was reversed and rendered. The court held that the statutory language, legislative history, and judicial interpretation of PURA showed that, under PURA § 26(c), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1446c, § 26(c) (1987), nonresident ratepayers of a municipally owned utility were authorized to contest before appellant Public Utility Commission any rate changes imposed. Further, the court found that the same authorities revealed the standards to govern such review were those set forth in PURA §§ 37-47, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1446c, §§ 37-47 (1987).


OUTCOME: The court reversed and rendered the trial court's judgment that the Public Utility Regulation Act (PURA) was unconstitutional because its language, history, and judicial interpretation showed that nonresident ratepayers of a municipally-owned utility were authorized to contest before appellant Public Utility Commission any rate changes imposed, and that the PURA prescribed the standards to govern such review.

 

1091 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Hupp v. State


Nos. 05-86-00531-CR, 05-86-00532-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


729 S.W.2d 355; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7386



April 15, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of a District Court, Dallas County (Texas), which convicted him of aggravated sexual assault of two children. The jury assessed punishment at life imprisonment in each case. Defendant contended that he had received ineffective assistance of counsel, which required a new trial, and that jury instructions as to the parole law were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault of two children and sentenced to life imprisonment for both convictions. Defendant appealed the judgment and claimed ineffective assistance of counsel and challenged the constitutionality of a statute requiring jury instructions as to parole law. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court was unable to find a reasonable probability that, absent the asserted errors, the jury would have had a reasonable doubt respecting guilt. The defense attorney's failure to request a pretrial hearing as to voluntariness could have been a tactical decision based on his perception that the statement was voluntary. Defendant's election to testify as well as the introduction by the defense of psychiatric testimony constituted a waiver of defendant's U.S. Const. amend. V privilege. The court held that the statute requiring jury instructions about parole law violated neither the separation of powers doctrine nor the due process clause, and thus was constitutional under the Texas and U.S. Constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of aggravated sexual assault and held that defendant's counsel rendered effective assistance. The court was unable to find a reasonable probability that, absent the asserted errors, the jury would have had a reasonable doubt respecting guilt. The statutorily required jury instructions regarding parole law and good conduct time were constitutional under the Texas Constitution and the U.S. Constitution.

Adams v. State


No. 01-86-00152-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6945



April 9, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 177th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 434,597.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for sexual assault from the 177th District Court, Harris County, Texas, and claimed that the evidence was insufficient to identify him, that the trial court erred when it failed to suppress the pre-trial identification, that a mistrial should have been granted because of the state's improper argument, and that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. art. 37.07(4) was unconstitutional and the instruction based on it was improper.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of sexual assault and assessed 15 years and one day confinement by a jury. The court affirmed defendant's conviction and found that the evidence, which established his identity, was sufficient for the jury to find that he was the perpetrator beyond a reasonable doubt. The court ruled that the pre-trial photo identification of the defendant by the victim was not impermissibly suggestive and that its admission was not erroneous, nor was the line-up at which defendant's counsel was present and to which he did not object. The court found that denial of a mistrial was proper because, even if the state's prosecutor had made improper argument, the trial court's instructions cured the error and no prejudice resulted. The court held that defendant's constitutional challenge to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Code art. 37.07(4) and the accompanying instruction on parole eligibility had been waived because he did not raise them before the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction because his identity was proven, and that the pre-trial identification was not impermissibly suggestive. The court held that even if the state's argument was improper, the trial judge's instructions cured any prejudice and a mistrial was not warranted. The court held that defendant's failure to raise the issue of parole eligibility statute's unconstitutionality at trial resulted in waiver of the issue.

Shaw v. State


No. 01-86-00479-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


728 S.W.2d 889; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6954



April 9, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from 180th the District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 437883.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the 180th District Court of Harris County, Texas, which convicted him of involuntary manslaughter.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found guilty of involuntary manslaughter and sought review of the judgment. The court affirmed appellant's conviction and held that the indictment was not defective. The court found that the testimony at trial was sufficient to satisfy the statutory predicate for the introduction of autopsy reports. The court refused to consider appellant's argument that the parole charge given pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.04(4) (1987) was unconstitutional because he failed to raise the issue in the trial court and therefore failed to preserve any error for review. The court also found that the parole law instructions were not fundamentally misleading. The court held that the trial court did not err by failing to instruct the jury that they could consider the fact that a videotape made of appellant shortly after his arrest was destroyed in assessing the credibility of the state's witness on the issue of intoxication. The court refused to consider appellant's argument that the trial court erred in permitting a police officer to testify concerning appellant's behavior while being videotaped because appellant's objection did not comport with his objection at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for involuntary manslaughter because the trial court did not err in allowing testimony from an autopsy report or in failing to instruct the jury that they could consider the destruction of a videotape made of appellant in assessing the credibility of a particular state witness.

Sanders v. State


No. 01-81-0276-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6958



April 9, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at law No. 7 of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 595,217


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his bench trial conviction for promoting obscene material. The Court of Criminal Appeals (Texas), vacated the appellate court's reversal of appellant's conviction and remanded the case to the court for reconsideration in light of recent rulings regarding the use of a presumption in Tex. Penal Code § 43.23(e), which had been declared unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of his conviction in a bench trial for promoting obscene material, where his punishment was assessed at a fine, probated for one year. Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1) (Supp. 1982). The court reversed appellant's conviction on constitutional grounds, but the higher court vacated the reversal and remanded the case back to the court for reconsideration. Specifically, the higher court directed the court to reconsider its ruling in light of the higher court's recent holding that the existence of the unconstitutional presumption in § 43.23 as part of the law at the time of a non-jury trial would not constitute reversible error unless some matter of record indicated that the trial court had relied on the presumption alone in its judgment. In light of the higher court's decision, the court affirmed the trial court's conviction of appellant, reasoning that there was nothing in the record to indicate that the trial judge had relied solely on the presumption and the record contained sufficient evidence to support the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting appellant of promoting obscene material because it could not assume that that the trial court based appellant's conviction on an unconstitutional presumption in the anti-obscenity statute. Viewing the evidence in the light most favorable to the trial court's judgment, the court assumed that the trial court either disregarded the presumption, or that any consideration of it was harmless.

Henry v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston

April 9, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 228th District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 439,447


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant criminal defendant challenged a judgment of the 228th District Court of Harris County, Texas, which convicted him of aggravated robbery.


OVERVIEW: Appellant criminal defendant, who was convicted of aggravated robbery, challenged the trial court's jury instruction on the parole law and contended that the statute authorizing such an instruction, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 (1987), was unconstitutional. Appellant contended that decisions with respect to parole were exclusively within the province of the executive branch. The court also concluded that art. 37.07, § 4 was not unconstitutionally vague because the statute had a beneficially clarifying effect.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant criminal defendant's conviction for aggravated robbery. The court held that the statute authorizing instructions on the parole law did not violate the separation of powers doctrine and was not unconstitutionally vague.

Tarrant County Hospital Dist. v. Hughes


No. 2-86-231-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


734 S.W.2d 675; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8221



April 9, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 12, 1987.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator hospital sought the issuance of a writ of mandamus to compel respondent judge to rescind an order of the 48th District Court of Tarrant County (Texas), which compelled relator as defendant to produce and make available to plaintiff in the underlying action certain documents identifying blood donors.


OVERVIEW: Relator hospital was the defendant in an underlying wrongful death action in which plaintiff alleged that the deceased was given blood transfusions by relator which resulted in her contracting Acquired Immune Deficiency Syndrome. Relator, as defendant in the underlying action, sought a protective order in response to plaintiff's request for documents identifying blood donors. Respondent judge denied relator's request and entered an order compelling production and prohibiting contact of donors without further order of the court. The court held that respondent's order did not violate the physician-patient privilege of Tex. R. Evid. 509 because the privilege was not applicable as the record did not reflect that donors were seen by a physician or received medical care when they donated blood. The court found that respondent's order did not violate the donors' constitutional right to privacy. The court reasoned that, balancing the competing interests, the interest served by the order outweighed the donors' interest in privacy. The court also held that relator failed to establish that the ordered discovery was an abuse of discretion because of injury to any societal interest.


OUTCOME: The court denied relator hospital's request for issuance of an order compelling respondent judge to rescind his order compelling respondent's production of documents in an underlying wrongful death action because physician-patient privilege was not applicable and order did not violate donors' rights to privacy.

Adams v. State


No. 01-86-00183-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6872



April 2, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 179th District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial COurt Cause No. 428,650.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the 179th District Court, Harris County (Texas), convicting him of aggravated perjury under Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 37.02-37.04 (1974) for giving false testimony before a grand jury.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated perjury under Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 37.02- 37.04 (1974) for making false statements to a grand jury investigating a child's death. Appellant sought review, and the court affirmed, finding that appellant was bound by his counsel's waiver of his right to a speedy trial. The court found that whether a statement was material in a given fact situation was a question of law under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 37.04(c), and that the trial court properly decided that question.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for aggravated perjury because evidence was sufficient to prove that false testimony to grand jury was material.

Atomanczky v. State


No. 01-86-0546-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6877



April 2, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 185th District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 374,591.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the 185th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted appellant of murder after a jury trial and assessed his punishment at confinement for life and a fine of $ 10,000.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of murder and sentenced to confinement for life. The court affirmed appellant's conviction, rejecting several points of error on appeal. Appellant contended that it was fundamental error to instruct the jury about parole eligibility as required by Tex. Code. Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 (1987), because the statute was unconstitutional. The court held that appellant's failure to object at trial waived review of the constitutionality of the statute, and furthermore, that the statute had been held to be constitutional. There was no evidence to support a finding that appellant was incompetent to stand trial. The trial court did not err in refusing to instruct the jury regarding the insanity defense, because the trial testimony did not raise the defense. The trial court did not err in refusing to grant appellant's motion for a court-appointed investigator, because defense counsel did not make a request for a specific amount of funds or indicate a specific reason for them. There was no showing that appellant was denied funds for expenses incurred, or that appellant was harmed by the denial of funds necessary for the proper investigation of the case.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction was affirmed. It was not a constitutional violation to instruct the jury on eligibility for parole. The trial court did not err in refusing the insanity defense, because the testimony at trial did not raise the defense. There was no error in the trial court's denial of defense counsel's general request for funds for investigatory purposes, nor a showing that appellant had been harmed by the denial of funds.

Houston v. Cascades, Inc.


No. A14-87-022-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


730 S.W.2d 59; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6909



April 2, 1987, Decided  
April 2, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 295th Judicial District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Cause No. 86-56205


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, city and chief of police, challenged a temporary injunction ordered by the 295th Judicial District Court of Harris County, Texas, which enjoined appellants from enforcing a city ordinance which regulated sexually oriented businesses as it applied to permits for business enterprises.


OVERVIEW: An ordinance was passed by a city council requiring owners of sexually oriented businesses to obtain a permit to continue operations. The ordinance also prohibited such a business if it were located within 750 feet of a school or licensed day care. Appellee corporation owned such a business within the prohibited area. Appellee petitioned the trial court for an injunction to enjoin appellants, city and chief of police, from enforcing the ordinance. The trial court issued a temporary injunction, and appellant's challenged. The court held that the trial court, as a court of equity, did not have jurisdiction to enjoin the enforcement of a penal ordinance unless the ordinance was unconstitutional and the enforcement caused irreparable injury to vested property rights. Because appellee never claimed, nor did the trial court find, that the ordinance was unconstitutional, the trial court was without jurisdiction to issue the injunction. Additionally, appellee failed to demonstrate an irreparable injury. Accordingly, the judgment was reversed and the injunction was dissolved.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and dissolved the temporary injunction enjoining appellants, city and chief of police, from enforcing a city ordinance which regulated sexually oriented businesses because the trial court was without jurisdiction to issue the injunction.

Richardson v. State


No. A14-85-751-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


728 S.W.2d 128; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6913



April 2, 1987, Decided  
April 2, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Discretionary Review Granted July 8, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 209th District Court of Harris County Cause No. 417,924.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the 209th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of aggravated robbery after he was certified to be tried as an adult on this charge by another district court.


OVERVIEW: State alleged defendant committed four acts of delinquent conduct and sought waiver of jurisdiction and transfer to a criminal district court for trial as an adult. The trial court waived jurisdiction for three offenses and retained one. Defendant was convicted of aggravated robbery as an adult. On appeal the court affirmed. The court held that on a motion to waive jurisdiction for multiple offenses, Tex. Fam. Code § 54.02(g) required the child's status be fixed as a juvenile for all offenses once the juvenile court retained and exercised jurisdiction over any count in the certification petition, and the trial court's subsequent exercise of jurisdiction over retained offenses would have rendered invalid the order waiving jurisdiction. The court found no reversible error because there was no evidence that the trial court exercised jurisdiction over the one retained offense, the waiver of jurisdiction as to the other offenses was valid, and jurisdiction over defendant was acquired by the criminal district court. The court held the Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 (1987) parole instruction statute was constitutional, which resolved defendant's other points of error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of aggravated robbery as an adult because the trial court's waiver of jurisdiction as to aggravated robbery was not invalidated by retention of jurisdiction over one juvenile offense where the court never exercised the retained jurisdiction.

 

1102 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Dudley v. State


No. B14-86-746-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


730 S.W.2d 51; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6922



April 2, 1987, Decided  
April 2, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Probate Court No. 3 of Harris County, Cause No. 41,003.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment in the Probate Court No. 3 of Harris County (Texas), which ordered appellant committed for alcoholism.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the probate court's order committing appellant for alcoholism. The court held that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5561c-2 (act) did not violate Tex. Const. art. III, § 35 because its provisions related to the same general subject of alcohol and drug abuse services offered by the state. The act's failure to require competent medical or psychiatric testimony prior to commitment did not violate Tex. Const. art. I, § 15-a because that provision did not apply to persons committed as alcoholics. The act was not void for vagueness because it sufficiently defined alcoholism and the conditions under which an alcoholic could be committed such that a person of common intelligence would agree to the statute's meaning and application. The doctor's testimony was properly admitted because Tex. R. Evid. 509(d)(7) and 510(d)(4) provided exceptions to the doctor/patient privilege in involuntary commitment proceedings, and the probate court limited the doctor's testimony to information disclosed after appellant received a warning that the information was not confidential. Appellant's additional complaints were waived because they were not raised before the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the probate court, which committed appellant for alcoholism because the act under which he was committed was not unconstitutional and the doctor's testimony was not privileged.

 

1103 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Omura v. State


No. 05-86-00701-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


730 S.W.2d 766; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7558



March 28, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Dallas County, Texas, that adopted a magistrate's order denying appellant's motion for a writ of habeas corpus, which sought to avoid extradition to the state of Utah. Appellant contended that the trial court erred, under the Magistrates Act, Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 54.301 et seq., by not reviewing the magistrate's findings, where no findings or conclusions had been made.


OVERVIEW: Appellant filed a motion for a writ of habeas corpus, seeking to avoid extradition to the state of Utah. The writ was denied and he appealed. The court held that the Magistrates Act (Act), Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 54.301 et seq. (1986), was not properly complied with. The court held that the record affirmatively showed that the district judge did not review the actions taken by the magistrate and there were no findings, no conclusions, no orders, and no recommendations made by the magistrate, from which the district court could have reviewed the actions taken by the magistrate. There was no evidence heard by the magistrate, which was transcribed and available to the trial court before the magistrate's actions were adopted by it. Accordingly, the Act was improperly applied, and the matter was remanded for further proceedings..


OUTCOME: The court held that the Magistrate's Act was not properly complied with when the trial court adopted a magistrate's order denying appellant's motion for a writ of habeas corpus, which sought to avoid extradition to the state of Utah. The court held that the trial court did not review the actions taken by the magistrate and there were no recommendations made by the magistrate. Thus, the ruling was improper.

Reese v. State


No. 01-86-0207-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6730



March 26, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 248th District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 435,501.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, found guilty of theft in the 248th District Court, Harris County (Texas), alleged that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 (Supp. 1987), was unconstitutional as vague and overbroad and violated U.S. amend. IV of the U.S. Constitution and that the trial court erred in overruling her objection to improper prosecutorial jury argument and committed reversible error when it admitted hearsay statements.


OVERVIEW: Appellant obtained money from the complainant by a pigeon drop scheme, and was convicted at trial for theft. On appeal, the court held that appellant had not preserved error because she did not make the same objection at trial as she asserted on appeal. Further, the prosecutor's argument was a plea for law enforcement, but even if error, appellant waived her objection when she failed to obtain a ruling from the court. The appellate court found this evidence sufficient to show that the unknown third party was a co-conspirator in the conspiracy and that appellant was an active participant. The third party's statements to the complainant were offered into evidence to show the conspiracy and, as such, were admissible as an exception to the hearsay rule. Therefore, the judgment of the trial court was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for theft was affirmed where she had waived her errors on appeal and her co-conspirator's comments were admissible to show conspiracy.

 

1105 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Faulkner v. State


No. 01-85-00557-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


727 S.W.2d 793; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6731



March 26, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 230th District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 411,009.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the 230th District Court of Harris County (Texas). The trial court convicted appellant of attempted capital murder and sentenced appellant to 20 years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: An officer heard gunshots and shortly thereafter observed appellant's truck make a quick U-turn and begin speeding. The officer heard on a radio broadcast that another officer had found the victim of the shooting. The officer pulled the truck over and heard a description of the perpetrators on a second broadcast that matched the occupants of the truck. Appellant gave both oral and videotaped confessions. Appellant was convicted of attempted capital murder. The court affirmed. The officer had a sufficient basis to stop the truck before he heard the radio broadcast. The officer heard gunshots and observed appellant's truck make a fast U-turn in a deserted area; moreover, the officer observed appellant speeding before he pulled the vehicle over. The trial court, as the sole judge of credibility of the witnesses, was entitled to disbelieve appellant's testimony that the officers threatened to beat him if he did not speak. The prosecutor had not commented on appellant's failure to testify during the punishment phase when the prosecutor indicated that appellant had not said that he was sorry; the prosecutor had been referring to appellant's testimony during the guilt phase of the trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction and sentence for attempted capital murder. The record supported the finding that appellant's confession was voluntary. Comments by the prosecutor that appellant was unrepentent did not violate appellant's right not to testify; the comments were references to appellant's testimony during the guilt phase of the trial, not to appellant's failure to testify during the punishment phase.

 

1106 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


McKethan v. McKethan


No. 01-86-00534-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


728 S.W.2d 856; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6735



March 26, 1987, Decided  
March 26, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 272nd District Court of Brazos County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 26,564.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, parents of deceased employee, sought review of a judgment from the 272nd District Court of Brazos County, Texas, that granted appellee employer's motion for summary judgment and found that Tex. Const. art. XVI, § 26 and the Workers' Compensation Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 8306, § 5 precluded recovery of exemplary damages, in their action for their son's death while at work, based on appellee's gross negligence.


OVERVIEW: Decedent was killed when a truck that he was performing maintenance on for appellee employer was driven over him. Appellee paid death benefits to appellants, parents of deceased employee, pursuant to the Workers' Compensation Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 8306, § 8 (1987). Appellants brought suit against appellee for gross negligence that proximately caused the death of their son. Appellee filed a motion for summary judgment, asserting that Tex. Const. art. XVI, § 26 and Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 8306, § 5 precluded recovery of the exemplary damages sought by appellants. The trial court granted the motion and entered a take-nothing judgment against appellants. The appeals court affirmed, holding that appellants, as parents of the decedent, were not permitted by the constitution to recover exemplary damages under the statute from appellee. The trial court did not err in entering summary judgment. A decedent's parents were not "begotten by him" and were not included in the class constitutionally permitted to recover exemplary damages for his death absent a survival action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment of the trial court that granted appellee employer's motion for summary judgment and found that the state constitution and statutory provisions of the Workers' Compensation Act precluded recovery of exemplary damages by appellants, parents of deceased employee, holding that the take-nothing judgment was proper.

 

1107 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. State


No. 01-85-00952-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


727 S.W.2d 344; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6741



March 26, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 228th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 428,478.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal appellant sought review of his conviction from the 228th District Court, Harris County, (Texas) of aggravated robbery, enhanced by two prior felony convictions.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated robbery. On appeal, the conviction was affirmed. The court held that appellant failed to state in what specific respect appellant regarded the jury charge defective. Even if error was committed, eyewitness testimony that established appellant's role as the person who used the pistol and held it to the back of the victim's head, and as the one who took the money was sufficient to sustain appellant's conviction as a primary actor. Also, the evidence supported the argument that appellant actually took the money. Although appellant objected to the "procedure" involved in line-ups, appellant did not object specifically to the officer's testimony regarding his filing of charges against appellant, therefore that point of error was waived. In addition, the requirement that specific language in jury charges be set forth did not usurp the judicial function or violate separation of powers. The judiciary remained free to interpret the law and determine guilt or innocence. Finally, appellant did not preserve for review the error in charging the jury on parole pursuant to Tex. Const. art. 37.07, § 4(a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of aggravated robbery, holding the eyewitness testimony that established appellant's role both as the person who used the pistol and held it to the back of the victim's head and as the one who took the money, was sufficient alone to sustain appellant's conviction as a primary actor. The court ruled that appellant's claim that legislative amendments violated Tex. Const. was not preserved for review.

Ganassi v. Fort Bend Cty. Appraisal Dist.


No. 01-86-00605-CV.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6792



March 26, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 268th Judicial Court of Fort Bend County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 52,334.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer filed an appeal from the decision of the 268th Judicial Court, Fort Bend County (Texas), which entered an order dismissing the appeal of a property valuation protest for want of jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxpayer filed an appeal from the decision of the trial court, which entered an order dismissing the appeal of a property valuation protest for want of jurisdiction. Appellee appraisal district's motion to dismiss for want of jurisdiction was granted on the basis that appellant failed to address his notice of appeal to the review board. Appellant asserted that appellee and the review board were the same entities and were not separate and distinct bodies. The court affirmed, holding that the review board was the "body" that entered the order that appellant wanted to appeal. Appellant, however, gave notice to appellee rather than the review board, as required under Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 42.06(b) (Supp. 1987). Although the review board was appointed by appellee, appellee and the review board were separate and distinct bodies pursuant to Tex. Tax Code Ann. §§ 6.01, 6.03 (1987), therefore, appellant did not give proper notice of appeal. The failure to serve the proper body with notice of appeal was jurisdictional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which dismissed the appeal of a property valuation protest for want of jurisdiction because appellant taxpayer gave notice of appeal to the wrong entity.

Thompson v. State


No. 01-86-00569-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


727 S.W.2d 351; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6795



March 26, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 228th District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 453,279.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed an appeal from the 228th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted appellant of credit card abuse, found the enhancement allegations to be true, and assessed punishment at 90 years of confinement.


OVERVIEW: After finding appellant guilty of credit card abuse, a jury found the enhancement allegations to be true and assessed punishment at 90 years confinement. Appellant filed an appeal, arguing that Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 (1986), the parole charge, was unconstitutional because it violated the "separation of powers" doctrine embodied in Tex. Const. art. 2, § 1. The record revealed that appellant made no objection at trial to the constitutionality of the parole charge. The court affirmed, holding that the constitutionality of a statute might not be raised on appeal unless the issue was first raised in the trial court. Further, the court had previously held that the parole charge did not violate the separation of powers doctrine. The court also held that the evidence was sufficient to support the jury's finding that appellant used the card knowing that it was not actually issued to him, in his own name, because he sought to obtain and to convert the name and background information of another living individual to his own use in his attempt to obtain funds on credit, and that he knew that he was not using the card with the effective consent of the cardholder.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that convicted appellant of credit card abuse because appellant made no objection at trial to the constitutionality of the parole charge, because he actively and knowingly sought to use another's name and background information to obtain funds on credit, and because he knew that he was not using the card with the effective consent of the cardholder.

Orn v. State


No. 3-86-198-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


727 S.W.2d 764; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7113



March 25, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled April 22, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE COUNTY COURT OF CALDWELL COUNTY, NO. 17,100, HONORABLE E. P. SLATER, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the County Court of Caldwell County (Texas) which found him guilty of driving while intoxicated and punishment was assessed at 180 days in jail and a fine.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged by complaint and information with the offense of driving while intoxicated. Appellant was found guilty by the trial court and was assessed punishment at 180 days in jail and a fine. Pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 44.02 (1979), appellant challenged the decision on the sole point that the trial court erred in overruling his motion to dismiss the information on the basis he had been denied his rights under the Speedy Trial Act. Appellant contended that because more than 90 days had elapsed between his arrest and the filing of the information, he was denied a speedy trial on his misdemeanor charge. The state argued that the delay was justified due to extensive investigation generally required in cases to uncover and gather the evidence necessary to prove prior offenses. The court held that while misdemeanor and felony acts of driving while intoxicated were separate offenses with different elements for purposes of charge and proof of guilt, they were committed and arose out of the same transaction, so that one arrest commenced the time for each for purposes of a speedy trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court which found appellant guilty of driving while intoxicated, and remanded with instructions to dismiss the information. The court held that appellant was denied his right to a speedy trial when more than 90 days elapsed between his arrest and the filing of the information.

Deloney v. State


No. 05-86-00300-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


734 S.W.2d 6; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8051



March 24, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From a District Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal appellant challenged the ruling of the District Court of Dallas County (Texas) which convicted him of aggravated robbery, a felony, and assessed punishment at 36 years of confinement.


OVERVIEW: Criminal appellant sought relief from his conviction for aggravated robbery and punishment was assessed at 36 years. Appellant contended that the trial court erred in denying his motion to set aside the indictment under the Texas Speedy Trial Act. The record reflected that appellant was indicted on February 4, 1985. The state filed an announcement of ready for trial on February 20, 1985. Appellant was not arrested until December 17, 1985, far more than 120 days after the indictment was filed. The court held that the facts in the record supported the trial court's finding. The trial court found that the state had exercised due diligence in attempting to determine appellant's location. The trial court was the primary finder of fact on motions such as this one and its findings were not to be disturbed unless manifestly contrary to the evidence. Therefore, the court affirmed the ruling of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the ruling of the trial court which convicted appellant of aggravated robbery. On review, the court held that appellant's motion to set aside an indictment in the absence of compliance with the speedy trial statute was without merit.

Matthews v. State


No. C14-86-462-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6708



March 19, 1987, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 263rd District Court of Harris County, Cause No. 440,283.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction for aggravated robbery entered upon a jury verdict in the 263rd District Court, Harris County, Texas. The jury assessed punishment at 30 years confinement.


OVERVIEW: After a jury convicted defendant of aggravated robbery, defendant challenged the conviction. In affirming, the court held that the trial court did not err by including an instruction on the law of parole, as authorized by Tex. Code Crim. Proc. art. 37.07, because the statute was not unconstitutional for violating the constitutional separation of powers doctrine. Further, the court held that because there was no hard evidence that defendant would have been guilty of the lesser offense of aggravated assault, the trial court did not err in failing to charge the jury on that lesser-included offense. Additionally, defendant's motion for mistrial was properly denied because prosecution's jury argument was not so extreme or manifestly improper as to have constituted reversible error. The court also held that because defendant did not file a motion to suppress identification prior to trial or make such objection at trial, the trial court did not err by permitting state to bolster the complainant's in-court identification with testimony by complainant that he identified defendant at a line-up. Finally, state could have impeached a witness by proof of a prior prostitution conviction.


OUTCOME: The trial court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated robbery because there was no evidence that defendant would have been guilty of the lesser-included offense of aggravated assault, and thus, the trial court did not err in failing to instruct the jury on that lesser-included offense. Moreover, the trial court's instruction on the law of parole did not violate the doctrine of separation of powers.

 

1113 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Burns v. State


No. C14-86-123-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


728 S.W.2d 114; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6709



March 19, 1987, Decided  
March 19, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 232nd District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court No. 440,156.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the order of the 232nd District Court of Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of aggravated sexual assault. Defendant contended that there was no sufficient statutory definition of a critical term applicable to the statute under which he was charged, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.02, and that it was meaningless and unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault for a rape committed with a deadly weapon. The court affirmed his convictions, rejecting his argument that the term "criminal episode" was not defined and that its use in the aggravated sexual assault statute, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.02, was meaningless and unconstitutionally vague. The court held that where words were not defined in a statute, they were to be given their plain meaning. The term "criminal episode" included the time immediately before and after the assault. Thus, the criminal episode began when defendant restricted the victim and ended when she was released. Defendant argued that the criminal episode should be construed to be limited to the sexual act only, during which the victim could not see a knife. The court held that because the victim saw the knife immediately before and after the act, the evidence showed that the knife was exhibited during the criminal episode. Defendant's argument that jurisdiction was not proven failed because circumstantial evidence elicited from the witnesses' testimony was sufficient to show the crime occurred in the court's jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for sexual assault because, where no statutory definition of a term existed, the court gave the term its plain meaning. The term "criminal episode," as used in the statute under which defendant was charged, had sufficiently clear meaning to support the finding that he committed the act for which he was indicted.

Tollett v. State


No. 3-86-010-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


727 S.W.2d 714; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7116



March 18, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled April 15, 1987. Appellant's Motion for Rehearing on Petition for Discretionary Review Denied November 21, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF WILLIAMSON COUNTY, 26TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT NO. 85-275-K, HONORABLE WILLIAM S. LOTT, JUDGE PRESIDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the District Court of Williamson County, (Texas), which convicted appellant for aggravated sexual assault under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.021 (Supp. 1987), and assessed punishment at imprisonment for 99 years. Appellant contended that the district court erred by giving the instruction on the law of parole that influenced the jury in his sentencing.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pleaded guilty to the offense of aggravated sexual assault and received a sentence of 99 years. The victim of the sexual assault was his 10 year old son. In addition, appellant sexually violated both his son and eight-year-old daughter. Appellant complained that the district court erred by giving the instruction on the law of parole. On appeal, the court found that there was no evidence that the jury's consideration of the law of parole caused any juror to agree to a harsher punishment. The evidence at the new trial hearing established that the jury gave minimal consideration, at best, to assessing appellant's punishment at a lesser term of years. More important, the testimony also showed that the jury had unanimously agreed that punishment in this appeal should be set at either imprisonment for 90 years or imprisonment for life before any discussion of the parole law took place and before any effort was made to calculate the effect the choice of punishment might have on appellant's parole eligibility date, and that appellant's parole eligibility was considered only in choosing between the two "maximum" punishments.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. Appellant's conviction and 99 year prison sentence for the sexual assault of his three children were upheld, because there was no reversible error and no evidence that the jury's consideration of the law of parole caused any juror to agree to a harsher punishment.

Coit v. State


No. 3-86-151-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


728 S.W.2d 105; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7135



March 18, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled April 15, 1987. State's Motion for Rehearing on Petition for Discretionary Review Denied May 15, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE COUNTY COURT AT LAW NO. 2 OF TRAVIS COUNTY NO. 259-226, HONORABLE STEVE RUSSELL, JUDGE PRESIDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought relief by an appeal de novo from the County Court at Law No. 2 of Travis County (Texas), which found defendant guilty of failing to maintain financial responsibility in violation of the Safety Responsibility Law, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701h. Defendant alleged that the evidence was insufficient to support the conviction as prosecution proved only that defendant failed to furnish evidence of financial responsibility.


OVERVIEW: Defendant driver was operating a motor vehicle and failed to furnish evidence of financial responsibility when requested to do so by a law enforcement officer. On appeal from her conviction for failing to maintain financial responsibility in violation of the Safety Responsibility Law, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701h, the court held that defendant's failure to furnish evidence of financial responsibility gave rise to a presumption that no policy of motor vehicle liability insurance was in effect in violation of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701h, § 1C. Under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701h, § 1D, the burden was on defendant to raise the issue of the existence of an applicable liability insurance policy by coming forward with evidence supporting the defense. As defendant offered no evidence that an automobile liability insurance policy or certificate of self-insurance was in effect to insure against potential losses arising out of her operation of the vehicle at the time the offense was alleged to have occurred, the evidence was sufficient to support the judgment of conviction. Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701h, § 1C, was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: Defendant driver's conviction for failing to maintain financial responsibility in violation of the Safety Responsibility Law was affirmed, because her failure to furnish evidence of financial responsibility to the officer who stopped her vehicle constituted prima facie proof that she had no liability insurance policy. Because she failed to demonstrate financial responsibility at trial, the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction.

Miles v. State


No. 01-86-00766-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6584



March 12, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 174th District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 448,206.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the order of the 174th District Court of Harris County, Texas, which convicted defendant of murder and assessed punishment at life confinement and a $ 10,000 fine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder and sentenced to life confinement and a $ 10,000 fine. On appeal, defendant contended that the trial court erred by including instructions regarding parole in its punishment charge, pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 (1987), and denied a fair trial by prosecutorial arguments that were outside the record. The court rejected defendant's contentions, finding that defendant did not urge the unconstitutionality of the statute at trial and, therefore, he could not raise it for the first time on appeal. The court also held that an argument that was invited by and fairly made in response to the argument of opposing counsel was proper. The court noted that that a rational trier of fact could have found all the essential elements of murder beyond a reasonable doubt. Accordingly, the court affirmed the holding of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the lower court that convicted defendant of murder and assessed punishment at life confinement and a $ 10,000 fine. The court held that a rational trier of fact could have found all the essential elements of murder beyond a reasonable doubt.
