Odom v. State


Nos. B14-86-053-CR, C14-86-054-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6588



March 12, 1987, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 351st District Court of Harris County, Cause Nos. 421,562, 421,563.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the order of the 351st District Court of Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of aggravated kidnapping and aggravated sexual assault.


OVERVIEW: On appeal from his conviction for aggravated kidnapping and aggravated sexual assault, defendant asserted that the lower court's instruction to the jury concerning parole and good conduct time, given pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07 § 4(a), violated the state constitutional separation of powers doctrine and that the lower court erred in failing to allow defendant the right to examine the complainant's notes for cross-examination and impeachment purposes. The court held that the statute was constitutional because the required charge did not violate the separation of powers doctrine. The court found that it was not a judicial usurpation of executive power, but merely an instruction to the jury that it may have considered the existence of parole law and good conduct time without considering their effect on any punishment assessed. The court noted that the lower court erred when it denied defendant access to complainant's notes for purposes of cross-examination and impeachment. The court held, however, that defendant failed to preserve error for review so as to enable the court to determine whether error was harmful pursuant to Tex. P. App. P. 50(d).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the lower court that convicted defendant of aggravated kidnapping and aggravated sexual assault. The court held that the relevant criminal procedure statute, relating to parole and credit for good time, was constitutional.

 

1118 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Bobbitt v. State


No. 01-86-00549-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6625



March 12, 1987, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 185th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 434,970.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the 185th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which found defendant guilty of possession of cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to possession of cocaine of less than 28 grams. At the time of his arrest, defendant was charged with public intoxication and possession of cocaine. The public intoxication charge was filed in municipal court and was dismissed pursuant to the Speedy Trial Act (act), Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32A.02(1987). On appeal, defendant argued that because the public intoxication and the cocaine charge arose from the same transaction and the public intoxication complaint had been discharged, dismissal of the cocaine charge was required by Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 28.061. The court found that Article 28.061 was mandatory and provided that if a charge was dismissed pursuant to the act, then any other offense arising out of the same transaction should be dismissed as well. Therefore, the judgment of the district court was reversed, and the indictment was dismissed. Further prosecution for the offense was barred.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision that found defendant guilty of possession of cocaine was reversed. Defendant had been charged in the same transaction of public intoxication, which was dismissed because of untimely prosecution. Therefore, the relevant statute required that the charge of cocaine possession, which was part of the same transaction, be dismissed as well.

 

1119 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Sloan v. State


No. 01-86-00116-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


738 S.W.2d 290; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6635



March 12, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 177th District Court of Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 417,547.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant drug manufacturer challenged a conviction from the 177th District Court of Harris County, Texas, for possession of a controlled substance, methamphetamine, in violation of the Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15.


OVERVIEW: Appellant drug manufacturer was arrested several miles from the scene where police found methamphetamine. The court affirmed appellant's conviction for possession of a controlled substance. The evidence affirmatively linked appellant to the contraband because police saw appellant leaving the building where the contraband was found, officers smelled odors associated with methamphetamine production while appellant was in the building, and utility bills for the building had appellant's name on them. Phenyl-2-propanone was a controlled substance pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 1.02(4) and an immediate precursor under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 1.02(18), that was used to manufacture methamphetamine. The Controlled Substances Act (Act), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, was not unconstitutionally void for vagueness despite the fact that it failed to define or mention adulterants and dilutants or diluents. The Act was vested with a presumption of validity, and its terms were not so vague that men of common intelligence had to guess its meaning or that it allowed the possibility of arbitrary and discriminatory enforcement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant drug manufacturer's conviction for possession of a controlled substance because the facts and circumstances affirmatively linked appellant to the controlled substance in such a manner to sufficiently prove that he knew of the contraband as well as had control over it. Also, the Controlled Substances Act was not vague because it gave ample notice that possession of a controlled substance was forbidden.

Engelking v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


727 S.W.2d 694; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6639

March 12, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 177th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 417,548.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction by the 177th District Court of Harris County (Texas), in which a jury found him guilty of possession of a controlled substance, methamphetamine, weighing at least 400 grams including adulterants and dilutants and the trial court assessed punishment at 45 years confinement.


OVERVIEW: Officers, under a warrant, entered a building and found a large amount of methamphetamine. A jury found appellant guilty of possession of a controlled substance, methamphetamine, weighing at least 400 grams including adulterants and dilutants and he was sentenced to confinement. Appellant challenged the conviction and the court found that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.04, the statute under which appellant was charged, was valid and not unconstitutionally vague. The court also found that there was sufficient evidence for a rational factfinder to conclude appellant's acts met the elements of the crime charged. Finally, the court found that the trial court did not err by refusing appellant's requested jury charge because it would not have aided the jury in deciding issues of fact.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of drug charges because the relevant statute was not vague and there was evidence sufficient to enable the jury to conclude that appellant had the required intent and possessed the drugs required for a violation of the statute. 1121 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Ray v. State


No. 01-86-0519-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6647



March 12, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 337th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 446,565


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction by the 337th District Court of Harris County, (Texas), for delivery of cocaine. Appellant contended that the prosecutor's arguments were improper, that the prosecution violated an order regarding disclosure of discovery, and that the prosecution improperly bolstered its exhibit.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was arrested during a drug bust after an undercover narcotics officer purchased cocaine from appellant and two co-defendants. Appellant's conviction for delivery of cocaine was affirmed. Although a comment by the prosecutor was improper, it did not amount to attorney misconduct and was based on evidence in the record. Because the comment was not a personal attack on appellant's counsel, it was not so extreme or inflammatory that an instruction to disregard would not have cured it. The prosecution's violation of a pretrial discovery order, under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 39.14 (1986), was harmless error because photos of the house where the drugs were purchased did not affect the outcome of the trial where witnesses had already described the house. Use of a court reporter on re-cross examination to rebut a co-defendant's testimony that contradicted his earlier written statement was not bolstering of a prosecution's exhibit but proper impeachment of the co-defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for delivery of cocaine because a remark by the prosecution was not so extreme or inflammatory that an instruction to disregard would not have cured it, the prosecution's failure to comply with a discovery order constituted harmless error when it did not affect the outcome of the trial, and use of a court reporter's testimony was not bolstering but proper impeachment of a co-defendant.

 

1122 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Carter v. State


No. 2-86-043-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


727 S.W.2d 108; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7032



March 11, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled, April 15, 1987. Opinion on Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Filed October 21, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 297TH DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal appellant challenged his conviction for aggravated sexual assault in the 297th District Court of Tarrant County (Texas) and argued that the trial court committed reversible error by instructing the jury on parole law and in denying his motion to dismiss for failure to grant a speedy trial.


OVERVIEW: Criminal appellant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault and argued on appeal that the trial court erred by denying his motion to dismiss for failure to grant a speedy trial. The delay in bringing appellant to trial was due solely to the trial court's crowded docket and a previously scheduled lengthy capital murder trial. The court found that the State announced ready for trial within the statutory time period and held that a mere showing by appellant that he was present in the county jail, but was not physically brought into the courtroom, did not by itself sufficiently rebut the presumption that the State was ready for trial. Once the State timely established that appellant was within its jurisdiction and it was ready for trial, the Speedy Trial Act, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32A.01-.02, was not negated by the subsequent actions of the trial court in temporarily removing appellant to another jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment on the basis that the delay in bringing appellant to trial could not be charged against the prosecution.

Winton v. State


No. 6-85-110-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Sixth District, Texarkana


727 S.W.2d 687; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6575



March 10, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Vacated November 23, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 6th Judicial District Court of Lamar County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction by the 6th Judicial District Court of Lamar County (Texas) for aggravated sexual assault. Defendant contended that evidence of an extraneous offense was improperly introduced during the punishment phase of his trial. He also contended that the mandatory parole charge of Tex. Crim. Proc. Code § 37.07 (1987) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to aggravated sexual assault and requested a jury for the penalty phase of his trial. Defendant did not object to evidence of an extrinsic offense or to the mandatory jury charge pursuant to Tex. Crim. Proc. Code § 37.07 (1987) concerning parole. The court affirmed the judgment and held that defendant waived the issues because he failed to object to them at trial. The court also concluded that the extrinsic offense was admissible, because it was so close in time to the charged offense that it was part of the res gestae. In addition, the court stated that the constitutionality of the mandatory parole charge was already established.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated sexual assault. Defendant waived the issues raised in his appeal because he did not object to them at trial. In addition, evidence of an extrinsic offense was admissible as part of the res gestae of the instant offense. Finally, the mandatory jury charge regarding parole was constitutional.

Foy v. State


No. 10-86-037-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Tenth District, Waco


726 S.W.2d 263; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6571



March 5, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from 54th Judicial District Court McLennan County, Texas, Trial Court No. 85-456-C.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the 54th Judicial District Court of McLennan County (Texas), which convicted him of felony driving while intoxicated. Defendant was sentenced to five years in the Texas Department of Corrections and fined.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of felony driving while intoxicated and was sentenced to five years confinement and a fine. Defendant appealed, asserting five points of error. Responding to defendant's contention that the trial court erred in refusing to impanel a separate jury to determine defendant's competency to stand trial, the court found that there was no evidence of incompetence sufficient to require the trial court to impanel a separate jury to determine competency. The court also held that the trial court was not required sua sponte to hold a competency hearing during the trial because the issue of defendant's competence was raised pretrial. The court also rejected defendant's contention that the trial court erred in overruling his objection to the introduction of a videotape showing him being booked because he did not waive his right to have counsel present. The court held that defendant's rights were not violated because the video showed that he waived his right to counsel when he told the officer that he would not call his attorney until morning. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting appellant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant for felony driving while intoxicated. The court held that there was no evidence of incompetence sufficient to require the trial court to impanel a separate jury to determine competence, and that the trial court was not required sua sponte to hold a competency hearing during trial because the issue of defendant's competence was raised pretrial.

 

1125 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


In Interest of S.H.A.


No. 05-85-00692-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


728 S.W.2d 73; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 7197



February 27, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents sought review from a district court of Dallas County, Texas, which terminated their parental rights to their son in a cause of action brought by appellee Dallas County Welfare Unit of the Texas Department of Human Resources. The trial court held that appellants had engaged in conduct that endangered the child and that the termination of parental rights was in the child's best interest.


OVERVIEW: Appellee Dallas County Welfare Unit of the Texas Department of Human Resources initiated a cause of action against appellant parents to terminate appellants' parental rights to their son. The trial court held that appellants had engaged in conduct that endangered the child and that the termination of appellants' parental rights was in the child's best interest. Pursuant to Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 15.02 (Supp. 1986), the involuntary termination of parental rights was proper if the evidence proved that the parent knowingly placed the child in conditions which endangered the child or engaged in conduct which knowingly endangered the child and termination was in the best interest of the child. The court held that § 15.02, did not require physical abuse toward the child but required conduct which endangered the child. The court overruled Higgins v. Dallas County Child Welfare Unit, 544 S.W. 2d 745 (Tex. Civ. App. 1976), which held that physical abuse was required under § 15.02. The court determined that the evidence was both legally and factually sufficient to support the jury's findings. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which terminated appellant parents' parental rights to their son upon appellee's, Dallas County Welfare Unit of the Texas Department of Human Resources, recommendation. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to support the involuntary termination of appellants' rights because appellants endangered the child and such termination was in the best interest of the child.

SCYRUS v. STATE


No. 01-86-00646-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6493



February 26, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 263rd District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 448,605.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction for possession of a firearm by a felon and four-year sentence from the 263rd District Court of Harris County, Texas. Appellant argued fundamental trial error for including parole instructions pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07(4) (1987) in the jury charge, for including the instruction despite objection, and for not sustaining his objection to the prosecutor's improper jury argument.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for possession of a firearm by a felon and his four-year sentence. Appellant argued fundamental trial error for including parole instructions in the jury charge, for including the instruction despite objection, and for not sustaining his objection to the prosecutor's improper jury argument. The court found no fundamental trial error or constitutional violation of separation of powers by including parole instructions pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07(4) (1987) in the jury charge. The court concluded that the issue was not raised at trial, that the trial court must be given an opportunity to correct any error, that the instruction was not fundamental error, and that the case relied on by appellant had since been reversed on rehearing. The court found appellant made no legal argument in his objection to the instruction as his second point of error and also found that appellant failed to obtain an adverse ruling regarding the prosecutor's jury argument, reserving nothing for review on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for possession of a firearm by a felon and four-year sentence. The court found no constitutional violation of the separation of powers by including parole instructions in the jury charge because the issue may not be raised on appeal unless raised at trial, because the trial court must be given opportunity to correct any error, and because the case appellant relied on had been reversed on rehearing.

Ruiz v. State


No. B14-86-212CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


726 S.W.2d 587; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6448



February 19, 1987, Decided  
February 19, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Discretionary Review Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 180th District Court of Harris County, Trial Court No. 402,654.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the 180th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of aggravated robbery in a jury trial and sentenced him to eighteen years of confinement.


OVERVIEW: The complainant drove back to her apartment with her two children. At the door she appellant pointed a gun at her chest. Appellant told her to give him her money. One of the persons with appellant said, "let's just take the car," and they left. The complainant saw appellant clearly for five minutes in bright light. Appellant was later stopped driving the car and charged with aggravated robbery. Appellant challenged his subsequent conviction. On appeal the court affirmed, holding that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, which instructed the jury on the possibility of parole, but which prohibited them from considering how parole laws would affect appellant, was constitutional in terms of both separation of powers and vagueness. The court also found that appellant's representation complied with U.S. Const. amend VI. Appellant failed to show that he was prejudiced by any errors of counsel, as the evidence of his guilt was overwhelming. Failure to object to extraneous offenses was not error as they were admissible to show identity and failure to question the complainant was sound strategy due to her clear earlier identification.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction because a statute that instructed the jury on the possibility of parole, but which prohibited them from considering how the parole laws would affect appellant, was constitutional, appellant's counsel was effective as failure to question the complainant was sound strategy due to her clear earlier identification and objection to extraneous offenses would have been overruled.

MARINO v. STATE


No. 01-86-00269-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6474



February 19, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 232nd District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 417,877.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of conviction for theft, pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.03(a), (b)(1) (1987), entered by the 232nd District Court of Harris County (Texas), after a jury trial, because the evidence was allegedly insufficient to support the conviction, the indictment against defendant was facially defective, and the trial court allegedly committed various evidentiary and instructional errors.


OVERVIEW: Defendant purchased truck tires and tubes from a supplier, allegedly on behalf of his former employer. At the time of the sale, defendant represented that he was authorized to purchase the goods when he had actually been terminated. A jury found that defendant guilty of theft, pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.03(a), (b)(1) (1987), and that two enhancement paragraphs were true. Punishment was assessed by the jury at 25 years confinement. Defendant appealed the judgment and the court affirmed. The court held that the evidence supported the conclusion that the consent of the tire supplier was induced by defendant's deception. Thus, there was sufficient evidence to support his conviction. Moreover, defendant was not entitled to a jury instruction with regard to purportedly exculpatory statements, as they were not exculpatory. The court also found that defendant was not prejudiced by failure of the trial court to include a specific definition of deception. Finally, defendant's points of error with regard to his indictment and the trial court's jury instructions contained only conclusory statements and, therefore, presented no issues for review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction for theft because the evidence established that defendant deceived a tire supplier into believing that he was authorized to purchase the goods on behalf on another. The court also found that defendant was not prejudiced when the trial court declined to give his requested jury charges. The court further found that defendant failed to properly present his other points of error on appeal.

Townsend v. State


No. 01-86-0490-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


725 S.W.2d 463; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6387



February 12, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 177th District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 433,273.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment entered by the 177th District Court, Harris County, Texas, which convicted him of involuntary manslaughter committed when operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated and sentenced him to 10 years confinement, probated for 10 years. The judgment also required him to serve 120 days in confinement as a condition of probation pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, § 6b(c) (1987).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of involuntary manslaughter committed when operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated. As part of his probation, appellant was required to serve 120 days in confinement pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, § 6b(c) (1987). On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of conviction and rejected appellant's points of error pertaining to § 6b(c). The court determined that appellant failed to demonstrate that § 6b(c) was unconstitutional as it was applied to him because he had received the minimum term of confinement, 120 days, provided by the statute. Therefore, the fact that the statute did not provide minimum guidelines did not harm appellant. The court further found that the 120 day term was not an unconstitutionally disproportionate length of time for appellant to serve in light of the fact that his driving while intoxicated resulted in the loss of human life. Finally, the court rejected appellant's contention that § 6b(c) failed to provide adequate notice of the bill's content because Tex. Const. art. III, § 35(c) provided that a law could not be held void on the basis of an insufficient title.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted appellant of involuntary manslaughter committed when operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated. The statute that required appellant to serve 120 days confinement as part of his probation was not unconstitutional because the term was proportionate to the crime. Further, appellant failed to demonstrate harm because he was sentenced to the minimum term.

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6391

NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 351st District Court of Harris County, Trial Court No. 427,668.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment entered by the 351st District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of the offense of delivery of more than one-fourth ounce and less than four ounces of marijuana and assessed punishment at 12 years confinement.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted after a jury trial of delivery of more than one-fourth ounce and less than four ounces of marijuana and was sentenced to 12 years confinement. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction and rejected appellant's points of error. The court found that the trial court's use of the parole charge set forth in Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 (1986) was proper because the case that had found that statute to be unconstitutional had been withdrawn, and the statute was constitutional. The court further found that the record reflected that appellant did not object when the trial court excused a prospective juror on its own motion, and therefore the error alleged by appellant was not preserved for review. Finally, the court determined that the prosecutor's arguments to the jury were not intended to persuade the jury to consider the parole law in assessing appellant's punishment, but rather were a plea to the jury to assess a longer period of confinement than had been previously assessed because appellant had not been rehabilitated by an earlier confinement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentence entered by the trial court because the trial court did not err when it instructed the jury regarding the parole charge. Although a case had previously declared the charge unconstitutional, that case had been withdrawn. Further, appellant did not object when the trial court excused a prospective juror, and therefore the alleged error was not preserved for review.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction by the 339th District Court of Harris County, Texas, of aggravated robbery with punishment assessed at 30 years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated robbery. Defendant asserted that the trial court erred in admitting evidence of extraneous offenses at the punishment stage of the trial. The court held that it was not error for the trial court to allow the introduction of extraneous offenses to refute the defendant's statement that this was "totally out-of-character." Defendant argued that the lineup was suggestive and conducive to misidentification, but the court held that there was no evidence that the police were suggestive or that the identifications were tainted. As to the argument that the trial court erred in refusing defendant's instruction on identification, the court held that the charge was sufficient with the instruction that the jury find beyond a reasonable doubt that the defendant committed the offense. The court also held that the record did not show that the defendant made a trial objection to the instructions so the issue was not preserved for appeal. The court affirmed, reforming the language of the judgment to allow the parole board to determine whether defendant was required to repay the costs of the appeal to the county.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of aggravated robbery because defendant opened the door for the state to admit evidence of his extraneous offenses by testifying that the act was out-of-character.

In re Adjudication of Water Rights of Brazos III Segment of Brazos River Basin


No. 10-86-132-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Tenth District, Waco


726 S.W.2d 214; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6451



February 12, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from 82nd Judicial District Court, Falls County, Texas, Trial Court No. 28,913.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Texas Water Commission challenged the judgment of the 82nd Judicial District Court, Falls County, Texas, which modified appellant's adjudication of appellee landowners' water rights as they pertained to a river.


OVERVIEW: Appellee landowners filed exceptions to appellant Texas Water Commission's final determination filed with the trial court. The trial court modified appellant's determination by recognizing equitable water rights for appellees. The court affirmed and held that the trial court was authorized to use its constitutional equity powers as it did, and that the evidence sustained such action. The court found that trial courts had equitable power by virtue of Tex. Const. art. V, § 8 (amended 1891), and that such equitable power was available in a proper situation to recognize water rights in land owners adjacent to rivers whose grants were patented prior to January 20, 1840. All parties had stipulated that for each claim at issue, the original land grant was made prior to January 20, 1840. The court found that appellees had used the river for a long time, with no complaints, had spent large sums developing irrigation systems, and that property values would be greatly reduced if water rights were denied. Thus, the evidence sustained the modification. The court also held that there was no error in setting the priority date as the date of first beneficial use for each appellee.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's modification of appellant Texas Water Commission's final determination that recognized equitable water rights of appellee landowners, because the trial court had constitutional equity power to recognize water rights in land owners adjacent to rivers that had own their land prior to a set date, and because evidence sustained the action.

Texaco, Inc. v. Pennzoil Co.


No. 01-86-0216-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


729 S.W.2d 768; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6484



February 12, 1987, Decided  
February 12, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 151st District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 84-05905.



DISPOSITION:  The court issued an order to plaintiff oil company to file a punitive damages remittitur of two billion dollars. The judgment would then be reformed to show one billion dollars in punitive damages and would be affirmed as reformed. If plaintiff failed to file the remittitur, the judgment would be reversed and remanded. Punitive damages of three billion dollars constituted a confiscation assets rather than punishment for past action.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant oil company appealed a judgment from the 151st District Court of Harris County (Texas), which awarded compensatory and punitive damages to plaintiff oil company for defendant's tortious interference with a contract between plaintiff and a third oil company.


OVERVIEW: Defendant oil company brought 90 points of error in its appeal of a judgment entered against it for tortious interference with a contract. The court denied all but one point of error. The court held that the jury assessment of 3 billion dollars was excessive in that it went beyond the amount needed to punish and deter future conduct. Plaintiff oil company was directed to file a remittitur of 2 billion dollars. Failure to file the remittitur would lead to reversal and remand of the judgment. On the remaining points of error the court held that the evidence supported the jury finding that a binding agreement existed between plaintiff and a third oil company for the purchase of the third company. Defendant knew of the agreement prior to its own purchase offer and tortiously induced a breach of that agreement. The jury charge correctly stated the law and explanatory instructions were proper to enable the jury to render a verdict. A retired judge was properly appointed to complete the trial when the original judge fell ill and defendant was not denied a fair trial. Defendant received due process in the handling of its motion for new trial. Further, there was no jury misconduct.


OUTCOME: The court issued an order to plaintiff oil company to file a punitive damages remittitur of two billion dollars. The judgment would then be reformed to show one billion dollars in punitive damages and would be affirmed as reformed. If plaintiff failed to file the remittitur, the judgment would be reversed and remanded. Punitive damages of three billion dollars constituted a confiscation assets rather than punishment for past action.

Pierce v. State


No. 3-86-012-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


724 S.W.2d 928; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6634



February 11, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF WILLIAMSON COUNTY, 26TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, NO. 85-443-K, HONORABLE WILLIAM S. LOTT, JUDGE PRESIDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the 26th Judicial District, District Court, Williamson County (Texas), convicting him of indecency with a child under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.11(a)(1) (Supp. 1987).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of indecency with a child under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.11(a)(1) (Supp. 1987) and sentenced to 20 years imprisonment. Appellant sought review, and the court affirmed, finding that the admission pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.071, § 2 (Supp. 1987), of a videotape of the complainant's police interview did not violate appellant's right to confrontation under U.S. Const. amend. VI and Tex. Const. art. I, § 10, because the witness who made the out-of-court statement was available for full and effective cross-examination at trial. The court found that the failure to allow appellant to cross-examine the witness during the state's case-in-chief rather than during the defense's presentation did not demonstrate any denial of due process. Further, appellant failed to assert the right at trial. Because appellant had not been charged, arrested, or subject to custodial interrogation at the time the complainant's statement was videotaped, he had no right to counsel for any purpose at that time.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for indecency with a child, finding that the admission of a videotape of complainant's police interview was not unconstitutional because the witness was available for cross-examination at trial.

Rose v. Doctors Hospital Facilities


No. 05-86-00009-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


735 S.W.2d 244; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 8200



February 9, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing of Cause Overruled January 23, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs surviving wife and parents appealed from the judgment notwithstanding the verdict that was entered by the District Court of Dallas County (Texas) in favor of defendant hospitals in a wrongful death medical malpractice action pursuant to the Texas Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i (Supp. 1986).


OVERVIEW: The jury returned a verdict for plaintiffs surviving wife and parents in a wrongful death medical malpractice action against defendant hospitals. However, the trial court entered a judgment notwithstanding the verdict for defendants. Plaintiffs appealed. The appellate court reversed in an unpublished opinion and rendered judgment on the verdict for plaintiffs subject to the $ 500,000 limitation set out in the Texas Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 11.02(a) (Supp. 1986), as adjusted for inflation. But because remittiturs were also suggested with respect to each plaintiff, only plaintiff surviving wife's award was over the limit and thus subject to reduction. The court ruled that the recovery cap and disparate treatment created by the cap did not violate the due process or equal protection provisions of U.S. Const. amend. XIV or Tex. Const. art. I, § 19, or the open courts provision of Tex. Const. art. I, § 13, because the limitation was rationally related to the legitimate governmental goal of reducing the frequency and severity of medical liability claims in order to make health care more affordable and available to all.


OUTCOME: The judgment for defendants was reversed, judgment was rendered for plaintiffs on the jury verdict, and remittiturs were suggested as to each plaintiff in an unpublished opinion. The award to plaintiff surviving wife was further reduced by application of the limits imposed by the Medical Liability Act because her jury award exceeded those limits and the limitations did not violate her due process or equal protection rights.

 

1137 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Ex parte Maddux


No. 01-86-0462-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


725 S.W.2d 724; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6322



February 5, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Reported at: 725 S.W.2d 724 at 727.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Opinion of December 11, 1986, Reported at: 725 S.W.2d 724. On Appeal from the 262nd District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 451,092, Judge Doug Shaver.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought a rehearing of the appeal by the court, which affirmed the order of the 262nd District Court, Harris County (Texas) dismissing the indictment of the accused on speedy trial grounds.


OVERVIEW: The state sought a rehearing by the court of an appeal in which the court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the indictment against the accused on speedy trial grounds. The court overruled the motion for rehearing. The court found no merit in the state's contention that in order for Tex. Code. Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 28.061 to operate to bar further prosecution, the entire indictment, rather than a single offense, must be dismissed. The state had stipulated that the two separate offenses arose from the same transaction, and one of the offenses was dismissed on speedy trial grounds. The court pointed out that the discharge portion of the statute referred to offenses, not indictments. There was no significance to the fact that the discharged offense was pleaded as part of an indictment and not as a separate indictment. The court had no jurisdiction to consider whether the trial court's ruling was plainly erroneous, because the state had no right to appeal in criminal cases. The court held that neither the Speedy Trial Act nor Article 28.061 violated the separation of powers doctrine set out in Tex. Const. art. II, § 1.


OUTCOME: The court overruled the state's motion for rehearing. The statute in question barred prosecution of any offenses arising out of the same transaction as an offense dismissed on speedy trial grounds, and it made no difference that the offense the state wished to prosecute was part of an indictment rather than a separate indictment. The speedy trial statutes did not violate the separation of powers doctrine.

Adams v. State


No. 01-86-0451-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


725 S.W.2d 446; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6323



February 5, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the Harris County Criminal Court at Law No. 3, Trial Court Cause No. 825,028, Trial Judge Jimmie Duncan.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the order of the Criminal Court at Law No. 3, Harris County (Texas) that revoked his probation for driving while intoxicated after he was convicted of driving while his license was suspended, and contended that his conviction should have been declared void because the caption to the amendment of the Texas DWI statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of driving while intoxicated and was placed on probation. Thereafter, his probation was revoked after he was convicted of driving while his license was suspended. This appeal followed. Appellant contended that his conviction should have been declared void because the caption to the amendment of the Texas DWI statute violated Tex. Const. art. III, § 35 because the legislative bill included more than one subject. The court disagreed and affirmed. Section 35 had been amended in 1986 to provide that laws enacted prior to its effective date would not be held void because of an inadequate caption.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the revocation of appellant's probation for driving while intoxicated because the Texas DWI statute was not void under the Texas Constitution.

HERNANDEZ v. STATE


No. 01-85-00831-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6332



February 5, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 209th District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 405,497.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction in the 209th District Court, Harris County (Texas) for capital murder for a crime which occurred when he was 16 years old.


OVERVIEW: 17 year old defendant was convicted of capital murder and sentenced to life imprisonment for a murder committed during the robbery of a convenience store. The court affirmed holding that the evidence when viewed in a light most favorable to the verdict was evidence from which any rational trier of fact could have found all of the essential elements of the crime beyond a reasonable doubt. The court held that because defendant neither joined the State's request for an instruction on the lesser included offense of murder nor objected to the failure of the charge to include it, error on this point was not preserved for review. The court held that because the evidence showed that the conduct of defendant alone was sufficient to sustain the conviction, or supported defendant's guilt as a principal actor, any error resulting from a failure to charge the jury on the law of parties was harmless error. The court held that the prosecutor's closing argument regarding flight was proper. The court held that defendant was properly prosecuted for capital murder and that the statutory scheme which required a mandatory sentence of life imprisonment was constitutional.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for capital murder affirmed because the evidence was sufficient to support the jury's verdict, the trial court did not err by not charging the jury as to the lesser included offense of murder or as to the law of parties and the converse of the law of parties, the prosecutor's closing argument on flight was proper, and defendant was properly prosecuted for capital murder under a constitutional statute.

BROOKS v. STATE


No. 01-86-0206-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6345



February 5, 1987, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 209th District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 433,447.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted by a jury of aggravated robbery in the 209th District Court of Harris County (Texas), and sentenced to 20 years confinement. Appellant sought review of his conviction, arguing that his right to due process was violated in light of a variation between the charge and the indictment, and raising three other errors.


OVERVIEW: Appellant stood guard at the door with a gun while two others shot a drug dealer and stole the dealer's money and cocaine. Appellant was indicted for aggravated robbery. At trial, the trial court charged the jury on the theory of parties; appellant did not object. Appellant was convicted and sentenced to 20 years. Appellant sought review, contending that he was denied a fair and impartial trial and due process because the indictment failed to give him notice of the specific theory with which he was charged. The court affirmed the conviction. Appellant's failure to object to the charge on parties undermined his contention that he was surprised by the charge. Appellant's objection to the constitutionality of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, was not raised at trial, and had already been rejected by another court. The court held that appellant failed to show ineffective assistance of counsel merely because his lawyer misspoke appellant's name and used the word "hisself."


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction, holding that the trial court properly charged the jury on the law of parties, even though there was no allegation in the indictment; in any event, the evidence was sufficient to convict appellant as a principal. The written instruction submitted by the trial court was constitutional. The court held that appellant failed to demonstrate ineffective assistance of counsel.

OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of aggravated sexual assault and sentence because the statute authorizing a jury charge on the law of parole was constitutional. The court found that appellant failed to preserve any error by failing to object to the charge at trial.

Schultz v. State


No. 01-86-0434-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


725 S.W.2d 411; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6283



January 29, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the County Court at Law No. 1 of Brazos County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 411-85. Trial Judge, Claude Davis.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the County Court at Law, Brazos County, Texas, which convicted him of driving while intoxicated pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 67011-1, § (a)(2)(B) (1987).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of driving while intoxicated. The court affirmed the conviction and held that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 67011-1 § (a)(2)(B) was not unconstitutionally vague for having different weight measurements due to different measuring substances or for not making sense because defendant's reading was strained. The court rejected defendant's claim that the statute was vague because of his lack of expertise. The court refused to rule on defendant's claim that state must plead the measure of intoxication used because this claim differed from the trial objection. The court affirmed the trial court's ruling against defendant's motion to quash the information because Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Code § 19.01-19 (1984) did not require individual certification.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of driving while intoxicated because the charging statute was not unconstitutionally vague, the motion to quash the information was properly denied because the complaint did not need to be filed before the information, defendant did not have a right to counsel during his breath test, and individual certification of the intoxilyzer test was not required.

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6301

NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision by the 228th District Court of Harris County, Texas, in which appellant pled guilty to a jury of felony possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver, namely, at least 400 grams of cocaine, and the jury assessed punishment at 55 years of confinement and a fine of one dollar.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed a decision by the trial court which, following appellant's plea of guilty before a jury of felony possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver, assessed punishment at 55 years of confinement. Because appellant did not object at trial that the state's remarks constituted an impermissible allusion to the parole laws, he could not raise the objection at the appellate level. CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of orders of a district court of Dallas County (Texas) that entered judgment, convicting defendant of aggravated robbery and that sentenced defendant, upon a jury recommendation, to 60 years in confinement.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled true to two enhancement paragraphs contained in an indictment. At the subsequent punishment phase of trial, the prosecution requested the jury impose a 20-year sentence based on calendar time in the penitentiary. The court found the prosecution's argument to the jury during the punishment phase of defendant's trial was error, was manifestly improper, and was so prejudicial that even an instruction to disregard would not have cured the error.

1149 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Moore v. State


No. 01-86-00044-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


723 S.W.2d 335; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6211



January 15, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 182nd District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 421,343.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the 182nd District Court of Harris County (Texas), which that found him guilty of murder and sentenced him to 35 years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of murder and sentenced to 35 years' imprisonment. Appellant claimed that the trial court erred in overruling his objection to the state's misstatement of the law during jury argument. The court disagreed, finding that the state was answering an argument raised by opposing counsel which was a permissible area for jury argument. Appellant argued that the trial court erred in unduly restricting his right to conduct voir dire examination. The right of counsel to question veniremembers and the right of the trial court to control the voir dire must be balanced. The court evaluated the reasonableness of a time limitation by noting whether or not an appellant did not attempt to prolong the voir dire, showed that he was not permitted to ask proper questions, and showed that he was not permitted to examine jurors who served on the jury. Here appellant attempted to prolong voir dire by questioning prospective jurors whom he had questioned earlier. He did not request a bill of exceptions, and he did not show that he was not permitted to examine jurors who served on the jury. The court affirmed the trial court's decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that convicted appellant of murder and sentenced him to 35 years' imprisonment, where the trial court did not err in overruling his objection to the state's misstatement of law during jury argument, and the court reasonably controlled voir dire where appellant attempted to prolong the process and failed to show he was not permitted to examine jurors who served on the jury.

Alvarado v. State


No. 3-85-234-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


723 S.W.2d 318; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6379



January 14, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 147TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, NO. 79,169, HONORABLE MACE B. THURMAN, JR., JUDGE PRESIDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a jury decision from the District Court of Travis County, 147th Judicial District (Texas), convicting him of aggravated robbery in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 29.03(a)(2) (1974).


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction for aggravated robbery under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 29.03(a)(2) (1974). Defendant argued that the trial court erred by including in its charge at the punishment stage of trial an instruction related to parole, as mandated by Tex. Crim. P. Code Ann. § art. 37.07, § 4(e) (1986). Defendant argued that the instruction operated as an ex post facto law and was therefore unconstitutional. On appeal, the court held that Tex. Crim. P. Code Ann. art. 37.07, §4 (1986), which generally apprised the jury of the nature of parole and the possibility that defendant's prison term could be shortened by application of good time credits and parole, did not violate Tex. Const. Ann. art. I. § 16 (1984). The statute was procedural in nature rather than substantive. Moreover, the statute correctly instructed the jury not to consider the manner in which the parole law might be applied to a particular defendant. The statute was not facially unconstitutional and did not operate as an ex post facto law. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of aggravated robbery because the trial court did not err by instructing the jury generally as to the possibility that parole might shorten a criminal sentence. The statute that required the trial court to give such an instruction was not facially unconstitutional and did not operate as an ex post facto law.

BOULDING v. STATE

1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6174



January 8, 1987, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 183rd District Court of Harris County, Cause No. 383,351


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment from the 183rd District Court of Harris County (Texas), which convicted appellant of sexual abuse of a child and sentenced appellant to prison.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of sexual abuse of a child in the trial court. Appellant sought the court's review, asserting that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.10(b) (repealed 1983) discriminated against homosexuals by failing to make the promiscuity defense available to them in the same way that it was available to heterosexuals. The court reversed appellant's conviction, holding that appellant was denied the promiscuity defense of § 21.10(b), in violation of the equal protection guarantees. Appellee filed a petition for discretionary review in the trial court for further consideration of appellant's case in light of newly decided case law. The trial court granted the petition and remanded to the court. The court held that there was no authority which held that homosexual conduct was a constitutionally protected activity under the equal protection clause or the state equal rights amendment, and appellant had cited to none in his appeal. Further, the constitutionality of Cal. Penal Code § 21.06, which declared homosexual conduct a misdemeanor offense, had been upheld against a claim that it constituted an equal protection violation. Accordingly, the trial court's judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Judgment of conviction was affirmed where the denial to appellant, as a homosexual, of the promiscuity defense did not violate appellant's constitutional rights as homosexual conduct was not a constitutionally protected activity under the equal protection clause or the state equal rights amendment.

Coleman v. State


No. 01-85-0976-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


735 S.W.2d 475; 1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6191



January 8, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 248th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 435,764.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appeals his conviction in the 248th District Court of Harris County, (Texas) of two counts of aggravated robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to two counts of aggravated robbery. Prior to entering his plea, defendant made a motion requesting the state to elect between the two counts. The trial court denied the motion. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction of the first count of aggravated robbery. The court ruled that defendant could not raise its objection regarding the constitutionality of jury instruction regarding parole on appeal for the first time as it was not raised at trial, that the jury instruction was not vague or misleading, that the trial court did not err in determining that aggravated robbery was one of the offenses covered under article 21.24(a) of the Texas Code of Criminal Procedure which allows two or more offenses to be joined in a single indictment, with each offense stated in a separate count, if the offense arises out of the same criminal episode. However, the court reversed the conviction of the second count of aggravated robbery, and remanded it to the trial court, because defendant was entitled to severance of the two kidnapping offenses upon his request for an election between the two counts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendant's conviction of the first count of aggravated robbery, but reversed the conviction as to the second count and remanded it to the trial court for further proceedings. The court ruled that defendant was entitled to severance of the two offenses.

JAMES v. STATE


No. A14-86-103-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1987 Tex. App. LEXIS 6154



January 2, 1987, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 337th Judicial District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Cause No. 436,345


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the 337th Judicial District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted defendant of robbery, found that he had two previous felony convictions, and assessed punishment at confinement for 50 years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant physically assaulted the complainant and took her purse as she got into her automobile. Defendant denied commission of the offense. The trial court convicted defendant of robbery, found that defendant had two previous felony convictions, and assessed punishment at confinement for 50 years. The court affirmed the judgment and held that there was no prosecutorial misconduct. The prosecutor testified, denying that any suggestion was made to a witness that one of the photographs would be the photo of the suspect in the case in which the witness was involved. The court found that the trial court did not err in instructing the jury on the law affecting good time and parole, Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 (Supp. 1986), because the statute was not unconstitutional. Although the trial court mistakenly stated that defendant pleaded guilty instead of not guilty, defendant made no objection, and therefore, did not preserve the matter for review. Furthermore, the docket sheet, the court's charge, and the judgment all reflected that defendant entered a plea of not guilty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court and found that defendant did not prove that there was any prosecutorial misconduct. The prosecutor testified that no suggestion was made to a witness that any of the photographs she would be viewing was that of defendant. Defendant failed to preserve for review the trial court's misstatement that defendant pleaded guilty because defendant failed to object at the time of the misstatement.

Amescua v. State


No. 04-85-00482-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


723 S.W.2d 266; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 9425



December 31, 1986, Decided  
December 31, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 22, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 25th District Court of Guadalupe County, Trial Court No. 85-53, Honorable B.B. Schraub, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the District Court of Guadalupe County (Texas) which convicted him of indecency with a child under Tex. Penal Code Ann. §21.11(1986). During the trial of this action, the court permitted videotaped testimony of the child, which showed the child demonstrating how appellant sexually abused her, even though appellant was unable to cross-examine the child at the time of the questioning.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of indecency with a child under Tex. Penal Code §21.11(1986). Appellant challenged the conviction and contended that the trial court erred in several respects with regard to the admission of evidence and violated appellant's constitutional rights of confrontation. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and held that there was sufficient evidence to support appellant's conviction. The court stated that it could not review appellant's contentions of error regarding the jury charges, the competency of the child witness, or the failure of the trial court to require cross-examination of the child witness immediately after the presentation of her videotaped testimony because appellant failed to object properly to these issues at trial, and thus, they were not preserved for review. The court also found that appellant failed to preserve any issue regarding the State's impeachment of its own witness. Finally, the court held that appellant's right to confront the child witness was not violated by this inability to be present during the videotaping of the child witness because appellant had the opportunity to cross-examine the witness at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction of appellant for indecency with a child. The court held that the evidence supported the conviction and that appellant failed to properly preserve the issues in his challenge regarding jury charges, the child's competency, or the timing of his cross-examination of the child, after her videotaped testimony was admitted. The court also held that appellant's right to confrontation was not violated.

Willis v. Maverick


No. 04-85-00177-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


723 S.W.2d 259; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 9427



December 31, 1986, Decided  
December 31, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 26, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 288th District Court of Bexar County, Trial Court No. 81-CI-19851, Honorable Raul Rivera, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant client sought review of a judgment of non obstante veredicto in a legal malpractice action entered in the 288th District Court, Bexar County, Texas.


OVERVIEW: Appellant client filed a legal malpractice suit against appellee attorney. The suit stemmed from appellee's representation of both appellant and her ex-husband in their divorce proceedings. Ten months after the divorce settlement, appellant learned that pursuant to a change in the agreement made by appellee, her ex-husband was filing partition suit on the marital home which appellant occupied with her children. Appellant had believed that such a suit was prohibited under their agreement. She then filed her action against appellee. A jury awarded to her actual damages and exemplary damages. However, the trial court then granted appellee's motion for judgment non obstante veredicto and entered a take-nothing judgment against appellant. On appeal, the court held that the two-year tort limitations statute provided a solid ground for the trial court's judgment. The court reasoned that the limitations was tolled until December 10, 1979, at the latest. Because appellant did not file her malpractice action until December 21, 1981, she exceeded the two-year period and her suit was barred.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment non obstante veredicto of the trial court and the entrance of a take nothing judgment against appellant client in a legal malpractice action against appellee attorney because a two-year tort limitations statute barred appellant's claim.

Glen Ridge I Condominiums, Ltd. v. Federal Sav. & Loan Ins. Corp.


No. 05-85-00873-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


734 S.W.2d 374; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 13061



December 30, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Reported at: 734 S.W.2d 374 at 387.<DSPQ2>


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant borrowers moved for rehearing of its challenge to a judgment of a District Court, Dallas County, Texas, which dismissed, for want of jurisdiction, its suit to enjoin appellees, receiver, lender, and trustees, from foreclosing on its property.


OVERVIEW: Appellant borrowers filed suit against appellees, receiver, lender, and various trustees, and sought the prevention of foreclosure on its property, to cancel deeds of trust, damages, injunctive relief, and attorney's fees. Appellees moved to dismiss asserting that the trial court lacked jurisdiction pursuant to 12 U.S.C.S. §1464(d)(6)(c). The court reversed the portion of the judgment pertaining to the adjudication of rights that arose under state law and stated that these claims were to have been adjudicated by a judiciary authorized by U.S. Const. art. III. The court stated that it had appropriate jurisdiction to hear appellants' challenges, that a uniform body of federal laws was not required to determine the parties' dispute, and that Congress could not remove appellants' state law claims from the judiciary. The court affirmed the portion of the judgment that appellants' actions under the federal securities' laws and those aimed at appellee receiver for disparagement of title and violation of state foreclosure laws were within the authority of agency adjudication.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion for rehearing, withdrew its former opinion, and reversed in part and remanded the judgment that conferred jurisdiction over appellant borrowers' state law claims to agency adjudication because it was unconstitutional. The court affirmed in part the judgment to confer jurisdiction of appellants' allegations of violations of federal securities laws and those aimed at appellee receiver to agency adjudication.

 

1157 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Winter v. State


No. 01-86-00031-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


725 S.W.2d 728; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 9382



December 18, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law Number Three of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 862,125.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for possession of less than two ounces of marijuana following a jury verdict in the County Criminal Court at Law Number Three, Harris County (Texas).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for possession of less than two ounces of marijuana. On appeal, the conviction was reversed and reformed to show a judgment of acquittal. The court held that because defendant did not admit guilt to the crime for which he had been convicted, he did not waive his challenge to the sufficiency of the evidence. The court held that the prosecution attempted to prove defendant's control and knowledge by an inference from defendant's response to a pre-arrest question posed by an officer. There were no direct facts to support the inference. Defendant was in the area where the drug was found, but was not in personal possession of or exercising control over the marijuana. There was no evidence of furtive gestures toward the contraband, no attempt to escape, no evidence that defendant was under the influence of marijuana or other drugs, and no incriminating statements. The evidence amounted to a suspicion of guilt through the stacking of inferences and was insufficient to sustain the conviction.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction of possession of less than two ounces of marijuana was reversed and reformed to show acquittal because there was insufficient evidence to support the essential elements of the crime beyond a reasonable doubt; the facts did not support an inference of defendant's personal possession or control over the marijuana.

Swope v. State


No. 3-85-193-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


723 S.W.2d 216; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 9432



December 17, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 11, 1987. Appellant's Motion for Rehearing on Petition for Discretionary Review Denied March 13, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF LAMPASAS COUNTY, 27TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, NO. 5377, HONORABLE C. W. DUNCAN, JR., JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the District Court of Lampasas County (Texas), convicting appellant as a party to the offense of theft by deception pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 31.01, 31.03, and 7.02. Appellant was sentenced to confinement for 20 years and a fine of $ 80,000.


OVERVIEW: Appellant and other relatives in efforts to obtain loans told many people that appellant's aunt was the heiress of her husband's multi-million dollar Swiss estate. Depending upon the potential lender, the value of the estate assets ranged from one million to ten million dollars and consisted of vineyards, chocolates, watches, or cuckoo clocks. Appellant and her aunt employed an attorney to set up a trust to place the estate proceeds when received, but only $ 10 was ever placed in the trust. The actual value of the estate belonging to the husband of appellant's aunt was $ 24,000. An elderly victim purchased 11 cashier's checks totaling over $ 500,000 and gave them to appellant's aunt as a loan so that she could close out her husband's multi-million dollar estate and obtain the assets. Appellant was convicted as a party to the offense of theft by deception. She contended that the evidence was insufficient to convict her. The court affirmed the conviction based on knowledge and intent shown by five extraneous transactions involving appellant and her aunt regarding attempts to borrow money based on the alleged bountiful legacy.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. Appellant's conviction as a party to the offense of theft by deception was upheld, because there was sufficient evidence that appellant and her aunt intentionally misrepresented her aunt's inheritance to the victim, knowing the falsity of their representations based on probate records showing only a slender estate and the inventory of the estate.

Beasley v. State


No. 01-86-00097-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


721 S.W.2d 426; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 9265



December 11, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 228th District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 433,083.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for aggravated sexual assault, enhanced by two prior felony convictions, following a jury verdict in the 228th District Court, Harris County (Texas), alleging error by the trial court in instructing the jury on parole and good conduct time.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for aggravated sexual assault, enhanced by two prior felony convictions. Defendant argued that the trial court erred in giving a jury instruction on parole and good conduct time pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07 § 4(b) (1986), asserting that the statute was unconstitutional and the jury instruction given thereunder was unintelligible, misleading, and confusing. The court affirmed the conviction, holding that, while it might be difficult for a juror to refrain from applying the parole law after being informed of its possible impact on a sentence, difficulty in following jury instructions did not render the instruction unconstitutional. The court held that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(b) (1986) was not an unconstitutional invasion of the province of the executive branch of the government. The court concluded that the jury instructions did not harm defendant as the jury was instructed that it could not consider how the parole law affected defendant in particular.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for aggravated sexual assault, enhanced by two prior felony convictions, was affirmed on the grounds that no harm was shown by the jury instructions, which advised the jurors that they could consider the existence of the parole law, but not as it affected defendant in particular.

Diaz v. State


No. 04-86-00037-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


722 S.W.2d 482; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 9391



December 10, 1986, Decided  
December 10, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 341st District Court of Webb County, Trial Court No. 18,958, Honorable Elma Teresa Salinas, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the 341st District Court of Webb County (Texas), which convicted appellant for murder, pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.02(a)(1) (1974).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of murder pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.02(a)(1). The court found that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 did not make the offense charged a greater one; nor did it make an innocent act criminal; nor did it inflict greater punishment than the murder law contained when the instant offense was committed. The court held that it had not been shown to be an ex post facto law. The court continued that there was no evidence of an act which needed to be explained by reputation and therefore the trial court correctly excluded the evidence offered to show that the deceased was the aggressor in fact. The court continued that an unimpeached witness' testimony could not be given more credibility by other state's evidence but that did not mean that the state could not present more than one witness to relate what had happened. The court also found that when not descriptive of that which was legally essential to the validity of an indictment or information, unnecessary words could be rejected as surplusage. The court affirmed the conviction.


OUTCOME: Judgment convicting appellant of murder was affirmed. The court held that the statute that went into effect after appellant had committed the murder was not an ex post facto law and was applicable. The law did not make the offense charged a greater one, it did not make an innocent act criminal, and it did not inflict greater punishment than the murder law contained when the instant offense was committed.
