Hyde v. State


No. 6-86-028-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Sixth District, Texarkana


723 S.W.2d 754; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 9164



December 2, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the 124th Judicial District Court of Gregg County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Judicial District Court of Gregg County (Texas), which convicted him of aggravated robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction of aggravated robbery. Defendant contended that the conviction should be reversed because the trial court failed to instruct the jury concerning the parole laws and because the sentence he received was excessive. The court affirmed and held that because defendant did not object to the failure of the trial court to instruct the jury concerning the effect of the parole laws, he was entitled to a reversal only if the failure to instruct was so egregious that he was deprived of a fair and impartial trial. The court determined that defendant had not demonstrated such harm. The court held that it did not have jurisdiction to review the reasonableness of punishments assessed by juries and trial courts if they were within the range of punishment prescribed by statute for the offense, unless the punishments were so plainly disproportionate to the offense as to shock the sense of humankind and thus constitute cruel and unusual punishment. The court held that defendant's punishment was not cruel or unusual because defendant admitted to robbing his victim by using a loaded pistol and by putting her in fear of her life.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which convicted defendant of aggravated robbery. The court held that the trial court's failure to instruct the jury regarding the effect of parole laws did not deprive him of a fair and impartial trial. The court found that it did not have jurisdiction to review defendant's punishment because the punishment was not cruel or unusual under the circumstances.

Rijo v. State


No. 07-86-0167-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Seventh District, Amarillo


721 S.W.2d 562; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 9170



December 2, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF POTTER COUNTY, 181ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT, NO. 23,543-B, HONORABLE GEORGE E. DOWLEN, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the 181st District Court, Potter County (Texas), convicting him of delivery of a controlled substance, namely cocaine, of 200 grams or more but less than 400 grams, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, §§ 4.02, 4.03 (1986), contending it was error for the trial court to deny his motion to discharge the jury after the prosecutor used a peremptory challenge to remove a black venireman.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction for delivery of a controlled substance, namely cocaine, of 200 grams or more but less than 400 grams, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, §§ 4.02, 4.03 (1986). His sole contention was that the trial court erred in denying his motion to discharge the jury after the prosecutor used a peremptory challenge to remove a black venireman. Appellant was determined to be black by physical characteristics and Hispanic by name. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the prosecutor's striking of the only member of the racial group to which appellant appeared to belong, while not striking a member of the racial group with which appellant was identified by his name, did not constitute the "pattern" of strikes which raises an inference of discrimination. The black venireman's statement that in his mind, the amount of cocaine delivered would not affect the fine that may be assessed as part of the punishment, indicated a bias against the range of punishment provided by statute and was a proper basis for a challenge for cause or a peremptory challenge.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. The trial court did not err in denying appellant's motion to discharge the jury. The trial court was justified in impliedly finding from the facts and relevant circumstances that appellant did not raise the necessary inference of purposeful discrimination in the selection of the petit jury.

 

1165 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Joslin v. State


No. 05-85-1222-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


722 S.W.2d 725; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 9398



December 1, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 31, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the District Court, Dallas County (Texas), convicting him of murder, sentencing him to life imprisonment, and imposing a $ 10,000 fine. Appellant challenged the sufficiency of the evidence and the constitutionality of a jury instruction regarding parole given pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 (1986).


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction for murder on the grounds of insufficiency of the evidence and the alleged unconstitutionality of a jury instruction regarding parole given pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 (1986). On appeal, the court affirmed. The circumstantial evidence was sufficient to establish motive, opportunity, and means, and excluded every reasonable hypothesis other than that appellant committed the murder. The reviewing court did not have to determine whether the evidence at trial established guilt beyond a reasonable doubt, only that any rational trier of fact could have believed that guilt was so established. The legislature did not exceed its powers when it passed Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4, which required the court to instruct the jury on parole laws. Tex. Const. art. IV, § 11 authorized the legislature to enact parole laws. Merely requiring that the jury be informed what the law is and admonishing them not to use the information in sentencing did not interfere with the court's discretion. Art. 37.07, § 4 did not constitute an ex post facto law because it did not change or enhance the punishment for murder.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. The circumstantial evidence was sufficient to exclude every reasonable hypothesis other than that appellant committed the murder. The enactment of the statute requiring a jury instruction on parole was a valid exercise of legislative power pursuant to the state constitution and was not otherwise unconstitutional as an ex post facto law.

 

1166 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Rose v. State


No. 05-85-01136-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


724 S.W.2d 832; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 9442



December 1, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 7, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from a district court of Dallas County (Texas), which convicted appellant of aggravated robbery.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated robbery. The court concluded that appellant's assault on the police officers was part and parcel of appellant's flight and therefore upheld the admission into evidence of proof that appellant assaulted the police officers. The court held that the legislature did not exceed its constitutional powers over parole when it enacted Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(a). The court found that the parole law instructions did not authorize the judicial branch to usurp or interfere with the exclusive authority to determine parole granted to the Board of Pardons and Paroles, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.18, § 1 (1986), and therefore the statute did not violate the separation of powers doctrine of the state constitution. The court determined that the required jury instructions presented no irreconcilable conflict because they clearly told the jury not to consider the manner in which the parole law may be applied to appellant. The court found that aiding the jury in understanding why they are prohibited from considering how the parole law may be applied was a proper subject for the trial court's instruction. The court affirmed the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court convicting appellant for aggravated robbery. The court held that appellant was not denied a fair and impartial trial or due process of law by the mere submission of the parole law instructions to the jury because the instructions did not authorize the judicial branch to usurp the authority to determine parole and thereby the statute did not violate the separation of powers doctrine.

Wun-Yi Tsai v. Wells


No. 13-86-124-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


725 S.W.2d 271; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 9082



November 26, 1986, Decided  
November 26, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the 130th District Court of Matagorda County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant physician appealed from the 130th District Court of Matagorda County, Texas, which issued judgment for plaintiffs and imposed punitive damages in plaintiffs' action for medical malpractice.


OVERVIEW: On March 10, 1980 defendant physician performed an operation on plaintiff wife's (plaintiff) pelvis area. On April 28, 1983 plaintiff was treated for pelvic inflammatory disease. Plaintiffs claimed defendant's operation was negligent and resulted in the inflammatory disease. The reviewing court affirmed the judgment for plaintiffs in their medical malpractice action against defendant. Plaintiffs' action was not barred by the two-year statute of limitations under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01 because plaintiff did not have a reasonable opportunity to discover defendant's wrong within the two-year period. Defendant never discovered the cause of plaintiff's continuing pain and plaintiff did not learn the exact cause until the 1983 operation. The trial court did not err in excluding evidence that plaintiff had contact with gonorrhea because there was no medical evidence that plaintiff had actually contracted gonorrhea. Defendant's use of silk sutures in plaintiff without medical justification and with plaintiff wanting to retain fertility was evidence of gross negligence. Considering the extensive damage done to plaintiff the exemplary damages award was reasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and punitive damages award for plaintiffs in their medical malpractice action against defendant physician. Plaintiffs were not barred by the two-year statute of limitations because plaintiffs did not have a reasonable opportunity to discover defendant's error within two years. The trial court properly excluded evidence concerning gonorrhea because there was no evidence plaintiff contracted gonorrhea.

 

1168 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Balash v. State


No. A14-85-754-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


720 S.W.2d 878; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 9165



November 26, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from County Criminal Court at Law No. 3 of Harris County, Cause No. 847,084.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision of the County Criminal Court at Law No. 3 of Harris County (Texas), which convicted her of public lewdness for rubbing her dance partner's genitals.


OVERVIEW: Appellant rubbed the genitals of her dance partner while dancing at a local nightclub. She was arrested and charged with public lewdness. The trial court convicted her of public lewdness. Appellant contended that the public lewdness statute, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.07 (1974), was unconstitutionally vague and that the evidence was insufficient to support her conviction. On appeal the court affirmed, because it found that the public lewdness statute was not vague as it applied to appellant's conduct. Further, viewing the evidence in the light most favorable to the verdict, the evidence was sufficient for a rational trier of fact to find the element of intent beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for public lewdness was affirmed on the grounds that the public lewdness statute was not vague as applied to appellant's conduct of rubbing her dance partner's genitals and there was sufficient evidence to allow a rational trier of fact to find the element of intent by a reasonable doubt.

 

1169 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Hardy v. State


No. A14-85-835-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


722 S.W.2d 164; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 9174



November 26, 1986, Decided  
November 26, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 177th District Court of Harris County, Cause No. 369,753.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction of aggravated rape from the 177th District Court of Harris County (Texas). Appellant complained that the evidence was insufficient, that the trial court erred in charging the jury on parole and good time law, and that his right to a fair and impartial jury was denied when the prosecutor used peremptory challenges to exclude all eligible black venirepersons from the jury.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated rape. On appeal, appellant argued that the evidence was insufficient to identify him as the perpetrator of the offense and that the trial court erred in giving the jury the instruction set out in Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07 § 4, which appellant asserted invited the jury to consider the affect of the parole laws on him. Appellant further contenmded that he was denied his right to a fair and impartial jury when the prosecutor used peremptory challenges to remove all eligible black venirepersons from the jury. The court affirmed appellant's conviction holding that appellant left his license at the victim's apartment and that she later identified appellant in a picture and in court, thus, a rational trier of fact could have resolved the issue of identification beyond a reasonable doubt. The court further found that the jury instruction referencing parole law did not invite the jury to consider how the parole laws would affect appellant and that the trial court had expressly directed the jury not to consider the topic. Further, the court found that there was no proof of the repeated striking of blacks by the prosecutor.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed because a rational trier of fact could have found that appellant was the perpetrator beyond a reasonable doubt based on the victim's identification, that the jury instruction referencing parole law was not unconstitutional and expressly directed the jury not to consider the affect of parole laws and good time conduct, and no proof was presented that the prosecutor repeatedly excluded blacks from the jury.

 

1170 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Weaver v. State


No. 01-86-00094-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


721 S.W.2d 495; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 9037



November 20, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Discretionary Review Refused March 18, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from County Criminal Court at Law No. 8 of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 863,129.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the County Criminal Court at Law No. 8 of Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of driving while intoxicated in violation of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701l-1 (1986), on the ground that the results of a blood test were the result of an unlawful search and seizure, and that the evidence was insufficient to prove that he was operating a motor vehicle on a public road at the time of the alleged offense.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was involved in a fatal traffic accident, which was not his fault. An investigating officer smelled a light odor of alcohol on appellant's breath while he was being interviewed, but not under arrest. He admitted he had been drinking. He was injured and taken to a hospital where a blood sample was requested that revealed a blood alcohol level of .16 percent. A second blood sample was drawn by the hospital that revealed a blood alcohol level of .18 percent. Appellant was convicted of driving while intoxicated in violation of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701l-1 (1986). On appeal, the court affirmed because appellant's contention that the blood tests used against him were unconstitutional was belied by the fact that the second blood test had not been requested by appellee state and therefore constitutional protections did not apply, even if the first test had bee unlawfully obtained. In addition, the time frame within which appellant testified he had been drinking was sufficiently probative of intoxication while driving a vehicle to justify the jury's verdict that he had been driving while under the influence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for driving while under the influence of alcohol because it was not the result of an unlawful search and seizure since any error in obtaining a first blood sample by appellee state was vitiated by the second sample that had not been obtained by appellee. In addition, the evidence tying alcohol consumption to driving was sufficient to permit a rational inference of guilt.

Garrett v. State


No. 09-86-059-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Ninth District, Beaumont


721 S.W.2d 480; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 9350



November 20, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEALED FROM THE 252ND DISTRICT COURT OF JEFFERSON COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the 252nd District Court Jefferson County, Texas, which overruled defendant's application for writ of habeas corpus. The writ alleged Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 47.03(a)(1) (1986), was unconstitutional and defendant's indictment under the statute was fundamentally defective.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 47.03(a)(1) (1986), for allegedly operating a gambling place. Defendant pleaded guilty and was placed on probation. Defendant later filed a writ of habeas corpus arguing the statute was unconstitutional and that the indictment was fundamentally defective. The trial court overruled defendant's application for the writ. Defendant appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court first determined that writs of habeas corpus had been allowed to test the constitutionality of statutes. The court refused to determine the ground of error attacking the indictment. The court found defendant did not provide them with any guidance as to why § 47.03(a)(1), was vague. The court found the challenged statute to be sound. The court held the words of the statute were clear, specific, and easily understandable by a person of ordinary intelligence. The court declined to hold the statute unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court denying defendant's application for writ of habeas corpus because the challenged statute under the Texas Penal Code was not so vague and uncertain as to be incapable of being understood, nor was it unconstitutional.

Allen v. Mauro


No. 08-85-00342-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eighth District, El Paso


733 S.W.2d 228; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 13057; 98 Oil & Gas Rep. 355



November 19, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from 238th District Court of Midland County, Texas, TC No. B-32,417.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individuals challenged the decision of the 238th District Court of Midland County, Texas, which denied applications for prospecting permits filed by appellants with appellee Commissioner of the General Land Office involving substantial acreage of University of Texas land and public school lands.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed the conclusions of the trial court that certain portions of the Nature Resources Code were unconstitutional and otherwise repealed as well as its other findings, but affirmed its judgment declaring that appellant individuals were not entitled to the permits. The court concluded that there existed adequate and independent grounds for the trial court to arrive at its judgment without employing the findings relied on, which the court disagreed with, including those that declared Tex. Nat. Res. Code Ann. subch. G, ch. 52 unconstitutional. The court concluded that appellants' avenue as to university land lied most appropriately through the Tex. Educ. Code which specifically dealt with those lands. The court concluded that the avenue to public school land was directly found in the more definitive provisions of the Tex. Nat. Res. Code labeled "School Land Board." The court concluded that the intent of the legislature that permit leasing was a general provision, while the bid method was a specific provision, was gleaned from the actual statutes relating to the lease of state land construed as a whole.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's conclusions that certain portions of Natural Resources Code were unconstitutional, but affirmed its judgment declaring that appellant individuals were not entitled to the permits because appellants' avenue to gain permits to the university land lied most appropriately in the Education Code while public school land permit provisions lied in the Natural Resources Code.

 

1173 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


State v. Enterprise Co.


No. B14-86-119CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


728 S.W.2d 812; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 8974



November 6, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Civil County Court at Law No. One of Harris County, Trial Court No. 459,719


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state challenged the judgment of the Civil County Court at Law No. One of Harris County (Texas), which entered judgment in favor of appellee landowners for the full market value of the land taken for highway purposes.


OVERVIEW: Appellant state condemned a portion of appellee landowner's land for highway purposes, and the trial court entered judgment for appellee for the full market value of the land taken. Appellant contended that the trial court erred when it did not require the benefit to the remainder be offset against the compensation paid for the part taken. The court affirmed. It found Tex. Const. art. I, § 17, required that a person's property not be taken for public use unless adequate compensation was made, and adequate compensation was the full market value of the land taken. The court found that, while Tex. Prop. Code Ann. § 21.042 (1984) suggested that the legislature could have intended to change the method for determining adequate compensation for land condemned for highway purposes, if that principle was to be changed, it had to be done directly and not by suggestive language.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment for the full market value of the land taken for highway purposes, because the state constitution required that the value of the land not be offset by estimated benefits to a condemnee's remaining land, and language in a new statute suggested that the legislature might have intended to change the method for determining adequate compensation but did not directly do so or amend the constitution.

 

1174 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


BATES v. STATE


No. B14-85-065CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 8977



November 6, 1986, Decided and Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 248th District Court of Harris County, Trial Court No. 396,750.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the 248th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which convicted appellant of theft. Appellant alleged numerous errors including the insufficiency of evidence and the unconstitutionality of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.09.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of theft. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. It found that the state's evidence was sufficient to support a conviction for theft. It further found that the evidence was sufficient for the jury to find that the thefts were part of a scheme or continuing course of conduct. The court concluded that all of the extraneous offenses were relative to show either intent or scheme and that their probative value outweighed any prejudice. The court found that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.09 was not unconstitutionally vague or ambiguous and did not proscribe conduct but provided merely that violations of the theft statute committed pursuant to one scheme or continuing course of conduct might be considered one offense and the amounts aggregated to determine the grade of the offense. The court rejected appellant's argument that the court erred in failing to instruct the jury as to the definition of "scheme or continuing course of conduct" because they were terms of common understanding and required no definition by the court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court which convicted appellant of theft. It found that the state's evidence was sufficient to support a conviction for theft and for the jury to find that the thefts were part of a scheme or continuing course of conduct. The court concluded that the aggregation statute was neither unconstitutionally vague nor ambiguous and did not proscribe conduct.

 

1175 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


GONZALES v. STATE


No. 01-86-00072-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 8983



November 6, 1986, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 232nd District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 417,304


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment from the 232nd District Court of Harris County (Texas), convicting him of burglary of a habitation, finding enhancements of two prior convictions of burglary of a building with intent to commit theft, and sentencing him to 25 years confinement.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of burglary of a habitation, enhanced by two prior convictions of burglary of a building with intent to commit theft. The jury assessed his punishment at 25 years confinement. The court affirmed the conviction. The court found that appellant did not waive his right to counsel and made no request that he be permitted to represent himself. In his pro se motion, and in his testimony at the motion hearing, he expressed his wish for substitute counsel. The trial court found that appellant's counsel of record was capable of rendering effective assistance to appellant and that his reason for seeking dismissal was inadequate. The court held that, on the evidence presented at the hearing, the trial court did not err in that ruling. Appellant's point of error that the jury was erroneously led to believe that an incarcerated person received good time credit that reduced the term of years assessed was not made by appellant's objection at trial with sufficient specificity to preserve error. Appellant could not assert that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07 was unconstitutional when appellant did not urge the constitutionality of the statute at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in appellant's conviction of burglary of a habitation. The court held, on the evidence presented at appellant's motion hearing, that appellant did not waive his right to counsel and that he expressed his wish for substitute counsel. The trial court did not err in ruling that appellant's counsel of record was adequate. Appellant's objection to the jury instruction on punishment did not preserve error.

Lopez v. State


No. 04-85-00444-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


720 S.W.2d 201; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 9316



October 31, 1986, Decided  
October 31, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Extension Denied December 3, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from County Court at Law No. 9 of Bexar County, Trial Court No. 347,978, Honorable Bonnie Reed, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the County Court at Law No. 9, Bexar County, Texas, which convicted him of cruelty to an animal in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.11(a)(4) (1986). On appeal, defendant attacked the sufficiency of the evidence and the constitutionality of the statute.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his wife went to a movie theatre on a hot, sunny, dry July afternoon and left their dog in the car, which was parked in the direct sun. The car windows were left open approximately an inch and one-half on each side. Defendant was convicted of cruelty to an animal, pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. 42.11(a)(4) (1986). Defendant appealed, attacking the sufficiency of the evidence and the constitutionality of the statute. The court held that even though the evidence against defendant was circumstantial, a rational trier of fact could have found the essential elements of the crime beyond a reasonable doubt, and thus the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction. The court held that by presenting defensive evidence before the court, defendant waived review of the court's denial of his motion for acquittal. The court rejected defendant's challenge to the constitutionality of the statute, holding that terms of § 42.11(a)(4) had a meaning which could be understood by a person of ordinary intelligence and gave fair notice of conduct subject to prosecution; hence, the statute was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad under either U.S. Const. amends. V or XIV.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for cruelty to an animal, holding that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction because, even though the evidence was circumstantial, the trier of fact could have found the essential elements of the crime beyond a reasonable doubt. The court found that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad under either the Fifth or Fourteenth Amendment.

Clark v. State


No. 01-85-01013-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


721 S.W.2d 424; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 8910



October 30, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 26, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 228th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 433,318.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the 228th District Court, Harris County, Texas, which convicted defendant of the felony offense of burglary of a habitation with intent to commit sexual assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction of felony burglary of a habitation with intent to commit sexual assault. Defendant challenged the constitutionality of the trial court's punishment phase instructions and Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(b) (1986). Defendant contended that the § 4(b) instructions violated the separation of powers doctrine and were unconstitutional as the instructions allowed the jury to speculate on matters not related to deciding proper punishment and were confusing and vague. The state claimed that defendant's failure to object at trial waived any error. The court affirmed the conviction but stated that defendant's statement was sufficient to apprise the trial court of his constitutional objection. The court applied the presumption that the statutory instruction was valid and concluded that the instructions were not an unconstitutional legislative encroachment upon judicial power or an unconstitutional judicial usurpation of executive power. The court held that the protective language given by the trial court was sufficient to preclude any speculation by the jury. The court ruled that the instructions had a clarifying effect and were not vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of felony burglary of a habitation with intent to commit sexual assault. The court held that the instructions did not violate the separation of powers doctrine and were not unconstitutionally vague. The court ruled that the instructions, which included protective language, were sufficient to preclude any speculation as to incarceration by the jury outside of the task of assessing proper punishment.

Spelling v. State


No. 2-85-293-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


719 S.W.2d 404; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 9002



October 23, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled November 13, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT NO. 2 OF TARRANT COUNTY


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the Criminal District Court No. 2 of Tarrant County (Texas), which convicted her of the murder of her three month old son under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.02(a)(2) (1974).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of murder under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.02(a)(2) (1974). After the verdict and assessment of punishment, appellant filed a motion in arrest of judgment under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. arts. 41.01-41.05 (1979). The motion was overruled. The court affirmed the conviction, holding that her indictment was not defective because it closely tracked the wording of the statute, and she should have brought a motion to quash for clarification. The court held that jury argument was not improper because, although the prosecutor continued after an objection with a statement that appellant's credibility was for the jury to decide, he did not bring in new evidence. The court found no reversible error in the prosecutor's comments about appellant's lack of remorse because the jurors had an opportunity to observe her. The court held that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07 (1981) did not violate due process rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1, or Tex. Const. art. I, § 19, because the statute set out the exact wording of the instruction to be used by the trial court, and appellant was not treated differently than any other defendant in the same situation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction, holding that her indictment was not defective because it closely tracked the wording of the statute, jury argument was not improper because the prosecutor did not bring in new evidence and because the jurors had an opportunity to judge her credibility, and the sentencing statute did not violate due process rights because it set out exact wording of the jury instruction for the trial court to use.

Botello v. State


No. 04-86-00077-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


720 S.W.2d 838; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 9303



October 22, 1986, Decided  
October 22, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 49th District Court of Webb County, Trial Court No. 19,889, Honorable Ruben Garcia, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of a judgment of the 49th District Court of Webb County, Texas, which convicted her for the sale of a child in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 25.06.


OVERVIEW: Appellant mother was convicted for sale of a child in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 25.06. The jury assessed punishment at six years imprisonment. Appellant argued that fundamental error resulted when the indictment failed to allege the delivery of the child was for purposes of adoption. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment, holding that there was no fundamental defect in the indictment and also held that any rational trier of fact could have found the essential elements of the offense of sale of a child beyond a reasonable doubt. The court found that since the statute was framed in the disjunctive, there was no necessity for the additional averment that the delivery of the child was for the purposes of adoption. Appellant claimed that the evidence was insufficient to prove she offered to accept, agreed to accept, or accepted a thing of value for the delivery of the child. The court found evidence that appellant participated in the transaction by signing the receipt, holding the baby during the deal, making no attempt to remove the child, or call the police, or take affirmative action to prevent the close of the sale.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted appellant for the sale of a child. The court held that there was no fundamental defect in the indictment and also held that any rational trier of fact could have found the essential elements of the offense of sale of a child beyond a reasonable doubt.

Burns v. Delmar-West Lamar Consol. Indep. Sch. Dist.


No. 9511


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Sixth District, Texarkana


720 S.W.2d 836; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 8840



October 21, 1986, Decided  
October 21, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 18, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 62nd Judicial District Court of Lamar County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers challenged a judgment issued by the 62nd Judicial District Court of Lamar County (Texas), which dismissed appellants' action against appellee school district because appellants did not post bond under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 717m-1, § 8 (1986).


OVERVIEW: In response to appellant taxpayers' school bond election contest, appellee school district filed a motion to require appellants to post bond under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 717m-1, § 8 (1986). The trial court ordered appellants to post bond, but when they did not do so, the case was dismissed for failure to post bond. The court dismissed the appeal for want of jurisdiction. The court held that Article 717m-1, § 8 operated to deprive the court of jurisdiction to consider appellants' contentions because appellants neither posted the bond nor appealed from the trial court's order requiring such bond. The court also held that the statute did not deprive appellants of their due process because the statute did not expressly deny waiver of the bond for indigents. The court held that appellants were afforded a hearing on the feasibility of a bond being required, but brought no evidence to show that they were indigent. Moreover, the court held that the judgment was not void because the trial court had jurisdiction over the proceedings and appellants failed to avail themselves of the right to appeal the judgment in the manner provided by the statute.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed appellant taxpayers' challenge to the trial court's dismissal of appellants' action against appellee school district for want of jurisdiction because appellants did not post bond or appeal the order in the manner provided by statute.

McWilliams v. State


No. 01-85-0809-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


719 S.W.2d 380; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 8813



October 16, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 13, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 179th District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 426,657.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the 179th District Court of Harris County, Texas, which convicted appellant of the third degree felony offense of escape and assessed his punishment, enhanced by proof of a prior felony conviction, at six years of confinement.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of the felony of escape after he escaped from a halfway house. On review, appellant asserted that the trial court erred in assessing punishment against him as an enhanced offender in that the offense alleged for enhancement was unavailable for that purpose. Appellant also alleged that the halfway house was not a penal institution. The court affirmed and held that appellant's prior conviction was not such an essential element of the primary offense of felony escape under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 38.07(c)(2) as to bar its use for enhancement purposes. The court concluded that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6166x-4 showed that pre-parole inmate transferees were not equated in law with a parolee, and the use of such terms as "unit of confinement" and "continuing actual physical custody" in art. 6166x-4 connoted continuing imprisonment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a decision to convict appellant of the felony of escape and to assess punishment against him as an enhanced offender because while appellant was at a halfway house, his imprisonment was continued, and his prior conviction was not an essential element of the felony of escape.

Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. § 1970-166d, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant husband contended that the trial court never acquired jurisdiction over his divorce matter. Appellant argued the statute that created the court, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art 1970-166d, was unconstitutional in that it provided that a jury be composed of six members, under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1970-166d, § 7(a), while the Tex. Const. art. Buckner v. State

October 15, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 355TH DISTRICT COURT OF HOOD COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the 355th District Court of Hood County (Texas) that convicted him of aggravated sexual assault in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 22.011 and 22.021(a)(5) (1986) and sentenced accordingly.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 22.011 and 22.021(a)(5) (1986) and sentenced accordingly. Defendant challenged his conviction, asserting that the jury should have been instructed on the lesser included offense of indecency with a child, that it was error to admit the videotaped statement of the child, and that the state's remarks to the jury constituted reversible error. The court also found that there was insufficient evidence to charge the jury on the lesser included offense of indecency with a child. The case was remanded for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for aggravated sexual assault because the admission of the child's videotaped statement constituted reversible error in that it violated defendant's constitutional right to confrontation, and the state's comments to the jury were not proper because they were based on facts not admitted into evidence. The case was remanded for a new trial.

 

1185 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Hypke v. State


No. C14-85-00915-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


720 S.W.2d 158; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 8742



October 9, 1986, Decided  
October 9, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 180th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court No. 415,479.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a conviction for involuntary manslaughter, entered in the 180th District Court, Harris County (Texas), asserting that the requirements of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, § 6b(c) (1986), imposing a jail term as condition of probation, was unconstitutionally vague and disproportionately harsh. Appellant also asserted that the caption of Senate Bill No. 1 failed to call attention to involuntary manslaughter laws.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his involuntary manslaughter conviction, on the grounds that the requirements of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, § 6b(c) (1986), imposing a jail term as condition of probation, was unconstitutionally vague and disproportionately harsh. Appellant contended that requirements violated U.S. Const. amend. V, VIII, and XIV, as well as Tex. Const. art. 1, § 10. Appellant challenged Senate Bill No. 1 for failure to call attention to involuntary manslaughter laws. After appellant pleaded guilty and received a 10-year sentence that was probated for 10 years, the court ordered him to serve 120 days in jail as a condition of probation. Article 42.12, §6b(c) required imposition of a period of detention for offenses under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.05(2)(a). On appeal, the court held that appellant had no standing to challenge the statute's vagueness for lack of an upper limit to incarceration, because he received the minimum period of confinement. The court stressed that the legislature had broad authority in mandating confinement as a probation condition and the court found that appellant's sentence was not unduly harsh, given that there was loss of life.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a conviction for involuntary manslaughter, holding that appellant had no standing to challenge statute's vagueness for lack of an upper limit to incarceration where he received the minimum confinement, and the trial court was authorized to require a period of not more than 10 years' detention. The legislature had broad authority in mandating confinement as a probation condition.

Temple Eastex, Inc. v. Spurger Independent School Dist.

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Ninth District, Beaumont


720 S.W.2d 607; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 9291



October 2, 1986, Decided  
October 2, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEALED FROM THE 1-A DISTRICT COURT OF TYLER COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners challenged a judgment from the District Court of Tyler County (Texas), which assessed the value of appellants' land in appellee school district.


OVERVIEW: Appellants brought suit for declaratory judgment to have the trial court construe Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 23.78 for land they owned in appellee's district. The property was appraised by a municipal appraiser, who certified both the market value and the rime use value of each tract of land. Appellants argued that the trial court incorrectly held that land meant any portion of a parcel of qualified timberland. The court held that the reference in the applicable statute to that land referred to an entire parcel rather than a portion of the parcel. The court further held that the trial court erred in construing the statute to require the tax assessor to substitute the average per acre appraised value for any part of the parcel that had a lower value. Lastly, the court held that the trial court erred in holding that ad valorem taxes had not been paid in full and that appellants were required to pay the amount billed. The judgment was reversed, and the cause was remanded.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment which assessed the value of appellants' land was reversed, and the cause was remanded, because the trial court erred in construing a statute related to the appraisal of appellants' land.

 

1188 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Exxon Corp. v. Scott


No. 9472


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Sixth District, Texarkana


720 S.W.2d 819; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 8714; 102 Oil & Gas Rep. 75



September 30, 1986, Decided  
September 30, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended on Denial of Rehearing October 28, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 49th Judicial District Court of Webb County, Texas


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a part owner in a surface estate, appealed from a judgment of the 49th Judicial District Court of Webb County (Texas), denying appellant's motion for partial summary judgment and granting the motions for summary judgment of appellee state and trustee for the state's General Land Office under the Relinquishment Act, Tex. Nat. Res. Code Ann. §§ 52.171 et. seq.


OVERVIEW: Appellant owner of a percentage of interest in a surface estate sought a proportionate share of one-half of the working interest which appellee State received as consideration for settlement of another case involving oil and gas leases for the estate. The trial court denied appellant's motion for partial summary disposition and granted appellee's motion on all issues. The court reversed, finding that the consideration for the settlement was interest in the oil and gas lease for the estate. Tex. Nat. Res. Code Ann. § 52.177 did not bar appellant, as a Relinquishment Act, Tex. Nat. Res. Code Ann. §§ 52.171 et seq., surface owner, from sharing in the proceeds of the settlement and appellant and appellant were to share equally in all bonuses, royalties, rentals, or other consideration paid by the lessee. The court concluded that appellant was entitle to a proportionate share of the settlement of the lawsuit had the other party paid cash to appellee and thus appellant was entitled to a proportionate share of the proceeds of the settlement. The court found that the trial court erred in denying appellant's motion as appellant was entitled to judgment as a matter of law.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed. Appellee state and trustee for the state's General Land Office were improperly granted summary judgment in a suit involving an oil and gas lease, because appellant owner of a percentage of interest in a surface estate was entitled to its share in the proceeds of the settlement received by appellees as provided by statute, regardless of whether the proceeds were in cash or interest in an oil and gas lease.

 

1189 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Smith


No. 01-85-0989-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


720 S.W.2d 586; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 8618



September 25, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 30, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 295th District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 85-04736.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant grandfather and other relatives sought review of a judgment of the 295th District Court of Harris County (Texas), awarding actual and exemplary damages to appellees, mother and her minor children, for interference with child custody, in violation of Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 36.02.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, mother and her minor children, brought suit against appellants, grandfather and other relatives, seeking damages for interference with child custody. Appellants sought review and the court rejected every contention. Appellants failed to show that any improper arguments prejudiced appellants. It was not error to permit the use of a deposition at trial, even thought it contained appellants' assertion of their U.S. Const. amend. V rights. The several matters contained in Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 36 related to the same general subject and did not violate Tex. Const. art. III, § 35. Tex. Fam. Code § 36.02 was not unconstitutionally vague because it was not impermissibly vague in all of its applications. A ppellants engaged in conduct which it clearly proscribed. Classifications within Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 36 were rationally related to a legitimate state interest. It was not error to permit an unsigned deposition to be used at trial because there were no facts that impugned the deposition's reliability. The trial court had continuing authority to impose sanctions against appellant grandfather for post-judgment discovery abuse. The court affirmed the trial court's decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that awarded actual and exemplary damages to appellees, mother and her minor children. The court upheld the constitutionality of certain family law statutes, and held that the trial court properly allowed the use of certain depositions at trial.

 

1190 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Patton v. State


No. 2-85-290-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


717 S.W.2d 772; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 8785



September 25, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT NO. 4 OF TARRANT COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant offender sought review of the judgment of the Criminal District Court No. 4 of Tarrant County (Texas), which convicted appellant of aggravated sexual assault of a child.


OVERVIEW: Appellant offender was convicted of aggravated sexual assault of a child and the court affirmed. It was not error to allow appellee state to introduce evidence of appellant's sexual offenses committed with the victim because appellant's trial testimony created a false impression concerning the incident and the state was permitted to present information of extraneous offenses to correct the impression. Moreover, the evidence was relevant to appellant's probation application. Appellee's summation did not ask the jury to speculate about prior sex offenses in determining punishment, and after the court sustained appellant's objection he did not renew a request to instruct the jury to disregard the statement and thus did not preserve the error for review. Appellant's counsel's failure to request court reporting of voir dire proceedings did not harm appellant, counsel's decision not to cross-examine victims was strategic, and thus appellant was not denied effective assistance of counsel. Finally, the mandate in Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(a) (Vernon Supp. 1986), to instruct the jury on parole law did not attempt to grant executive power to the jury and was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting appellant offender of aggravated sexual assault. Evidence of appellant's offenses with the victim was admissible to correct a false impression that appellant gave the jury and was relevant to appellant's probation application. Appellee state's jury summation did not ask the jury to speculate about prior sex offenses in determining punishment and appellant received effective assistance of counsel.

 

1191 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Romines v. State


No. 2-84-341-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


717 S.W.2d 745; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 8803



September 24, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 211TH DISTRICT COURT OF DENTON COUNTY


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant offender challenged the judgment of the 211th District Court of Denton County (Texas), which convicted him of aggravated assault of a minor, claiming that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.071, § 2 (Vernon Supp. 1986) deprived him of his right to confront and cross-examine witnesses against him.


OVERVIEW: Appellant offender challenged his conviction of aggravated sexual assault of a minor. The court reversed and remanded for a new trial. Appellant's admission to committing the offense on a different date than alleged in the indictment did not mean that two separate offenses were shown and went only to the credibility of appellant's statement. It was proper to admit a victim's videotaped testimony recorded prior to trial because the trial court reviewed the testimony and determined that the victim was competent and the questions were permissible. But admission of the videotape pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.071, § 2 (Vernon Supp. 1986) deprived appellant of his right to confront and cross-examine the victim. The statute did not insure fundamental fairness by allowing appellee state to record the victim's testimony in a relaxed atmosphere, but required appellant to subject the victim to the pressure of the courtroom or waive his right to confrontation. Had appellant cross-examined the victim, the jury would have been twice presented with the testimony. Moreover, prior statements should not have been used until the witness had forgotten or given inconsistent testimony.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant offender's conviction of aggravated sexual assault and remanded for a new trial. Statutory law allowing admission in evidence of a child's testimony videotaped prior to trial deprived appellant of his right to confront and cross-examine witnesses because a prior statement was not justified, and appellant would have had to subject the victim to courtroom testimony and present the jury with the testimony a second time.

 

1192 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Sexton v. Mt. Olivet Cemetery Asso.


No. 14,579


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


720 S.W.2d 129; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 9259



September 24, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 12, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 147TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, NO. 367,720, HONORABLE JOE DIBRELL, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state banking commissioner challenged the judgment of the District Court of Travis County (Texas), which, based on Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 548b (1973 & Supp. 1986), granted appellee cemetery association declaratory and injunctive relief in its action to prevent appellant from reopening prior administrative proceedings and reconsidering its approval of appellee's funeral services plan.


OVERVIEW: The state banking department rejected appellee cemetery association's application to withdraw accrued interest from its bank accounts consistent with a prepaid funeral services plan that the department had approved in administrative proceedings held in 1981, and the department attempted to reopen the proceedings. Appellee filed suit against appellant state banking commissioner. The trial court granted appellee declaratory and injunctive relief, and appellee sought review. The court directed reform of the judgment and affirmed. It found that new evidence regarding appellee's plan, and new considerations regarding administrative policy, did not entitle the department to reopen prior proceedings and reconsider its approval of the plan. Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 548b (1973 & Supp. 1986) neither expressly nor impliedly empowered the department to reopen proceedings for such a purpose. The legislature anticipated that sellers would assume financial obligations in reliance on unconditional department approval. The court directed that the portion of the judgment allowing appellant to reconsider plan approval upon a specific factual showing be reformed accordingly.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed judgment in favor of appellee cemetery association for declaratory and injunctive relief against appellant state banking commissioner. Statutory law did not expressly or impliedly empower the state banking department to reopen proceedings and reconsider approval of appellee's funeral services plan. The court directed judgment reform to the extent that it allowed plan approval reconsideration upon a specific factual showing.

ROBLES v. FIREMEN'S & POLICEMEN'S CIV. SERV. COMMN. OF HOUSTON


No. 01-86-00258-CV.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 8560



September 18, 1986, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 133rd District Court of Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 84-28500.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant fire department chauffeur sought review of the judgment of the 133rd District Court of Harris County, Texas, which affirmed an order of appellee civil service commission that upheld appellant's indefinite suspension under appellee's rules and Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1269m, § 5, for committing a criminal act by issuing a check on a closed account.


OVERVIEW: Appellant fire department chauffeur was suspended by the chief and appellee civil service commission after he wrote a check on a closed account in violation of Tex. Penal Code § 32.41 (Supp. 1986). The trial court upheld the suspension because it was supported by substantial evidence. Appellant claimed that "substantial evidence" was the wrong standard of review because the rule under which he was suspended was an unconstitutional exercise of authority by appellee. The court held that appellant waived this point of error because he did not make the argument in the trial court, stipulated that the substantial evidence rule applied, and failed to brief the point properly under Tex. R. Civ. P. Ann. § 414(e) (1985). Assuming appellant preserved his claim, the court found no unconstitutional exercise of authority. The rule under which appellant was suspended was consistent with Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1269m, § 5, which did not require a conviction and provided for suspension if a firefighter committed acts that showed a lack of good moral character or was guilty of a criminal or immoral act. The court affirmed the suspension because it was supported by substantial evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the indefinite suspension of appellant fire department chauffeur. The suspension order was supported by substantial evidence. Appellant waived his claim that appellee civil service commission's rule was unconstitutional because he did not raise the issue at trial and failed to brief the point properly. The rule was constitutional because it was consistent with the statute.

Bolling v. Texas Animal Health Com.


No. 13-86-013-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


718 S.W.2d 819; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 8724



September 18, 1986, Decided  
September 18, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 30, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 267th District Court of Jackson County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant cattle owner challenged the summary judgment entered by the 267th District Court of Jackson County, Texas, in favor of appellee, Texas Animal Health Commission, in appellee's suit, brought under Tex. Agric. Code Ann. § 161.131 (1982), to tag and slaughter appellant's cattle which had been exposed to Brucellosis.


OVERVIEW: Appellee, Texas Animal Health Commission, sought an injunction to tag and brand the cattle belonging to appellant cattle owner that had been exposed to Brucellosis. The trial court granted appellee's motion for summary judgment. The court ordered appellant to have his reactor cattle tagged, branded, and moved for immediate slaughter to a slaughtering establishment. Appellant challenged the trial court order, complaining that the trial court reversibly erred by granting appellee's summary judgment which precluded appellant from litigating genuine issues as to material facts relating to defenses and counterclaims that the Brucellosis control program was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, holding that the trial court had not reversibly erred by granting summary judgment to appellee. Appellee had the authority to bring its action pursuant to Tex. Agric. Code Ann. § 161.131 (1982). Despite the fact that Brucellosis control deprived appellant of his most beneficial use of the cattle, it was not, as such, an unconstitutional "taking." Rather, the program was a valid exercise of the state's police power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, holding that the trial court had not reversibly erred by granting summary judgment to appellee, Texas Animal Health Commission, authorizing it to tag and brand Brucellosis exposed cattle belonging to appellant cattle owner because appellee acted under appropriate police authority and its actions did not constitute an . unconstitutional "taking" of appellant's property.

McCraw v. Vickers


No. 04-86-00254-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


717 S.W.2d 738; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 8828



September 18, 1986, Decided  
September 18, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 166th District Court of Bexar County, Trial Court No. 86-CI-00586, Honorable Joe E. Kelly, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff justices appealed a judgment by the 166th District Court of Bexar County, Texas, which upheld the order of defendant Commissioner's Court of Bexar County. The order abolished three Justice of the Peace positions.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff justices appealed the affirmation of the order of defendant commissioner's court. Plaintiffs claimed the order abolishing three justice of the peace positions violated Tex. Const. art. 16, § 65, and equal protection, U.S. Const. amend. XIV. These issues were not preserved for appeal because they were not before the trial court. The court further held that the order did not violate Tex. Const. art. 5, § 18, because as a matter of law, the trial court's judgment was in accordance with the plain meaning of the statute. There was nothing in the record which indicated that the trial court failed to follow the rules of constitutional or statutory interpretation. Plaintiffs received as much due process and protection as they were due. They clearly had notice of defendant's pre-order hearing and an opportunity to be heard. The U.S. Justice Department concurred with both the redistricting of the five justice of the peace precincts and the elimination of the three justice of the peace positions. There was no evidence that defendant acted arbitrarily, without reason, or in bad faith when it passed the order. The action by defendant did not constitute an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: Because there was no evidence that defendant commissioners' court acted arbitrarily when it passed the Justice Abolition Order, the action did not constitute an abuse of discretion. Plaintiff justices were not denied due process of law. Therefore, the judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Price v. Price


No. 04-85-00579-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


718 S.W.2d 65; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 8848



September 17, 1986, Decided  
September 17, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 14, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 73rd District Court of Bexar County, Trial Court No. 85-CI-07030A, Honorable Carol R. Haberman, Judge Presiding, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant wife challenged a summary judgment of the 73rd District Court of Bexar County (Texas), which denied her recovery from appellee husband for personal injuries suffered by appellant prior to her marriage to appellee as a result of appellee's negligence.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted summary judgment to appellee husband, denying appellant wife recovery for personal injuries suffered by her prior to her marriage to appellee as a result of appellee's negligence. On appeal, the court reluctantly affirmed the decision. Generally, the doctrine of interspousal immunity barred recovery for personal injuries suffered by one spouse as the result of the negligence of the other spouse. While the state supreme court held the doctrine inapplicable in cases of intentional tort, it was clear that it adopted the theory that the immunity doctrine was based on a public policy aimed at the preservation of marital peace and harmony. Although neither courts nor commentators had satisfactorily explained how denying relief to the injured spouse would promote harmony, the court was constrained to follow the unambiguous, if indefensible, precedent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision denying recovery from defendant husband in a suit for personal injuries brought by plaintiff wife. It found that the theory of interspousal immunity doctrine barred recovery for personal injuries suffered by one spouse as the result of the negligence of the other spouse.

KNAPP v. STATE


No. 01-85-0907-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 8481



September 11, 1986, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 262nd District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 423110.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the 262nd District Court of Harris County, Texas, which convicted him of murder after a jury found him guilty. Punishment, enhanced by one prior felony conviction, was assessed at 50 years' confinement. Appellant asserted seven grounds of error.


OVERVIEW: Appellant's murder conviction was affirmed on appeal, with the court rejecting each of his asserted errors. His challenge to the instruction on parole failed because the charge was specifically required by statute and the instruction given tracked the statutory language. There was no merit to the argument that two prospective jurors should have been excused sua sponte on grounds of bias or prejudice to appellant; none of the limited circumstances allowed by statute for such an action was shown. The argument that the trial court should have quashed the indictment was moot because the state dropped the burglary charge. The court held that a mistrial was not shown to be warranted for any reason on the basis of the testimony of two witnesses challenged by appellant. The court disagreed that a hearing was warranted on appellant's competence to stand trial; the record revealed no evidentiary basis or complaint of defense counsel to suggest the necessity of such a hearing. Appellant had waived his final complaint that the jury should have been specially instructed regarding the credibility of a particular witness, because he made no request or objection at trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. The court noted that appellant did not challenge the sufficiency of the evidence in support of the murder conviction. The court rejected each of the procedural errors asserted by appellant as grounds for reversal of his conviction, holding that some were moot, some had not been preserved for appeal, and others simply lacked merit.

Murmur Corp. v. Board of Adjustment


No. 05-85-00528-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


718 S.W.2d 790; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 8944



September 11, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 27, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review from a district court of Dallas County, Texas, which approved an order of appellee Board of Adjustment of the City of Dallas terminating appellant's nonconforming use of land as a lead smelter and issued a permanent injunction against appellant restraining the operation of the smelter.


OVERVIEW: Appellee Board of Adjustment of the City of Dallas issued an order immediately terminating appellant corporation's nonconforming use of certain land as a lead smelter. Appellant sought review seeking a declaratory judgment establishing its right to operate the smelter and damages for interference with its operation. The trial court denied all relief sought by appellant and issued a permanent injunction restraining operation of the smelter. The court held that the ordinance was valid and applicable to the operation of the smelter. The court determined that, pursuant to Dallas, Tex., Development Code §§ 51-3.102 and 51-4.704 (1983), appellant was entitled to continue the use during the period required for recoupment of its investment in the nonconforming use. The court held that appellee's order of immediate termination was an abuse of discretion because there was no substantial evidence supporting an implied finding that appellant had no investment in the nonconforming structure. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed judgment of the trial court, which issued a permanent injunction restraining appellant corporation's operation of certain land as a lead smelter. The court held that appellant was entitled to continue use during period required for recoupment of its investment in nonconforming use. Appellee Board of Adjustment of the City of Dallas abused its discretion in holding that appellant had no investment in the nonconforming structure.

 

1200 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Fielding v. State


Nos. 05-85-01019-CR, 05-85-01020-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


719 S.W.2d 361; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 9073



September 10, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 10, 1986.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted for the possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver. The trial court deferred adjudication pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, § 3d (1986). After appellant committed a subsequent offense, on the state's motion, the trial court proceeded with adjudication of guilt. Appellant sought review of the decision of the Texas trial court, which assessed punishment at 60 years per offense.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted for possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver. Pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, § 3d (1986), appellant was placed on deferred adjudication. When appellant drove with a suspended license, the state brought a motion to proceed with adjudication, and appellant was assessed punishment. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment to proceed to adjudication because, under art. 42.12, § 3d, that decision was within the sole discretion of the trial court and was not subject to appellate review. The court determined that appellant's motion for a new trial was properly denied because appellant failed to present new extrinsic evidence. Additionally, the court rejected appellant's claim that he had substantially complied with "probation" terms because that standard applied to "probation" that occurred after guilt was adjudicated, and not before, as in appellant's deferred adjudication. The court held that appellant's due process rights were not violated, even if the trial court failed to consider mitigating evidence, because any error would be harmless and appellant failed to rebut the presumption of proper trial court action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision that proceeded with adjudication and assessed punishment for the possession of a controlled substance at 60 years per offense. The court held that the decision to proceed with adjudication was not subject to review, appellant's motion for a new trial was properly denied by his failure to produce new evidence, and that any error in the trial court's treatment of mitigating evidence was harmless.
